31: --------
32: Translator's note
33: Few foreign masterpieces can have suffered more than Eugene Onegin from
34: the English  translator's failure to convey anything more than -- at best --
35: the literal meaning.  It is  as if  a  sound-proof wall separated  Pushkin's
36: poetic novel from the English-reading world.  There  is  a whole magic which
37: goes by default: the  touching lyrical  beauty, the cynical wit of the poem;
38: the  psychological  insight,  the  devious  narrative  skill, the thrilling,
39: compulsive  grip of the novel; the tremendous gusto and swing and panache of
40: the whole performance.
41: Vladimir Nabokov's rendering into unrhymed iambics reproduces the exact
42: meaning, but explicitly disclaims any further ambition. While Nabokov admits
43: that  in  losing  its  rhyme   the  work  loses  its  ``bloom''  he  argues,
44: irrefutably,  that  no rhyming  version  can  be literally  accurate. It can
45: however certainly strive  for something else. It can attempt to produce some
46: substitute for  the ``bloom'' of  the original, without  which the  work  is
47: completely  dead.  It  can try to convey the poet's tone  of voice,  whether
48: world-weary  or romantic, the sparkle  of  his jokes,  the  flavour  of  his
49: epigrams, the snap of his  final couplets. None of these effects can  emerge
50: from  a  purely  literal  unrhymed  translation.  In  fact,  to  offset  the
51: inevitable  loss in verbal  exactness,  a  rhyming  version  can  aim  at  a
52: different sort of accuracy, an equivalence or parallelism conveying, however
53: faintly, the impact of the original.
54: Apart from the overall  difficulty of  his  task, the  translator  with
55: ambitions of this  type will find  that Pushkin's work presents him with two
56: particular problems.
57: The brio of the Russian text partly depends on a lavish use not only of
58: French and other foreign words, but of  slang and of  audacious Byronic-type
59: rhymes.  If  the  translator produces nothing comparable, he is emasculating
60: his original. If he attempts to follow suit, he must  do all he can to avoid
61: the pitfalls of the embarrassing, the facetious and the arch. {29}
62: Secondly, he must be on his guard against the ludicrous effect that the
63: feminine  ending (for instance the pleasure/measure rhyme, which is so  much
64: derided by Nabokov) can all too easily produce in English. He must not sing,
65: like Prince Gremin in one English version of Chaykovsky's opera:
66: ``I wouldn't be remotely human
67: Did I not love the Little Woman.''
68: (The libretto of the opera, which was  written and first performed more
69: than  forty  years  after  Pushkin's  death,  is by  Chaykovsky  himself and
70: Konstantin Shilovsky, a minor  poet of the time.  It  is  nominally based on
71: Pushkin's text, but in fact the relationship is not very close.)
72: Anyway, it should  be possible now, with  the help of Nabokov's literal
73: translation and commentary, to produce a reasonably accurate rhyming version
74: of  Pushkin's  work  which   can  at  least  be   read  with   pleasure  and
75: entertainment, and which,  ideally,  might even be able to stand on  its own
76: feet as English. That, in all humility, is the aim of the present text.
77: Acknowledgements are  due  to  Messrs. Routledge  and  Kegan  Paul  for
78: permission to quote from Vladimir Nabokov's notes in volumes 2 and 3 of  his
79: edition of Eugene Onegin (London, 1964. Revised edition, 1976).
80: I  am much  indebted  to  my  friends Sir Sacheverell Sitwell, for  his
81: interest  and  support,  and  Sir  John  Balfour,  for  his   searching  and
82: constructive criticism of the  translation;  to  Professor  Gleb Struve, for
83: generously  giving me the benefit of his unrivalled scholarship and insight;
84: above all, to my wife Natasha, for her loving encouragement.
85: C. H. J.
86: {30}
87: --------
88: x x x
89: Pétri de  vanité,  il  avait encore plus de cette espèce  d'orgueil qui
90: fait  avouer avec  la  même  indifférence  les  bonnes  comme  les mauvaises
91: actions, suite d'un sentiment de supériorité peut-être imaginaire.
92: (Tiré d'une lettre particulière)
93: {31} {32}
94: --------
95: x x x
96: To Peter Alexandrovich Pletnev
97: Heedless of the proud world's enjoyment,
98: I prize the attention of my friends,
99: and only wish that my employment
100: could have been turned to worthier ends --
101: worthier of you in the perfection
102: your soul displays, in holy dreams,
103: in simple but sublime reflection,
104: in limpid verse that lives and gleams.
105: But, as it is, this pied collection
106: begs your indulgence -- it's been spun
107: from threads both sad and humoristic,
108: themes popular or idealistic,
109: products of carefree hours, of fun,
110: of sleeplessness, faint inspirations,
111: of powers unripe, or on the wane,
112: of reason's icy intimations,
113: and records of a heart in pain.
114: {33} {34}
115: --------
116: Chapter One
117: To live, it hurries, and to feel it hastes.
118: Prince Vyazemsky
119: I
120: ``My uncle -- high ideals inspire him;
121: but when past joking he fell sick,
122: he really forced one to admire him --
123: and never played a shrewder trick.
124: Let others learn from his example!
125: But God, how deadly dull to sample
126: sickroom attendance night and day
127: and never stir a foot away!
128: And the sly baseness, fit to throttle,
129: of entertaining the half-dead:
130: one smoothes the pillows down in bed,
131: and glumly serves the medicine bottle,
132: and sighs, and asks oneself all through:
133: "When will the devil come for you?"''
134: {35}
135: II
136: Such were a young rake's meditations --
137: by will of Zeus, the high and just,
138: the legatee of his relations --
139: as horses whirled him through the dust.
140: Friends of my Ruslan and Lyudmila,
141: without preliminary feeler
142: let me acquaint you on the nail
143: with this the hero of my tale:
144: Onegin, my good friend, was littered
145: and bred upon the Neva's brink,
146: where you were born as well, I think,
147: reader, or where you've shone and glittered!
148: There once I too strolled back and forth:
149: but I'm allergic to the North...1
150: III
151: After a fine career, his father
152: had only debts on which to live.
153: He gave three balls a year, and rather
154: promptly had nothing left to give.
155: Fate saved Evgeny from perdition:
156: at first Madame gave him tuition,
157: from her Monsieur took on the child.
158: He was sweet-natured, and yet wild.
159: Monsieur l'Abbé, the mediocre,
160: reluctant to exhaust the boy,
161: treated his lessons as a ploy.
162: No moralizing from this joker;
163: a mild rebuke was his worst mark,
164: and then a stroll in Letny Park.
165: {36}
166: IV
167: But when the hour of youthful passion
168: struck for Evgeny, with its play
169: of hope and gloom, romantic-fashion,
170: it was goodbye, Monsieur l'Abbé.
171: Eugene was free, and as a dresser
172: made London's dandy his professor.
173: His hair was fashionably curled,
174: and now at last he saw the World.
175: In French Onegin had perfected
176: proficiency to speak and write,
177: in the mazurka he was light,
178: his bow was wholly unaffected.
179: The World found this enough to treat
180: Eugene as clever, and quite sweet.
181: V
182: We all meandered through our schooling
183: haphazard; so, to God be thanks,
184: it's easy, without too much fooling,
185: to pass for cultured in our ranks.
186: Onegin was assessed by many
187: (critical judges, strict as any)
188: as well-read, though of pedant cast.
189: Unforced, as conversation passed,
190: he had the talent of saluting
191: felicitously every theme,
192: of listening like a judge-supreme
193: while serious topics were disputing,
194: or, with an epigram-surprise,
195: of kindling smiles in ladies' eyes.
196: {37}
197: VI
198: Now Latin's gone quite out of favour;
199: yet, truthfully and not in chaff,
200: Onegin knew enough to savour
201: the meaning of an epigraph,
202: make Juvenal his text, or better
203: add vale when he signed a letter;
204: stumblingly call to mind he did
205: two verses of the Aeneid.
206: He lacked the slightest predilection
207: for raking up historic dust
208: or stirring annalistic must;
209: but groomed an anecdote-collection
210: that stretched from Romulus in his prime
211: across the years to our own time.
212: VII
213: He was without that dithyrambic
214: frenzy which wrecks our lives for sound,
215: and telling trochee from iambic
216: was quite beyond his wit, we found.
217: He cursed Theocritus and Homer,
218: in Adam Smith was his diploma;
219: our deep economist had got
220: the gift of recognizing what
221: a nation's wealth is, what augments it,
222: and how a country lives, and why
223: it needs no gold if a supply
224: of simple product supplements it.
225: His father failed to understand
226: and took a mortgage on his land.
227: {38}
228: VIII
229: Evgeny's total store of knowledge
230: I have no leisure to recall;
231: where he was master of his college,
232: the art he'd studied best of all,
233: his young heyday's supreme employment,
234: its work, its torture, its enjoyment,
235: what occupied his chafing powers
236: throughout the boredom of the hours --
237: this was the science of that passion
238: which Ovid sang, for which the bard,
239: condemned to a lifetime of hard,
240: ended his wild career of fashion
241: deep in Moldavia the abhorred,
242: far, far from Italy, his adored.
243: (IX,2) X
244: How early he'd learnt to dissemble,
245: to hide a hope, to make a show
246: of jealousy, to seem to tremble
247: or pine, persuade of yes or no,
248: and act the humble or imperious,
249: the indifferent, or the deadly serious!
250: In languid silence, or the flame
251: of eloquence, and just the same
252: in casual letters of confession --
253: one thing inspired his breath, his heart,
254: and self-oblivion was his art!
255: How soft his glance, or at discretion
256: how bold or bashful there, and here
257: how brilliant with its instant tear!
258: {39}
259: XI
260: How well he donned new shapes and sizes --
261: startling the ingenuous with a jest,
262: frightening with all despair's disguises,
263: amusing, flattering with the best,
264: stalking the momentary weakness,
265: with passion and with shrewd obliqueness
266: swaying the artless, waiting on
267: for unmeant kindness -- how he shone!
268: then he'd implore a declaration,
269: and listen for the heart's first sound,
270: pursue his love -- and at one bound
271: secure a secret assignation,
272: then afterwards, alone, at ease,
273: impart such lessons as you please!
274: XII
275: How early on he learnt to trouble
276: the heart of the professional flirt!
277: When out to burst a rival's bubble,
278: how well he knew the way to hurt --
279: what traps he'd set him, with what malice
280: he'd pop the poison in his chalice!
281: But you, blest husbands, to the end
282: you kept your friendship with our friend:
283: the subtle spouse was just as loyal --
284: Faublas'3 disciple for an age --
285: as was the old suspicious sage,
286: and the majestic, antlered royal,
287: always contented with his life,
288: and with his dinner, and his wife.
289: {40}
290: (XIII, XIV,) XV
291: Some days he's still in bed, and drowses,
292: when little notes come on a tray.
293: What? Invitations? Yes, three houses
294: have each asked him to a soirée:
295: a ball here, there a children's party;
296: where shall he go, my rogue, my hearty?
297: Which one comes first? It's just the same
298: to do them all is easy game.
299: Meanwhile, attired for morning strolling
300: complete with broad-brimmed bolivar,
301: Eugene attends the boulevard,
302: and there at large he goes patrolling
303: until Bréguet's unsleeping chime
304: advises him of dinner-time.
305: XVI
306: He mounts the sledge, with daylight fading:
307: ``Make way, make way,'' goes up the shout;
308: his collar in its beaver braiding
309: glitters with hoar-frost all about.
310: He's flown to Talon's,4 calculating
311: that there his friend Kavérin's5 waiting;
312: he arrives -- the cork goes flying up,
313: wine of the Comet6 fills the cup;
314: before him roast beef, red and gory,
315: and truffles, which have ever been
316: youth's choice, the flower of French cuisine:
317: and pâté, Strasbourg's deathless glory,
318: sits with Limburg's vivacious cheese
319: and ananas, the gold of trees.
320: {41}
321: XVII
322: More wine, he calls, to drench the flaming
323: fire of the cutlets' scalding fat,
324: when Bréguet's chime is heard proclaiming
325: the new ballet he should be at.
326: He's off -- this ruthless legislator
327: for the footlights, this fickle traitor
328: to all the most adored actrices,
329: this denizen of the coulisses
330: that world where every man's a critic
331: who'll clap an entrechat, or scoff
332: at Cleopatra, hiss her off,
333: boo Phaedra out as paralytic,
334: encore Moëna,7 -- and rejoice
335: to know the audience hears his voice.
336: XVIII
337: Enchanted land! There like a lampion
338: that king of the satiric scene,
339: Fonvizin8 sparkled, freedom's champion,
340: and the derivative Knyazhnín:8
341: there сzerov8 shared the unwilling
342: tribute of tears, applause's shrilling,
343: with young Semyónova,9 and there
344: our friend Katénin8 brought to bear
345: once more Corneille's majestic story;
346: there caustic Shakhovskóy8 came in
347: with comedies of swarm and din;
348: there Didelot10 crowned himself with glory:
349: there, where the coulisse entrance went,
350: that's where my years of youth were spent.
351: {42}
352: XIX
353: My goddesses! Where are you banished?
354: lend ears to my lugubrious tone:
355: have other maidens, since you vanished,
356: taken your place, though not your throne?
357: your chorus, is it dead for ever?
358: Russia's Terpsichore, shall never
359: again I see your soulful flight?
360: shall my sad gaze no more alight
361: on features known, but to that dreary,
362: that alien scene must I now turn
363: my disillusioned glass, and yearn,
364: bored with hilarity, and weary,
365: and yawn in silence at the stage
366: as I recall a bygone age?
367: XX
368: The house is packed out; scintillating,
369: the boxes; boiling, pit and stalls;
370: the gallery claps -- it's bored with waiting --
371: and up the rustling curtain crawls.
372: Then with a half-ethereal splendour,
373: bound where the magic bow will send her,
374: Istómina,11 thronged all around
375: by Naiads, one foot on the ground,
376: twirls the other slowly as she pleases,
377: then suddenly she's off, and there
378: she's up and flying through the air
379: like fluff before Aeolian breezes;
380: she'll spin this way and that, and beat
381: against each other swift, small feet.
382: {43}
383: XXI
384: Applause. Onegin enters -- passes
385: across the public's toes; he steers
386: straight to his stall, then turns his glasses
387: on unknown ladies in the tiers;
388: he's viewed the boxes without passion,
389: he's seen it all; with looks and fashion
390: he's dreadfully dissatisfied;
391: to gentlemen on every side
392: he's bowed politely; his attention
393: wanders in a distracted way
394: across the stage; he yawns: ``Ballet --
395: they all have richly earned a pension;''
396: he turns away: ``I've had enough --
397: now even Didelot's tedious stuff.''
398: XXII
399: Still tumbling, devil, snake and Cupid
400: on stage are thumping without cease;
401: Still in the porch, exhausted-stupid,
402: the footmen sleep on the pelisses;
403: the audience still is busy stamping,
404: still coughing, hissing, clapping, champing;
405: still everywhere the lamps are bright;
406: outside and in they star the night;
407: still shivering in the bitter weather
408: the horses fidget worse and worse;
409: the coachmen ring the fire, and curse
410: their lords, and thwack their palms together;
411: but Eugene's out from din and press:
412: by now he's driving home to dress.
413: {44}
414: XXIII
415: Shall I depict with expert knowledge
416: the cabinet behind the door
417: where the prize-boy of fashion's college
418: is dressed, undressed, and dressed once more?
419: Whatever for caprice of spending
420: ingenious London has been sending
421: across the Baltic in exchange
422: for wood and tallow; all the range
423: of useful objects that the curious
424: Parisian taste invents for one --
425: for friends of languor, or of fun,
426: or for the modishly luxurious --
427: all this, at eighteen years of age,
428: adorned the sanctum of our sage.
429: XXIV
430: Porcelain and bronzes on the table,
431: with amber pipes from Tsaregrad;12
432: such crystalled scents as best are able
433: to drive the swooning senses mad;
434: with combs, and steel utensils serving
435: as files, and scissors straight and curving,
436: brushes on thirty different scales;
437: brushes for teeth, brushes for nails.
438: Rousseau (forgive a short distraction)
439: could not conceive how solemn Grimm13
440: dared clean his nails in front of him,
441: the brilliant crackpot: this reaction
442: shows freedom's advocate, that strong
443: champion of rights, as in the wrong.
444: {45}
445: XXV
446: A man who's active and incisive
447: can yet keep nail-care much in mind:
448: why fight what's known to be decisive?
449: custom is despot of mankind.
450: Dressed like -- --,14 duly dreading
451: the barbs that envy's always spreading,
452: Eugene's a pedant in his dress,
453: in fact a thorough fop, no less.
454: Three whole hours, at the least accounting,
455: he'll spend before the looking-glass,
456: then from his cabinet he'll pass
457: giddy as Venus when she's mounting
458: a masculine disguise to aid
459: her progress at the masquerade.
460: XXVI
461: Your curiosity is burning
462: to hear what latest modes require,
463: and so, before the world of learning,
464: I could describe here his attire;
465: and though to do so would be daring,
466: it's my profession; he was wearing --
467: but pantaloons, waistcoat, and frock,
468: these words are not of Russian stock:
469: I know (and seek your exculpation)
470: that even so my wretched style
471: already tends too much to smile
472: on words of foreign derivation,
473: though years ago I used to look
474: at the Academic Diction-book.
475: {46}
476: XXVII
477: That isn't our immediate worry:
478: we'd better hasten to the ball,
479: where, in a cab, and furious hurry,
480: Onegin has outrun us all.
481: Along the fronts of darkened houses,
482: along the street where slumber drowses,
483: twin lamps of serried coupés throw
484: a cheerful glimmer on the snow
485: and radiate a rainbow: blazing
486: with lampions studded all about
487: the sumptuous palais shines out;
488: shadows that flit behind the glazing
489: project in silhouette the tops
490: of ladies and of freakish fops.
491: XXVIII
492: Up to the porch our hero's driven:
493: in, past concierge, up marble stair
494: flown like an arrow, then he's given
495: a deft arrangement to his hair,
496: and entered. Ballroom overflowing...
497: and band already tired of blowing,
498: while a mazurka holds the crowd;
499: and everything is cramped and loud;
500: spurs of Chevalier Gardes are clinking,
501: dear ladies' feet fly past like hail,
502: and on their captivating trail
503: incendiary looks are slinking,
504: while roar of violins contrives
505: to drown the hiss of modish wives.
506: {47}
507: XXIX
508: In days of carefree aspirations,
509: the ballroom drove me off my head:
510: the safest place for declarations,
511: and where most surely notes are sped.
512: You husbands, deeply I respect you!
513: I'm at your service to protect you;
514: now pay attention, I beseech,
515: and take due warning from my speech.
516: You too, mamas, I pray attend it,
517: and watch your daughters closer yet,
518: yes, focus on them your lorgnette,
519: or else... or else, may God forfend it!
520: I only write like this, you know,
521: since I stopped sinning years ago.
522: XXX
523: Alas, on pleasure's wild variety
524: I've wasted too much life away!
525: But, did they not corrupt society,
526: I'd still like dances to this day:
527: the atmosphere of youth and madness,
528: the crush, the glitter and the gladness,
529: the ladies' calculated dress;
530: I love their feet -- though I confess
531: that all of Russia can't contribute
532: three pairs of handsome ones -- yet there
533: exists for me one special pair!
534: one pair! I pay them memory's tribute
535: though cold I am and sad; in sleep
536: the heartache that they bring lies deep.
537: {48}
538: XXXI
539: Oh, when, and to what desert banished,
540: madman, can you forget their print?
541: my little feet, where have you vanished,
542: what flowers of spring display your dint?
543: Nursed in the orient's languid weakness,
544: across our snows of northern bleakness
545: you left no steps that could be tracked:
546: you loved the opulent contact
547: of rugs, and carpets' rich refinement.
548: Was it for you that I became
549: long since unstirred by praise and fame
550: and fatherland and grim confinement?
551: The happiness of youth is dead,
552: just like, on turf, your fleeting tread.
553: XXXII
554: Diana's breast, the cheeks of Flora,
555: all these are charming! but to put
556: it frankly, I'm a firm adorer
557: of the Terpsichorean foot.
558: It fascinates by its assurance
559: of recompense beyond endurance,
560: and fastens, like a term of art,
561: the wilful fancies of the heart.
562: My love for it is just as tender,
563: under the table's linen shield,
564: on springtime grasses of the field,
565: in winter, on the cast-iron fender,
566: on ballroom's looking-glass parquet
567: or on the granite of the bay.
568: {49}
569: XXXIII
570: On the seashore, with storm impending,
571: how envious was I of the waves
572: each in tumultuous turn descending
573: to lie down at her feet like slaves!
574: I longed, like every breaker hissing,
575: to smother her dear feet with kissing.
576: No, never in the hottest fire
577: of boiling youth did I desire
578: with any torture so exquisite
579: to kiss Armida's lips, or seek
580: the flaming roses of a cheek,
581: or languid bosoms; and no visit
582: of raging passion's surge and roll
583: ever so roughly rocked my soul!
584: XXXIV
585: Another page of recollection:
586: sometimes, in reverie's sacred land,
587: I grasp a stirrup with affection,
588: I feel a small foot in my hand;
589: fancies once more are hotly bubbling,
590: once more that touch is fiercely troubling
591: the blood within my withered heart,
592: once more the love, once more the smart...
593: But, now I've praised the queens of fashion,
594: enough of my loquacious lyre:
595: they don't deserve what they inspire
596: in terms of poetry or passion --
597: their looks and language in deceit
598: are just as nimble as their feet.
599: {50}
600: XXXV
601: And Eugene? half-awake, half-drowsing,
602: from ball to bed behold him come;
603: while Petersburg's already rousing,
604: untirable, at sound of drum:
605: the merchant's up, the cabman's walking
606: towards his stall, the pedlar's hawking;
607: see with their jugs the milk-girls go
608: and crisply crunch the morning snow.
609: The city's early sounds awake her;
610: shutters are opened and the soft
611: blue smoke of chimneys goes aloft,
612: and more than once the German baker,
613: punctilious in his cotton cap,
614: has opened up his serving-trap.
615: XXXVI
616: Exhausted by the ballroom's clamour,
617: converting morning to midnight,
618: he sleeps, away from glare and glamour,
619: this child of luxury and delight.
620: Then, after midday he'll be waking;
621: his life till dawn's already making,
622: always monotonously gay,
623: tomorrow just like yesterday.
624: But was it happy, his employment,
625: his freedom, in his youth's first flower,
626: with brilliant conquests by the shower,
627: and every day its own enjoyment?
628: Was it to no effect that he,
629: at feasts, was strong and fancy-free?
630: {51}
631: XXXVII
632: No, early on his heart was cooling
633: and he was bored with social noise;
634: no, not for long were belles the ruling
635: objective of his thoughts and joys:
636: soon, infidelity proved cloying,
637: and friends and friendship, soul-destroying;
638: not every day could he wash down
639: his beefsteak with champagne, or drown
640: his Strasbourg pie, or point a moral,
641: full of his usual pith and wit,
642: with cranium aching fit to split;
643: and though he liked a fiery quarrel --
644: yet he fell out of love at last
645: with sabre's slash, and bullet's blast.
646: XXXVIII
647: The illness with which he'd been smitten
648: should have been analysed when caught,
649: something like spleen, that scourge of Britain,
650: or Russia's chondria, for short;
651: it mastered him in slow gradation;
652: thank God, he had no inclination
653: to blow his brains out, but in stead
654: to life grew colder than the dead.
655: So, like Childe Harold, glum, unpleasing,
656: he stalked the drawing-rooms, remote
657: from Boston's cloth or gossip's quote;
658: no glance so sweet, no sigh so teasing,
659: no, nothing caused his heart to stir,
660: and nothing pierced his senses' blur.
661: {52}
662: (XXXIX, XL, XLI,) XLII
663: Capricious belles of grand Society!
664: you were the first ones he forswore;
665: for in our time, beyond dubiety,
666: the highest circles are a bore.
667: It's true, I'll not misrepresent them,
668: some ladies preach from Say and Bentham,
669: but by and large their talk's a hash
670: of the most harmless, hopeless trash.
671: And what's more, they're so supercilious,
672: so pure, so spotless through and through,
673: so pious, and so clever too,
674: so circumspect, and so punctilious,
675: so virtuous that, no sooner seen,
676: at once they give a man the spleen.
677: XLIII
678: You too, prime beauties in your flower
679: who late at night are whirled away
680: by drozhkies jaunting at full power
681: over the Petersburg pavé --
682: he ended even your employment;
683: and in retreat from all enjoyment
684: locked himself up inside his den
685: and with a yawn took up his pen,
686: and tried to write, but a hard session
687: of work made him feel sick, and still
688: no word came flowing from his quill;
689: he failed to join that sharp profession
690: which I myself won't praise or blame
691: since I'm a member of the same.
692: {53}
693: XLIV
694: Idle again by dedication,
695: oppressed by emptiness of soul,
696: he strove to achieve the appropriation
697: of other's thought -- a splendid goal;
698: with shelves of books deployed for action,
699: he read, and read -- no satisfaction:
700: here's boredom, madness or pretence,
701: here there's no conscience, here no sense;
702: they're all chained up in different fetters,
703: the ancients have gone stiff and cold,
704: the moderns rage against the old.
705: He'd given up girls -- now gave up letters,
706: and hid the bookshelf's dusty stack
707: in taffeta of mourning black.
708: XLV
709: Escaped from social rhyme and reason,
710: retired, as he, from fashion's stream,
711: I was Onegin's friend that season.
712: I liked his quality, the dream
713: which held him silently subjected,
714: his strangeness, wholly unaffected,
715: his mind, so cold and so precise.
716: The bitterness was mine -- the ice
717: was his; we'd both drunk passion's chalice:
718: our lives were flat, and what had fired
719: both hearts to blaze had now expired;
720: there waited for us both the malice
721: of blind Fortuna and of men
722: in lives that were just dawning then.
723: {54}
724: XLVI
725: He who has lived and thought is certain
726: to scorn the men with whom he deals;
727: days that are lost behind the curtain,
728: ghostlike, must trouble him who feels --
729: for him all sham has found rejection,
730: he's gnawed by serpent Recollection,
731: and by Repentance. All this lends,
732: on most occasions between friends,
733: a great attraction to conversing.
734: At first Onegin's tongue produced
735: a haze in me, but I grew used
736: to his disputing and his cursing;
737: his virulence that made you smile,
738: his epigrams topped up with bile.
739: XLVII
740: How often, when the sky was glowing,
741: by Neva, on a summer night,
742: and when its waters were not showing,
743: in their gay glass, the borrowed light
744: of Dian's visage, in our fancies
745: recalling earlier time's romances,
746: recalling earlier loves, did we,
747: now sensitive, and now carefree,
748: drink in the midnight benediction,
749: the silence when our talk had ceased!
750: Like convicts in a dream released
751: from gaol to greenwood, by such fiction
752: we were swept off, in reverie's haze,
753: to the beginning of our days.
754: {55}
755: XLVIII
756: Evgeny stood, with soul regretful,
757: and leant upon the granite shelf;
758: he stood there, pensive and forgetful,
759: just as the Poet15 paints himself.
760: Silence was everywhere enthralling;
761: just sentries to each other calling,
762: and then a drozhky's clopping sound
763: from Million Street16 came floating round;
764: and then a boat, with oars a-swinging,
765: swam on the river's dreaming face,
766: and then, with an enchanting grace,
767: came distant horns, and gallant singing.
768: Yet sweeter far, at such a time,
769: the strain of Tasso's octave-rhyme!
770: XLIX
771: O Adrian waves, my invocation;
772: O Brenta, I'll see you in dream;
773: hear, once more filled with inspiration,
774: the magic voices of your stream,
775: sacred to children of Apollo!
776: Proud Albion's lyre is what I follow,
777: through it they're known to me, and kin.
778: Italian nights, when I'll drink in
779: your molten gold, your charmed infusion;
780: with a Venetian maiden who
781: can chatter, and be silent too,
782: I'll float in gondola's seclusion;
783: from her my lips will learn and mark
784: the tongue of love and of Petrarch.
785: {56}
786: L
787: When comes my moment to untether?
788: ``it's time!'' and freedom hears my hail.
789: I walk the shore,17 I watch the weather,
790: I signal to each passing sail.
791: Beneath storm's vestment, on the seaway,
792: battling along that watery freeway,
793: when shall I start on my escape?
794: It's time to drop astern the shape
795: of the dull shores of my disfavour,
796: and there, beneath your noonday sky,
797: my Africa,18 where waves break high,
798: to mourn for Russia's gloomy savour,
799: land where I learned to love and weep,
800: land where my heart is buried deep.
801: LI
802: Eugene would willingly have started
803: with me to see an alien strand;
804: but soon the ways we trod were parted
805: for quite a while by fortune's hand.
806: His father died; and (as expected)
807: before Onegin there collected
808: the usurers' voracious tribe.
809: To private tastes we each subscribe:
810: Evgeny, hating litigation,
811: and satisfied with what he'd got,
812: made over to them his whole lot,
813: finding in that no deprivation --
814: or else, from far off, he could see
815: old Uncle's end was soon to be.
816: {57}
817: LII
818: In fact one day a note came flying
819: from the agent, with this tale to tell:
820: Uncle, in bed, and near to dying,
821: wished him to come and say farewell.
822: Evgeny read the sad epistle
823: and set off prompter than a whistle
824: as fast as post-horses could go,
825: already yawned before the show,
826: exercised, under lucre's banner,
827: in sighs and boredom and deceits
828: (my tale's beginning here repeats);
829: but, when he'd rushed to Uncle's manor,
830: a corpse on boards was all he found,
831: an offering ready for the ground.
832: LIII
833: The yard was bursting with dependants;
834: there gathered at the coffin-side
835: friends, foes, priests, guests, inured attendants
836: of every funeral far and wide;
837: they buried Uncle, congregated
838: to eat and drink, then separated
839: with grave goodbyes to the bereaved,
840: as if some goal had been achieved.
841: Eugene turned countryman. He tasted
842: the total ownership of woods,
843: mills, lands and waters -- he whose goods
844: till then had been dispersed and wasted --
845: and glad he was he'd thus arranged
846: for his old courses to be changed.
847: {58}
848: LIV
849: It all seemed new -- for two days only --
850: the coolness of the sombre glade,
851: the expanse of fields, so wide, so lonely,
852: the murmur where the streamlet played...
853: the third day, wood and hill and grazing
854: gripped him no more; soon they were raising
855: an urge to sleep; soon, clear as clear,
856: he saw that, as in cities, here
857: boredom has just as sure an entry,
858: although there are no streets, no cards,
859: no mansions, no ballrooms, no bards.
860: Yes, spleen was waiting like a sentry,
861: and dutifully shared his life
862: just like a shadow, or a wife.
863: LV
864: No, I was born for peace abounding
865: and country stillness: there the lyre
866: has voices that are more resounding,
867: poetic dreams, a brighter fire.
868: To harmless idleness devoted,
869: on waves of far niente floated,
870: I roam by the secluded lake.
871: And every morning I awake
872: to freedom, softness and enjoyment:
873: sleep much, read little, and put down
874: the thought of volatile renown.
875: Was it not in such sweet employment
876: such shadowy and leisured ways,
877: that once I spent my happiest days?
878: {59}
879: LVI
880: O flowers, and love, and rustic leisure,
881: o fields -- to you I'm vowed at heart.
882: I regularly take much pleasure
883: in showing how to tell apart
884: myself and Eugene, lest a reader
885: of mocking turn, or else a breeder
886: of calculated slander should,
887: spying my features, as he could,
888: put back the libel on the table
889: that, like proud Byron, I can draw
890: self-portraits only -- furthermore
891: the charge that poets are unable
892: to sing of others must imply
893: the poet's only theme is ``I.''
894: LVII
895: Poets, I'll say in this connection,
896: adore the love that comes in dream.
897: In time past, objects of affection
898: peopled my sleep, and to their theme
899: my soul in secret gave survival;
900: then from the Muse there came revival:
901: my carefree song would thus reveal
902: the mountain maiden,19 my ideal,
903: and captive girls, by Salgir20 lying.
904: And now, my friends, I hear from you
905: a frequent question: ``tell me who
906: inspires your lute to sounds of sighing?
907: To whom do you, from all the train
908: of jealous girls, devote its strain?
909: {60}
910: LVIII
911: ``Whose glance, provoking inspiration,
912: rewards the music of your mind
913: with fond caress? whose adoration
914: is in your poetry enshrined?''
915: No one's, I swear by God! in sadness
916: I suffered once from all the madness
917: of love's anxiety. Blessed is he
918: who can combine it with the free
919: fever of rhyme: thereby he's doubled
920: poetry's sacred frenzy, made
921: a stride on Petrarch's path, allayed
922: the pangs with which his heart was troubled,
923: and, with it, forced renown to come --
924: but I, in love, was dull and dumb.
925: LIX
926: Love passed, the Muse appeared, the weather
927: of mind got clarity new-found;
928: now free, I once more weave together
929: emotion, thought, and magic sound;
930: I write, my heart has ceased its pining,
931: my thoughtless pen has stopped designing,
932: beside unfinished lines, a suite
933: of ladies' heads, and ladies' feet;
934: dead ash sets no more sparks a-flying;
935: I'm grieving still, but no more tears,
936: and soon, oh soon the storm's arrears
937: will in my soul be hushed and dying.
938: That's when I'll sit down to compose
939: an ode in twenty-five cantos.
940: {61}
941: LX
942: I've drawn a plan and a projection,
943: the hero's name's decided too.
944: Meanwhile my novel's opening section
945: is finished, and I've looked it through
946: meticulously; in my fiction
947: there's far too much of contradiction,
948: but I refuse to chop or change.
949: The censor's tribute, I'll arrange:
950: I'll feed the journalists for dinner
951: fruits of my labour and my ink...
952: So now be off to Neva's brink,
953: you newborn work, and like a winner
954: earn for me the rewards of fame --
955: misunderstanding, noise, and blame!
956: {62}
957: Notes to Chapter One
958: 1 ``Written in Bessarabia.'' Pushkin's note.
959: 2 Stanzas IX, XIII, XIV, XXXIX, XL and XLI were omitted by Pushkin.
960: 3 Hero of Louvet's novel about betrayed husbands.
961: 4 ``Well-known restaurateur.'' Pushkin's note.
962: 5 Hussar and friend of Pushkin.
963: 6 Vintage 1811, the year of the Comet.
964: 7 Heroine of Ozerov's tragedy Fingal.
965: 8 Playwrights of the late eighteenth and early nineteenth centuries.
966: 9 Actress in tragedy.
967: 10 Dancer and choreographer.
968: 11 Ballerina, once courted by Pushkin.
969: 12 Constantinople.
970: 13 French encyclopedist.
971: 14 Pushkin leaves blank the name of Onegin's model dandy.
972: 15 A mocking  reference to Mikhail  Muraviev's poem ``To the Goddess of
973: the Neva.''
974: 16  Millyonaya, a street  parallel to the Neva, and one block away from
975: it.
976: 17 ``Written at Odessa.'' Pushkin's note.
977: 18 ``The  author, on  his mother's  side,  is of  African  descent...''
978: Pushkin's note.
979: 19 Refers  to the  Circassian girl  in  Pushkin's  poem  The  Caucasian
980: Prisoner.
981: 20 River  in  the  Crimea.  The  reference  is to  the  harem  girls in
982: Pushkin's poem The Fountain of Bakhchisarai.
983: --------
984: Chapter Two
985: O rus!
986: Horace
987: O Russia!
988: I
989: The place where Eugene loathed his leisure
990: was an enchanting country nook:
991: there any friend of harmless pleasure
992: would bless the form his fortune took.
993: The manor house, in deep seclusion,
994: screened by a hill from storm's intrusion,
995: looked on a river: far away
996: before it was the golden play
997: of light that flowering fields reflected:
998: villages flickered far and near,
999: and cattle roamed the plain, and here
1000: a park, enormous and neglected,
1001: spread out its shadow all around --
1002: the pensive Dryads' hiding-ground.
1003: {63}
1004: II
1005: The château was of a construction
1006: befitting such a noble pile:
1007: it stood, defiant of destruction
1008: in sensible old-fashioned style.
1009: High ceilings everywhere abounded;
1010: in the saloon, brocade-surrounded,
1011: ancestral1 portraits met the view
1012: and stoves with tiles of various hue.
1013: All this has now gone out of fashion,
1014: I don't know why, but for my friend
1015: interior décor in the end
1016: excited not a hint of passion:
1017: a modish taste, a dowdy touch --
1018: both set him yawning just as much.
1019: III
1020: The rustic sage, in that apartment,
1021: forty years long would criticise
1022: his housekeeper and her department
1023: look through the pane, and squash the flies.
1024: Oak-floored, and simple as a stable:
1025: two cupboards, one divan, a table,
1026: no trace of ink, no spots, no stains.
1027: And of the cupboards, one contains
1028: a book of household calculations,
1029: the other, jugs of applejack,
1030: fruit liqueurs and an Almanack
1031: for 1808: his obligations
1032: had left the squire no time to look
1033: at any other sort of book.
1034: {64}
1035: IV
1036: Alone amid all his possessions,
1037: to pass the time was Eugene's theme:
1038: it led him, in these early sessions,
1039: to institute a new regime.
1040: A thinker in a desert mission,
1041: he changed the corvée of tradition
1042: into a small quit-rent -- and got
1043: his serfs rejoicing at their lot.
1044: But, in a fearful huff, his thrifty
1045: neighbour was sure, from this would flow
1046: consequences of hideous woe;
1047: another's grin was sly and shifty,
1048: but all concurred that, truth to speak,
1049: he was a menace, and a freak.
1050: V
1051: At first they called; but on perceiving
1052: invariably, as time went on,
1053: that from the backdoor he'd be leaving
1054: on a fast stallion from the Don,
1055: once on the highway he'd detected
1056: the noise their rustic wheels projected --
1057: they took offence at this, and broke
1058: relations off, and never spoke.
1059: ``The man's a boor; his brain is missing,
1060: he's a freemason too; for him,
1061: red wine in tumblers to the brim --
1062: but ladies' hands are not for kissing;
1063: it's yes or no, but never sir.''
1064: The vote was passed without demur.
1065: {65}
1066: VI
1067: Meanwhile another new landowner
1068: came driving to his country seat,
1069: and, in the district, this persona
1070: drew scrutiny no less complete --
1071: Vladimir Lensky, whose creator
1072: was Göttingen, his alma mater,
1073: good-looking, in the flower of age,
1074: a poet, and a Kantian sage.
1075: He'd brought back all the fruits of learning
1076: from German realms of mist and steam,
1077: freedom's enthusiastic dream,
1078: a spirit strange, a spirit burning,
1079: an eloquence of fevered strength,
1080: and raven curls of shoulder-length.
1081: VII
1082: He was too young to have been blighted
1083: by the cold world's corrupt finesse;
1084: his soul still blossomed out, and lighted
1085: at a friend's word, a girl's caress.
1086: In heart's affairs, a sweet beginner,
1087: he fed on hope's deceptive dinner;
1088: the world's éclat, its thunder-roll,
1089: still captivated his young soul.
1090: He sweetened up with fancy's icing
1091: the uncertainties within his heart;
1092: for him, the objective on life's chart
1093: was still mysterious and enticing --
1094: something to rack his brains about,
1095: suspecting wonders would come out.
1096: {66}
1097: VIII
1098: He was convinced, a kindred creature
1099: would be allied to him by fate;
1100: that, meanwhile, pinched and glum of feature,
1101: from day to day she could but wait;
1102: and he believed his friends were ready
1103: to put on chains for him, and steady
1104: their hand to grapple slander's cup,
1105: in his defence, and smash it up;
1106: < that there existed, for the indulgence
1107: of human friendship, holy men,
1108: immortals picked by fate for when,
1109: with irresistible refulgence,
1110: their breed would (some years after this)
1111: shine out and bring the world to bliss. >2
1112: IX
1113: Compassion, yes, and indignation,
1114: honest devotion to the good,
1115: bitter-sweet glory's inspiration,
1116: already stirred him as they should.
1117: He roamed the world, his lyre behind him;
1118: Schiller and Goethe had refined him,
1119: and theirs was the poetic flame
1120: that fired his soul, to burn the same;
1121: the Muses' lofty arts and fashions,
1122: fortunate one, he'd not disgrace;
1123: but in his songs kept pride of place
1124: for the sublime, and for the passions
1125: of virgin fancy, and again
1126: the charm of what was grave and plain.
1127: {67}
1128: X
1129: He sang of love, to love subjected,
1130: his song was limpid in its tune
1131: as infant sleep, or the unaffected
1132: thoughts of a girl, or as the moon
1133: through heaven's expanse serenely flying,
1134: that queen of secrets and of sighing.
1135: He sang of grief and parting-time,
1136: of something vague, some misty clime;
1137: roses romantically blowing;
1138: of many distant lands he sang
1139: where in the heart of silence rang
1140: his sobs, where his live tears were flowing;
1141: he sang of lifetime's yellowed page --
1142: when not quite eighteen years of age.
1143: XI
1144: But in that desert his attainments
1145: only to Eugene showed their worth;
1146: Lensky disliked the entertainments
1147: of neighbouring owners of the earth --
1148: he fled from their resounding chatter!
1149: Their talk, so sound on every matter,
1150: on liquor, and on hay brought in,
1151: on kennels, and on kith and kin,
1152: it had no sparkle of sensation,
1153: it lacked, of course, poetic heart,
1154: sharpness of wit, and social art,
1155: and logic; yet the conversation
1156: upon the side of the distaff --
1157: that was less clever still by half.
1158: {68}
1159: XII
1160: Vladimir, wealthy and good-looking,
1161: was asked around as quite a catch --
1162: such is the usual country cooking;
1163: and all the neighbours planned a match
1164: between their girls and this half-Russian.
1165: As soon as he appears, discussion
1166: touches obliquely, but with speed,
1167: on the dull life that bachelors lead;
1168: and then it's tea that comes to mention,
1169: and Dunya works the samovar;
1170: and soon they bring her... a guitar
1171: and whisper ``Dunya, pay attention!''
1172: then, help me God, she caterwauls:
1173: ``Come to me in my golden halls.''
1174: XIII
1175: Lensky of course was quite untainted
1176: by any itch for marriage ties;
1177: instead the chance to get acquainted
1178: with Eugene proved a tempting prize.
1179: So, verse and prose, they came together.
1180: No ice and flame, no stormy weather
1181: and granite, were so far apart.
1182: At first, disparity of heart
1183: rendered them tedious to each other;
1184: then liking grew, then every day
1185: they met on horseback; quickly they
1186: became like brother knit to brother.
1187: Friendship, as I must own to you,
1188: blooms when there's nothing else to do.
1189: {69}
1190: XIV
1191: But friendship, as between our heroes,
1192: can't really be: for we've outgrown
1193: old prejudice; all men are zeros,
1194: the units are ourselves alone.
1195: Napoleon's our sole inspiration;
1196: the millions of two-legged creation
1197: for us are instruments and tools;
1198: feeling is quaint, and fit for fools.
1199: More tolerant in his conception
1200: than most. Evgeny, though he knew
1201: and scorned his fellows through and through,
1202: yet, as each rule has its exception,
1203: people there were he glorified,
1204: feelings he valued -- from outside.
1205: XV
1206: He smiled as Lensky talked: the heady
1207: perfervid language of the bard,
1208: his mind, in judgement still unsteady,
1209: and always the inspired regard --
1210: to Eugene all was new and thrilling;
1211: he struggled to bite back the chilling
1212: word on his lips, and thought: it's sheer
1213: folly for me to interfere
1214: with such a blissful, brief infection --
1215: even without me it will sink;
1216: but meanwhile let him live, and think
1217: the universe is all perfection;
1218: youth is a fever; we must spare
1219: its natural right to rave and flare.
1220: {70}
1221: XVI
1222: Between them, every topic started
1223: reflection or provoked dispute:
1224: treaties of nations long departed,
1225: and good and ill, and learning's fruit,
1226: the prejudices of the ages,
1227: the secrets of the grave, the pages
1228: of fate, and life, each in its turn
1229: became their scrutiny's concern.
1230: In the white heat of some dissension
1231: the abstracted poet would bring forth
1232: fragments of poems from the North,
1233: which, listening with some condescension,
1234: the tolerant Evgeny heard --
1235: but scarcely understood a word.
1236: XVII
1237: But it was passion that preempted
1238: the thoughts of my two anchorites.
1239: From that rough spell at last exempted,
1240: Onegin spoke about its flights
1241: with sighs unconsciously regretful.
1242: Happy is he who's known its fretful
1243: empire, and fled it; happier still
1244: is he who's never felt its will,
1245: he who has cooled down love with parting,
1246: and hate with malice; he whose life
1247: is yawned away with friends and wife
1248: untouched by envy's bitter smarting,
1249: who on a deuce, that famous cheat,
1250: has never staked his family seat.
1251: {71}
1252: XVIII
1253: When we've retreated to the banner
1254: of calm and reason, when the flame
1255: of passion's out, and its whole manner
1256: become a joke to us, its game,
1257: its wayward tricks, its violent surging,
1258: its echoes, its belated urging,
1259: reduced to sense, not without pain --
1260: we sometimes like to hear again
1261: passion's rough language talked by others,
1262: and feel once more emotion's ban.
1263: So a disabled soldier-man,
1264: retired, forgotten by his brothers,
1265: in his small shack, will listen well
1266: to tales that young moustachios tell.
1267: XIX
1268: But it's the talent for concealing
1269: that ardent youth entirely lacks;
1270: hate, love, joy, sorrow -- every feeling,
1271: it blabs, and spills them in its tracks.
1272: As, lovingly, in his confession,
1273: the poet's heart found full expression,
1274: Eugene, with solemn face, paid heed,
1275: and felt himself love's invalide.
1276: Lensky ingenuously related
1277: his conscience's record, and so
1278: Onegin swiftly came to know
1279: his tale of youthful love, narrated
1280: with deep emotion through and through,
1281: to us, though, not exactly new.
1282: {72}
1283: XX
1284: Ah, he had loved a love that never
1285: is known today; only a soul
1286: that raves with poetry can ever
1287: be doomed to feel it: there's one goal
1288: perpetually, one goal for dreaming,
1289: one customary object gleaming,
1290: one customary grief each hour!
1291: not separation's chilling power,
1292: no years of absence past returning,
1293: no beauties of a foreign clime,
1294: no noise of gaiety, no time
1295: devoted to the Muse, or learning,
1296: nothing could alter or could tire
1297: this soul that glowed with virgin fire.
1298: XXI
1299: Since earliest boyhood he had doted
1300: on Olga; from heart's ache still spared,
1301: with tenderness he'd watched and noted
1302: her girlhood games; in them he'd shared,
1303: by deep and shady woods protected;
1304: the crown of marriage was projected
1305: for them by fathers who, as friends
1306: and neighbours, followed the same ends.
1307: Away inside that unassuming
1308: homestead, before her parents' gaze,
1309: she blossomed in the graceful ways
1310: of innocence: a lily blooming
1311: in deepest grasses, quite alone,
1312: to bee and butterfly unknown.
1313: {73}
1314: XXII
1315: And our young poet -- Olga fired him
1316: in his first dream of passion's fruit,
1317: and thoughts of her were what inspired him
1318: to the first meanings of his flute.
1319: Farewell the games of golden childhood!
1320: he fell in love with darkest wildwood,
1321: solitude, stillness and the night,
1322: the stars, the moon -- celestial light
1323: to which so oft we've dedicated
1324: those walks amid the gloom and calm
1325: of evening, and those tears, the balm
1326: of secret pain... but it's now rated
1327: by judgement of the modern camp
1328: almost as good as a dim lamp.
1329: XXIII
1330: Full of obedience and demureness,
1331: as gay as morning and as clear,
1332: poetic in her simple pureness,
1333: sweet as a lover's kiss, and dear,
1334: in Olga everything expresses --
1335: the skyblue eyes, the flaxen tresses,
1336: smile, voice and movements, little waist --
1337: take any novel, clearly traced
1338: you're sure to find her portrait in it:
1339: a portrait with a charming touch;
1340: once I too liked it very much;
1341: but now it bores me every minute.
1342: Reader, the elder sister now
1343: must be my theme, if you'll allow.
1344: {74}
1345: XXIV
1346: Tatyana3 was her name... I own it,
1347: self-willed it may be just the same;
1348: but it's the first time you'll have known it,
1349: a novel graced with such a name.
1350: What of it? it's euphonious, pleasant,
1351: and yet inseparably present,
1352: I know it, in the thoughts of all
1353: are old times, and the servants' hall.
1354: We must confess that taste deserts us
1355: even in our names (and how much worse
1356: when we begin to talk of verse);
1357: culture, so far from healing, hurts us;
1358: what it's transported to our shore
1359: is mincing manners -- nothing more.
1360: XXV
1361: So she was called Tatyana. Truly
1362: she lacked her sister's beauty, lacked
1363: the rosy bloom that glowed so newly
1364: to catch the eye and to attract.
1365: Shy as a savage, silent, tearful,
1366: wild as a forest deer, and fearful,
1367: Tatyana had a changeling look
1368: in her own home. She never took
1369: to kissing or caressing father
1370: or mother; and in all the play
1371: of children, though as young as they,
1372: she never joined, or skipped, but rather
1373: in silence all day she'd remain
1374: ensconced beside the window-pane.
1375: {75}
1376: XXVI
1377: Reflection was her friend and pleasure
1378: right from the cradle of her days;
1379: it touched with reverie her leisure,
1380: adorning all its country ways.
1381: Her tender touch had never fingered
1382: the needle, never had she lingered
1383: to liven with a silk atour
1384: the linen stretched on the tambour.
1385: Sign of the urge for domination:
1386: in play with her obedient doll
1387: the child prepares for protocol --
1388: that corps of social legislation --
1389: and to it, with a grave import,
1390: repeats what her mama has taught.
1391: XXVII
1392: Tatyana had no dolls to dandle,
1393: not even in her earliest age;
1394: she'd never tell them news or scandal
1395: or novelties from fashion's page.
1396: Tatyana never knew the attraction
1397: of childish pranks: a chilled reaction
1398: to horror-stories told at night
1399: in winter was her heart's delight.
1400: Whenever nyanya had collected
1401: for Olga, on the spreading lawn,
1402: her little friends, Tatyana'd yawn,
1403: she'd never join the game selected,
1404: for she was bored by laughs and noise
1405: and by the sound of silly joys.
1406: {76}
1407: XXVIII
1408: She loved the balcony, the session
1409: of waiting for the dawn to blush,
1410: when, in pale sky, the stars' procession
1411: fades from the view, and in the hush
1412: earth's rim grows light, and a forewarning
1413: whisper of breeze announces morning,
1414: and slowly day begins to climb.
1415: In winter, when for longer time
1416: the shades of night within their keeping
1417: hold half the world still unreleased,
1418: and when, by misty moon, the east
1419: is softly, indolently sleeping,
1420: wakened at the same hour of night
1421: Tatyana'd rise by candlelight.
1422: XXIX
1423: From early on she loved romances,
1424: they were her only food... and so
1425: she fell in love with all the fancies
1426: of Richardson and of Rousseau.
1427: Her father, kindly, well-regarded,
1428: but in an earlier age retarded,
1429: could see no harm in books; himself
1430: he never took one from the shelf,
1431: thought them a pointless peccadillo;
1432: and cared not what his daughter kept
1433: by way of secret tome that slept
1434: until the dawn beneath her pillow.
1435: His wife, just like Tatyana, had
1436: on Richardson gone raving mad.
1437: {77}
1438: XXX
1439: And not because she'd read him, either,
1440: and not because she'd once preferred
1441: Lovelace, or Grandison, or neither;
1442: but in the old days she had heard
1443: about them -- nineteen to the dozen --
1444: so often from her Moscow cousin
1445: Princess Alina. She was still
1446: engaged then -- but against her will;
1447: loved someone else, not her intended,
1448: someone towards whose heart and mind
1449: her feelings were far more inclined --
1450: this Grandison of hers was splendid,
1451: a fop, a punter on the cards,
1452: and junior Ensign in the Guards.
1453: XXXI
1454: She was like him and always sported
1455: the latest fashions of the town;
1456: but, without asking, they transported
1457: her to the altar and the crown.
1458: The better to dispel her sorrow
1459: her clever husband on the morrow
1460: took her to his estate, where she,
1461: at first, with God knows whom to see,
1462: in tears and violent tossing vented
1463: her grief, and nearly ran away.
1464: Then, plunged in the housekeeper's day,
1465: she grew accustomed, and contented.
1466: In stead of happiness, say I,
1467: custom's bestowed us from on high.
1468: {78}
1469: XXXII
1470: For it was custom that consoled her
1471: in grief that nothing else could mend;
1472: soon a great truth came to enfold her
1473: and give her comfort to the end:
1474: she found, in labours and in leisure,
1475: the secret of her husband's measure,
1476: and ruled him like an autocrat --
1477: so all went smoothly after that.
1478: Mushrooms in brine, for winter eating,
1479: fieldwork directed from the path,
1480: accounts, shaved forelocks,4 Sunday bath;
1481: meantime she'd give the maids a beating
1482: if her cross mood was at its worst --
1483: but never asked her husband first.
1484: XXXIII
1485: No, soon she changed her old demeanour:
1486: girls' albums, signed in blood for choice;
1487: Praskovya re-baptized ``Polina'';
1488: conversing in a singsong voice;
1489: lacing her stays up very tightly;
1490: pronouncing through her nose politely
1491: the Russian N, like N in French;
1492: soon all that went without a wrench:
1493: album and stays, Princess Alina,
1494: sentiment, notebook, verses, all
1495: she quite forgot -- began to call
1496: ``Akulka'' the onetime Selina,
1497: and introduced, for the last lap,
1498: a quilted chamber-robe and cap.
1499: {79}
1500: XXXIV
1501: Her loving spouse with approbation
1502: left her to follow her own line,
1503: trusted her without hesitation,
1504: and wore his dressing-gown to dine.
1505: His life went sailing in calm weather;
1506: sometimes the evening brought together
1507: neighbours and friends in kindly group,
1508: a plain, unceremonious troop,
1509: for grumbling, gossiping and swearing
1510: and for a chuckle or a smile.
1511: The evening passes, and meanwhile
1512: here's tea that Olga's been preparing;
1513: after that, supper's served, and so
1514: bed-time, and time for guests to go.
1515: XXXV
1516: Throughout their life, so calm, so peaceful,
1517: sweet old tradition was preserved:
1518: for them, in Butterweek5 the greaseful,
1519: Russian pancakes were always served;
1520: < ...
1521: ... >2
1522: they needed kvas like air; at table
1523: their guests, for all they ate and drank,
1524: were served in order of their rank.
1525: {80}
1526: XXXVI
1527: And so they lived, two ageing mortals,
1528: till he at last was summoned down
1529: into the tomb's wide open portals,
1530: and once again received a crown.
1531: Just before dinner, from his labours
1532: he rested -- wept for by his neighbours,
1533: his children and his faithful wife,
1534: far more than most who leave this life.
1535: He was a good and simple barin;6
1536: above the dust of his remains
1537: the funeral monument explains:
1538: ``A humble sinner, Dimitry Larin,
1539: beneath the stone reposes here,
1540: servant of God, and Brigadier.''
1541: XXXVII
1542: Lensky, restored to his manorial
1543: penates, came to cast an eye
1544: over his neighbour's plain memorial,
1545: and offer to that ash a sigh;
1546: sadly he mourned for the departed.
1547: ``Poor Yorick,'' said he, broken-hearted:
1548: ``he dandled me as a small boy.
1549: How many times I made a toy
1550: of his Ochákov7 decoration!
1551: He destined Olga's hand for me,
1552: kept asking: "shall I live to see"...''
1553: so, full of heart-felt tribulation,
1554: Lensky composed in autograph
1555: a madrigal for epitaph.
1556: {81}
1557: XXXVIII
1558: There too, he honoured, hotly weeping,
1559: his parents' patriarchal dust
1560: with lines to mark where they were sleeping...
1561: Alas! the generations must,
1562: as fate's mysterious purpose burrows,
1563: reap a brief harvest on their furrows;
1564: they rise and ripen and fall dead:
1565: others will follow where they tread...
1566: and thus our race, so fluctuating,
1567: grows, surges, boils, for lack of room
1568: presses its forebears to the tomb.
1569: We too shall find our hour is waiting;
1570: it will be our descendants who
1571: out of this world will crowd us too.
1572: XXXIX
1573: So glut yourselves until you're sated
1574: on this unstable life, my friends!
1575: its nullity I've always hated,
1576: I know too surely how it ends.
1577: I'm blind to every apparition;
1578: and yet a distant admonition
1579: of hope sometimes disturbs my heart;
1580: it would be painful to depart
1581: and leave no faint footprint of glory...
1582: I never lived or wrote for praise;
1583: yet how I wish that I might raise
1584: to high renown my doleful story,
1585: that there be just one voice which came,
1586: like a true friend, to speak my name.
1587: {82}
1588: XL
1589: And someone's heart will feel a quiver,
1590: for maybe fortune will have saved
1591: from drowning's death in Lethe river
1592: the strophe over which I slaved;
1593: perhaps -- for flattering hope will linger --
1594: some future dunce will point a finger
1595: at my famed portrait and will say:
1596: he was a poet in his day.
1597: I thank him without reservation,
1598: the peaceful Muses' devotee,
1599: whose memory will preserve for me
1600: the fleeting works of my creation,
1601: whose kindly hand will ruffle down
1602: the laurel in the old man's crown!
1603: {83}
1604: Notes to Chapter Two
1605: 1 Pushkin first wrote ``imperial portraits''; but this he later altered
1606: ``for reasons of censorship'' because, as Nabokov explains, ``tsars were not
1607: to be mentioned in so offhand a way''.
1608: 2 Lines discarded by Pushkin.
1609: 3  ``Sweet-sounding Greek names like  Agathon... etc., are only current
1610: in Russia among the common people.'' Pushkin's note.
1611: 4 Serfs chosen as recruits for the army had their forelock cut off.
1612: 5 The week before Lent.
1613: 6 Gentleman, squire.
1614: 7 Fortress captured from the Turks in 1788.
1615: --------
1616: Chapter Three
1617: Elle était fille, elle était amoureuse.
1618: Malfilâtre
1619: ``You're off? why, there's a poet for you!''
1620: ``Goodbye, Onegin, time I went.''
1621: ``Well, I won't hold you up or bore you;
1622: but where are all your evenings spent?''
1623: ``At the Larins'!'' ``But how mysterious.
1624: For goodness' sake, you can't be serious
1625: killing each evening off like that?''
1626: ``You're wrong.'' ``But what I wonder at
1627: is this -- one sees from here the party:
1628: in first place -- listen, am I right? --
1629: a simple Russian family night:
1630: the guests are feasted, good and hearty,
1631: on jam, and speeches in regard
1632: to rains, and flax, and the stockyard.''
1633: {84}
1634: II
1635: ``I don't see what's so bad about it.''
1636: ``Boredom, that's what so bad, my friend.''
1637: ``Your modish world, I'll do without it;
1638: give me the homely hearth, and lend...''
1639: ``You pile one eclogue on another!
1640: for God's sake, that will do. But, brother,
1641: you're really going? Well, I'm sad.
1642: Now, Lensky, would it be so bad
1643: for me to glimpse this Phyllis ever
1644: with whom your thoughts are so obsessed --
1645: pen, tears, and rhymes, and all the rest?
1646: Present me, please.'' ``You're joking.'' ``Never.''
1647: ``Gladly.'' ``So when?'' ``Why not tonight?
1648: They will receive us with delight.''
1649: III
1650: ``Let's go.'' The friends, all haste and vigour,
1651: drive there, and with formality
1652: are treated to the fullest rigour
1653: of old-lime hospitality.
1654: The protocol is all one wishes:
1655: the jams appear in little dishes;
1656: on a small table's oilcloth sheen
1657: the jug of bilberry wine is seen.1
1658: {85}
1659: IV
1660: And home was now their destination;
1661: as by the shortest way they flew,
1662: this was our heroes' conversation
1663: secretly overheard by you.
1664: ``You yawn, Onegin?'' ``As I'm used to.''
1665: ``This time I think you've been reduced to
1666: new depths of boredom.'' ``No, the same.
1667: The fields are dark, since evening came.
1668: Drive on, Andryushka! quicker, quicker!
1669: the country's pretty stupid here!
1670: oh, à propos: Larin's a dear
1671: simple old lady; but the liquor --
1672: I'm much afraid that bilberry wine
1673: won't benefit these guts of mine.''
1674: V
1675: ``But tell me, which one was Tatyana?''
1676: ``She was the one who looked as still
1677: and melancholy as Svetlana,2
1678: and sat down by the window-sill.''
1679: ``The one you love's the younger daughter?''
1680: ``Why not?'' ``I'd choose the other quarter
1681: if I, like you, had been a bard.
1682: Olga's no life in her regard:
1683: the roundest face that you've set eyes on,
1684: a pretty girl exactly like
1685: any Madonna by Van Dyck:
1686: a dumb moon, on a dumb horizon.''
1687: Lensky had a curt word to say
1688: and then sat silent all the way.
1689: {86}
1690: VI
1691: Meanwhile the news of Eugene coming
1692: to the Larins' had caused a spout
1693: of gossip, and set comment humming
1694: among the neighbours round about.
1695: Conjecture found unending matter:
1696: there was a general furtive chatter,
1697: and jokes and spiteful gossip ran
1698: claiming Tatyana'd found her man;
1699: and some were even testifying
1700: the marriage plans were all exact
1701: but held up by the simple fact
1702: that modish rings were still a-buying.
1703: Of Lensky's fate they said no more --
1704: they'd settled that some years before.
1705: VII
1706: Tatyana listened with vexation
1707: to all this tattle, yet at heart
1708: in indescribable elation,
1709: despite herself, rehearsed the part:
1710: the thought sank in, and penetrated:
1711: she fell in love -- the hour was fated...
1712: so fires of spring will bring to birth
1713: a seedling fallen in the earth.
1714: Her feelings in their weary session
1715: had long been wasting and enslaved
1716: by pain and languishment; she craved
1717: the fateful diet; by depression
1718: her heart had long been overrun:
1719: her soul was waiting... for someone.
1720: {87}
1721: VIII
1722: Tatyana now need wait no longer.
1723: Her eyes were opened, and she said
1724: ``this is the one!'' Ah, ever stronger,
1725: in sultry sleep, in lonely bed,
1726: all day, all night, his presence fills her,
1727: by magic everything instils her
1728: with thoughts of him in ceaseless round.
1729: She hates a friendly voice's sound,
1730: or servants waiting on her pleasure.
1731: Sunk in dejection, she won't hear
1732: the talk of guests when they appear;
1733: she calls down curses on their leisure,
1734: and, when one's least prepared for it
1735: their tendency to call, and sit.
1736: IX
1737: Now, she devours, with what attention,
1738: delicious novels, laps them up;
1739: and all their ravishing invention
1740: with sheer enchantment fills her cup!
1741: These figures from the world of seeming,
1742: embodied by the power of dreaming,
1743: the lover of Julie Wolmar,3
1744: and Malek Adel,4 de Linar,5
1745: and Werther, martyred and doom-laden,
1746: and Grandison beyond compare,
1747: who sets me snoring then and there --
1748: all for our tender dreamy maiden
1749: are coloured in a single tone,
1750: all blend into Eugene alone.
1751: {88}
1752: X
1753: Seeing herself as a creation --
1754: Clarissa, Julie, or Delphine6 --
1755: by writers of her admiration,
1756: Tatyana, lonely heroine,
1757: roamed the still forest like a ranger,
1758: sought in her book, that text of danger
1759: and found her dreams, her secret fire,
1760: the full fruit of her heart's desire;
1761: she sighed, and in a trance coopted
1762: another's joy, another's breast,
1763: whispered by heart a note addressed
1764: to the hero that she'd adopted.
1765: But ours, whatever he might be,
1766: ours was no Grandison -- not he.
1767: XI
1768: Lending his tone a grave inflection,
1769: the ardent author of the past
1770: showed one a pattern of perfection
1771: in which his hero's mould was cast.
1772: He gave this figure -- loved with passion,
1773: wronged always in disgraceful fashion --
1774: a soul of sympathy and grace,
1775: and brains, and an attractive face.
1776: Always our fervid hero tended
1777: pure passion's flame, and in a trice
1778: would launch into self-sacrifice;
1779: always before the volume ended
1780: due punishment was handed down
1781: to vice, while virtue got its crown.
1782: {89}
1783: XII
1784: Today a mental fog enwraps us,
1785: each moral puts us in a doze,
1786: even in novels, vice entraps us,
1787: yes, even there its triumph grows.
1788: Now that the British Muse is able
1789: to wreck a maiden's sleep with fable,
1790: the idol that she'll most admire
1791: is either the distrait Vampire,
1792: Melmoth,7 whose roaming never ceases,
1793: Sbogar,8 mysterious through and through,
1794: the Corsair, or the Wandering Jew.
1795: Lord Byron, with his shrewd caprices,
1796: dressed up a desperate egoism
1797: to look like sad romanticism.
1798: XIII
1799: In this, dear reader, if you know it,
1800: show me the sense. Divine decree
1801: may wind up my career as poet;
1802: perhaps, though Phoebus warns, I'll see
1803: installed in me a different devil,
1804: and sink to prose's humble level:
1805: a novel on the established line
1806: may then amuse my glad decline.
1807: No secret crimes, and no perditions,
1808: shall make my story grim as hell;
1809: no, quite naively I'll retell
1810: a Russian family's old traditions;
1811: love's melting dreams shall fill my rhyme,
1812: and manners of an earlier time.
1813: {90}
1814: XIV
1815: I'll catalogue each simple saying
1816: in father's or old uncle's book,
1817: and tell of children's plighted playing
1818: by ancient limes, or by a brook;
1819: and after jealousy's grim weather
1820: I'll part them, bring them back together;
1821: I'll make them spar another round,
1822: then to the altar, to be crowned.
1823: I'll conjure up that swooning fashion
1824: of ardent speech, that aching flow
1825: of language which, so long ago,
1826: facing a belle I loved with passion,
1827: my tongue kept drawing from the heart --
1828: but now I've rather lost the art.
1829: XV
1830: Tatyana dear, with you I'm weeping:
1831: for you have, at this early date,
1832: into a modish tyrant's keeping
1833: resigned disposal of your fate.
1834: Dear Tanya, you're condemned to perish;
1835: but first, the dreams that hope can cherish
1836: evoke for you a sombre bliss;
1837: you learn life's sweetness, and with this
1838: you drink the magic draught of yearning,
1839: that poison brew; and in your mind
1840: reverie hounds you, and you find
1841: shelter for trysts at every turning;
1842: in front of you, on every hand,
1843: you see your fated tempter stand.
1844: {91}
1845: XVI
1846: Tatyana, hunted by love's anguish,
1847: has made the park her brooding-place,
1848: suddenly lowering eyes that languish,
1849: too faint to stir a further pace:
1850: her bosom heaves, her cheeks are staring
1851: scarlet with passion's instant flaring,
1852: upon her lips the breathing dies,
1853: noise in her ears, glare in her eyes...
1854: then night comes on; the moon's patrolling
1855: far-distant heaven's vaulted room;
1856: a nightingale, in forest gloom,
1857: sets a sonorous cadence rolling --
1858: Tatyana, sleepless in the dark,
1859: makes to her nurse low-voiced remark:
1860: XVII
1861: ``I can't sleep, nyanya: it's so stifling!
1862: open the window, sit down near.''
1863: ``Why, Tanya, what...?'' ``All's dull and trifling.
1864: The olden days, I want to hear...''
1865: ``What of them, Tanya? I was able,
1866: years back, to call up many a fable;
1867: I kept in mind an ancient store
1868: of tales of girls, and ghosts, and lore:
1869: but now my brain is darkened, Tanya:
1870: now I've forgotten all I knew.
1871: A sorry state of things, it's true!
1872: My mind is fuddled.'' ``Tell me, nyanya,
1873: your early life, unlock your tongue:
1874: were you in love when you were young?''
1875: {92}
1876: XVIII
1877: ``What nonsense, Tanya! in those other
1878: ages we'd never heard of love:
1879: why, at the thought, my husband's mother
1880: had chased me to the world above.''
1881: ``How did you come to marry, nyanya?''
1882: ``I reckon, by God's will. My Vanya
1883: was younger still, but at that stage
1884: I was just thirteen years of age.
1885: Two weeks the matchmaker was plying
1886: to see my kin, and in the end
1887: my father blessed me. So I'd spend
1888: my hours in fear and bitter crying.
1889: Then, crying, they untwined my plait,
1890: and sang me to the altar-mat.
1891: XIX
1892: ``So to strange kinsfolk I was taken...
1893: but you're not paying any heed.''
1894: ``Oh nurse, I'm sad, I'm sad, I'm shaken,
1895: I'm sick, my dear, I'm sick indeed.
1896: I'm near to sobbing, near to weeping!...''
1897: ``You're ill, God have you in his keeping,
1898: the Lord have mercy on us all!
1899: whatever you may need, just call...
1900: I'll sprinkle you with holy water,
1901: you're all in fever... heavens above.''
1902: ``Nurse, I'm not ill; I... I'm in love.''
1903: ``The Lord God be with you, my daughter!''
1904: and, hands a-tremble, Nyanya prayed
1905: and put a cross-sign on the maid.
1906: {93}
1907: XX
1908: ``I am in love,'' Tatyana's wailing
1909: whisper repeated to the crone.
1910: ``My dearest heart, you're sick and ailing.''
1911: ``I am in love; leave me alone.''
1912: And all the while the moon was shining
1913: and with its feeble glow outlining
1914: the girl's pale charms, her loosened hair,
1915: her drops of tears, and seated there,
1916: in quilted coat, where rays were gleaming
1917: on a small bench by Tanya's bed,
1918: the grey-haired nurse with kerchiefed head;
1919: and everything around was dreaming,
1920: in the deep stillness of the night,
1921: bathed in the moon's inspiring light.
1922: XXI
1923: Tatyana watched the moon, and floated
1924: through distant regions of the heart...
1925: A thought was born, and quickly noted...
1926: ``Go, nurse, and leave me here apart.
1927: Give me a pen and give me paper,
1928: bring up a table, and a taper;
1929: good night; I swear I'll lie down soon.''
1930: She was alone, lit by the moon.
1931: Elbow on table, spirit seething,
1932: still filled with Eugene, Tanya wrote,
1933: and in her unconsidered note
1934: all a pure maiden's love was breathing.
1935: She folds the page, lays down the plume.,
1936: Tatyana! it's addressed... to whom?
1937: {94}
1938: XXII
1939: I've known too many a haughty beauty,
1940: cold, pure as ice, and as unkind,
1941: inexorably wed to duty,
1942: unfathomable to the mind;
1943: shocked by their modish pride, and fleeing
1944: the utter virtue of their being,
1945: I've run a mile, I must avow,
1946: having decyphered on their brow
1947: hell's terrifying imprecation:
1948: ``Abandon hope for evermore.''9
1949: Our love is what they most abhor;
1950: our terror is their consolation.
1951: Ladies of such a cast, I think,
1952: you too have seen on Neva's brink.
1953: XXIII
1954: Thronged by adorers, I've detected
1955: another, freakish one, who stays
1956: quite self-absorbed and unaffected
1957: by sighs of passion or by praise.
1958: To my astonishment I've seen her,
1959: having by her severe demeanour
1960: frightened to death a timid love,
1961: revive it with another shove --
1962: at least by a regretful kindness;
1963: at least her tone is sometimes found
1964: more tender than it used to sound.
1965: I've seen how, trustful in his blindness,
1966: the youthful lover once again
1967: runs after what is sweet, and vain.
1968: {95}
1969: XXIV
1970: Why is Tatyana guiltier-seeming?
1971: is it that she, poor simple sweet,
1972: believes in her elected dreaming
1973: and has no knowledge of deceit?
1974: that, artless, and without concealing,
1975: her love obeys the laws of feeling,
1976: that she's so trustful, and imbued
1977: by heaven with such an unsubdued
1978: imagination, with such reason,
1979: such stubborn brain, and vivid will,
1980: and heart so tender, it can still
1981: burst to a fiery blaze in season?
1982: Such feckless passion -- as I live,
1983: is this then what you can't forgive?
1984: XXV
1985: The flirt has reason's cool volition;
1986: Tatyana's love is no by-play,
1987: she yields to it without condition
1988: like a sweet child. She'll never say:
1989: ``By virtue of procrastinating
1990: we'll keep love's price appreciating,
1991: we'll draw it deeper in our net;
1992: first, we'll take vanity, and let
1993: hope sting it, then we'll try deploying
1994: doubts, to exhaust the heart, then fire
1995: jealousy's flame, to light desire;
1996: else, having found his pleasure cloying,
1997: the cunning prisoner can quite well
1998: at any hour escape his cell.''
1999: {96}
2000: XXVI
2001: I see another problem looming:
2002: to save the honour of our land
2003: I must translate -- there's no presuming --
2004: the letter from Tatyana's hand:
2005: her Russian was as thin as vapour,
2006: she never read a Russian paper,
2007: our native speech had never sprung
2008: unhesitating from her tongue,
2009: she wrote in French... what a confession!
2010: what can one do? as said above,
2011: until this day, a lady's love
2012: in Russian never found expression,
2013: till now our language -- proud, God knows --
2014: has hardly mastered postal prose.
2015: XXVII
2016: They should be forced to read in Russian,
2017: I hear you say. But can you see
2018: a lady -- what a grim discussion! --
2019: with The Well-Meaner10 on her knee?
2020: I ask you, each and every poet!
2021: the darling objects -- don't you know it? --
2022: for whom, to expiate your crimes,
2023: you've made so many secret rhymes,
2024: to whom your hearts are dedicated,
2025: is it not true that Russian speech,
2026: so sketchily possessed by each,
2027: by all is sweetly mutilated,
2028: and it's the foreign phrase that trips
2029: like native idiom from their lips?
2030: {97}
2031: XXVIII
2032: Protect me from such apparition
2033: on dance-floor, at breakup of ball,
2034: as bonneted Academician
2035: or seminarist in yellow shawl!
2036: To me, unsmiling lips bring terror,
2037: however scarlet; free from error
2038: of grammar, Russian language too.
2039: Now, to my cost it may be true
2040: that generations of new beauties,
2041: heeding the press, will make us look
2042: more closely at the grammar-book;
2043: that verse will turn to useful duties;
2044: on me, all this has no effect:
2045: tradition still keeps my respect.
2046: XXIX
2047: No, incorrect and careless chatter,
2048: words mispronounced, thoughts ill-expressed
2049: evoke emotion's pitter-patter,
2050: now as before, inside my breast;
2051: too weak to change, I'm staying vicious,
2052: I still find Gallicism delicious
2053: as youthful sinning, or the strains
2054: of Bogdanóvich's11 refrains.
2055: But that's enough. My beauty's letter
2056: must now employ my pen; somehow
2057: I gave my word, alas, though now
2058: a blank default would suit me better.
2059: I own it: tender Parny's12 rhyme
2060: is out of fashion in our time.
2061: {98}
2062: XXX
2063: Bard13 of The Feasts, and heart's depression,
2064: if you'd still been with me, dear friend,
2065: I would have had the indiscretion
2066: to ask of you that you transcend
2067: in music's own bewitching fashion
2068: the foreign words a maiden's passion
2069: found for its utterance that night.
2070: Where are you? come -- and my own right
2071: with an obeisance I'll hand over...
2072: But he, by sad and rocky ways,
2073: with heart that's grown unused to praise,
2074: on Finland's coast a lonely rover --
2075: he doesn't hear when I address
2076: his soul with murmurs of distress.
2077: XXXI
2078: Tatyana's letter, treasured ever
2079: as sacred, lies before me still.
2080: I read with secret pain, and never
2081: can read enough to get my fill.
2082: Who taught her an address so tender,
2083: such careless language of surrender?
