2084: Who taught her all this mad, slapdash,
2085: heartfelt, imploring, touching trash
2086: fraught with enticement and disaster?
2087: It baffles me. But I'll repeat
2088: here a weak version, incomplete,
2089: pale transcript of a vivid master,
2090: or Freischütz as it might be played
2091: by nervous hands of a schoolmaid:
2092: {99}
2093: Tatyana's Letter to Onegin
2094: ``I write to you -- no more confession
2095: is needed, nothing's left to tell.
2096: I know it's now in your discretion
2097: with scorn to make my world a hell.
2098: ``But, if you've kept some faint impression
2099: of pity for my wretched state,
2100: you'll never leave me to my fate.
2101: At first I thought it out of season
2102: to speak; believe me: of my shame
2103: you'd not so much as know the name,
2104: if I'd possessed the slightest reason
2105: to hope that even once a week
2106: I might have seen you, heard you speak
2107: on visits to us, and in greeting
2108: I might have said a word, and then
2109: thought, day and night, and thought again
2110: about one thing, till our next meeting.
2111: But you're not sociable, they say:
2112: you find the country godforsaken;
2113: though we... don't shine in any way,
2114: our joy in you is warmly taken.
2115: ``Why did you visit us, but why?
2116: Lost in our backwoods habitation
2117: I'd not have known you, therefore I
2118: would have been spared this laceration.
2119: In time, who knows, the agitation
2120: of inexperience would have passed,
2121: I would have found a friend, another,
2122: and in the role of virtuous mother
2123: and faithful wife I'd have been cast.
2124: {100}
2125: ``Another!... No, another never
2126: in all the world could take my heart!
2127: Decreed in highest court for ever...
2128: heaven's will -- for you I'm set apart;
2129: and my whole life has been directed
2130: and pledged to you, and firmly planned:
2131: I know, Godsent one, I'm protected
2132: until the grave by your strong hand:
2133: you'd made appearance in my dreaming;
2134: unseen, already you were dear,
2135: my soul had heard your voice ring clear,
2136: stirred at your gaze, so strange, so gleaming,
2137: long, long ago... no, that could be
2138: no dream. You'd scarce arrived, I reckoned
2139: to know you, swooned, and in a second
2140: all in a blaze, I said: it's he!
2141: ``You know, it's true, how I attended,
2142: drank in your words when all was still --
2143: helping the poor, or while I mended
2144: with balm of prayer my torn and rended
2145: spirit that anguish had made ill.
2146: At this midnight of my condition,
2147: was it not you, dear apparition,
2148: who in the dark came flashing through
2149: and, on my bed-head gently leaning,
2150: with love and comfort in your meaning,
2151: spoke words of hope? But who are you:
2152: the guardian angel of tradition,
2153: or some vile agent of perdition
2154: sent to seduce? Resolve my doubt.
2155: Oh, this could all be false and vain,
2156: a sham that trustful souls work out;
2157: {101}
2158: fate could be something else again..,
2159: ``So let it be! for you to keep
2160: I trust my fate to your direction,
2161: henceforth in front of you I weep,
2162: I weep, and pray for your protection..,
2163: Imagine it: quite on my own
2164: I've no one here who comprehends me,
2165: and now a swooning mind attends me,
2166: dumb I must perish, and alone.
2167: My heart awaits you: you can turn it
2168: to life and hope with just a glance --
2169: or else disturb my mournful trance
2170: with censure -- I've done all to earn it!
2171: ``I close. I dread to read this page...
2172: for shame and fear my wits are sliding...
2173: and yet your honour is my gage
2174: and in it boldly I'm confiding''...
2175: {102}
2176: XXXII
2177: Now Tanya's groaning, now she's sighing;
2178: the letter trembles in her grip;
2179: the rosy sealing-wafer's drying
2180: upon her feverish tongue; the slip
2181: from off her charming shoulder's drooping,
2182: and sideways her poor head is stooping.
2183: But now the radiance of the moon
2184: is dimmed. Down there the valley soon
2185: comes clearer through the mists of dawning.
2186: Down there, by slow degrees, the stream
2187: has taken on a silvery gleam;
2188: the herdsman's horn proclaimed the morning
2189: and roused the village long ago:
2190: to Tanya, all's an empty show.
2191: XXXIII
2192: She's paid the sunrise no attention,
2193: she sits with head sunk on her breast,
2194: over the note holds in suspension
2195: her seal with its engraven crest.
2196: Softly the door is opened, enter
2197: grey Filatevna, to present her
2198: with a small tray and a teacup.
2199: ``Get up, my child, it's time, get up!
2200: Why, pretty one, you're up already!
2201: My early bird! you know, last night
2202: you gave me such a shocking fright!
2203: but now, thank God, you're well and steady,
2204: your night of fretting's left no trace!
2205: fresh as a poppy-flower, your face.''
2206: {103}
2207: XXXIV
2208: ``Oh nurse, a favour, a petition...''
2209: ``Command me, darling, as you choose.''
2210: ``Now don't suppose... let no suspicion...
2211: but, nurse, you see... Oh, don't refuse...''
2212: ``My sweet, God warrants me your debtor.''
2213: ``Then send your grandson with this letter
2214: quickly to O... I mean to that...
2215: the neighbour... you must tell the brat
2216: that not a syllable be uttered
2217: and not a mention of my name...''
2218: ``Which neighbour, dear? My head became
2219: in these last years all mixed and fluttered.
2220: We've many neighbours round about;
2221: even to count them throws me out.''
2222: XXXV
2223: ``How slow you are at guessing, nyanya!''
2224: ``My sweet, my dearest heart, I'm old,
2225: I'm old, my mind is blunted, Tanya;
2226: times were when I was sharp and bold:
2227: times were, when master's least suggestion...''
2228: ``Oh nyanya, nyanya, I don't question...
2229: what have your wits to do with me?
2230: Now here's a letter, as you see,
2231: addressed to Onegin''... ...'Well, that's easy.
2232: But don't be cross, my darling friend,
2233: you know I'm hard to comprehend...
2234: Why have you gone all pale and queasy?''
2235: ``It's nothing, nurse, nothing, I say...
2236: just send your grandson on his way.''
2237: {104}
2238: XXXVI
2239: Hours pass; no answer; waiting, waiting.
2240: No word: another day goes by.
2241: She's dressed since dawn, dead pale; debating,
2242: demanding: when will he reply?
2243: Olga's adorer comes a-wooing.
2244: ``Tell me, what's your companion doing?''
2245: enquired the lady of the hall:
2246: ``it seems that he forgot us all.''
2247: Tatyana flushed, and started shaking.
2248: ``Today he promised he'd be here,''
2249: so Lensky answered the old dear:
2250: ``the mail explains the time he's taking.''
2251: Tatyana lowered her regard
2252: as at a censure that was hard.
2253: XXXVII
2254: Day faded; on the table, glowing,
2255: the samovar of evening boiled,
2256: and warmed the Chinese teapot; flowing
2257: beneath it, vapour wreathed and coiled.
2258: Already Olga's hand was gripping
2259: the urn of perfumed tea, and tipping
2260: into the cups its darkling stream --
2261: meanwhile a hallboy handed cream;
2262: before the window taking station,
2263: plunged in reflection's deepest train,
2264: Tatyana breathed on the cold pane,
2265: and in the misted condensation
2266: with charming forefinger she traced
2267: ``OE'' devotedly inlaced.
2268: {105}
2269: XXXVIII
2270: Meanwhile with pain her soul was girdled,
2271: and tears were drowning her regard.
2272: A sudden clatter!... blood was curdled...
2273: Now nearer... hooves... and in the yard
2274: Evgeny! ``Ah!'' Tatyana, fleeting
2275: light as a shadow, shuns a meeting,
2276: through the back porch runs out and flies
2277: down to the garden, and her eyes
2278: daren't look behind her; fairly dashing --
2279: beds, bridges, lawn, she never stops,
2280: the allée to the lake, the copse;
2281: breaking the lilac bushes, smashing
2282: parterres, she runs to rivulet's brink,
2283: to gasp, and on a bench to sink.
2284: XXXIX
2285: She dropped... ``It's he! Eugene arriving!
2286: Oh God, what did he think!'' A dream
2287: of hope is somehow still surviving
2288: in her torn heart -- a fickle gleam;
2289: she trembles, and with fever drumming
2290: awaits him -- hears nobody coming.
2291: Maidservants on the beds just now
2292: were picking berries from the bough,
2293: singing in chorus as directed
2294: (on orders which of course presume
2295: that thievish mouths cannot consume
2296: their masters' berries undetected
2297: so long as they're employed in song:
2298: such rustic cunning can't be wrong!) --
2299: {106}
2300: The Song of the Girls
2301: ``Maidens, pretty maidens all,
2302: dear companions, darling friends,
2303: pretty maidens, romp away,
2304: have your fill of revelry!
2305: Strike the ditty up, my sweets,
2306: ditty of our secret world,
2307: and entice a fellow in
2308: to the circle of our dance.
2309: When we draw a fellow in,
2310: when we see him from afar,
2311: darlings, then we'll run away,
2312: cherries then we'll throw at him,
2313: cherries throw and raspberries
2314: and redcurrants throw at him.
2315: Never come and overhear
2316: ditties of our secret world,
2317: never come and like a spy
2318: watch the games we maidens play.''
2319: {107}
2320: XL
2321: They sing; unmoved by their sweet-sounding
2322: choruses, Tanya can but wait,
2323: listless, impatient, for the pounding
2324: within her bosom to abate,
2325: and for her cheeks to cease their blushing;
2326: but wildly still her heart is rushing,
2327: and on her cheeks the fever stays,
2328: more and more brightly still they blaze.
2329: So the poor butterfly will quiver
2330: and beat a nacreous wing when caught
2331: by some perverse schoolboy for sport;
2332: and so in winter-fields will shiver
2333: the hare who from afar has seen
2334: a marksman crouching in the green.
2335: XLI
2336: But finally she heaved a yearning
2337: sigh, and stood up, began to pace;
2338: she walked, but just as she was turning
2339: into the allée, face to face,
2340: she found Evgeny, eyes a-glitter,
2341: still as a shadow, grim and bitter;
2342: seared as by fire, she stopped. Today
2343: I lack the strength required to say
2344: what came from this unlooked-for meeting;
2345: my friends, I need to pause a spell,
2346: and walk, and breathe, before I tell
2347: a story that still wants completing;
2348: I need to rest from all this rhyme:
2349: I'll end my tale some other time.
2350: {108}
2351: Notes to Chapter Three
2352: 1 Stanza left incomplete by Pushkin.
2353: 2 Heroine of Zhukovsky's poem of the same name.
2354: 3 Julie, ou la nouvelle Héloise. by Rousseau, 1761.
2355: 4 Hero of Mathilde, by Sophie Cottin, 1805.
2356: 5 Lover of Valérie, by Madame de Krudener, 1803.
2357: 6 Delphine, by Madame de Staël, 1805.
2358: 7 Melmoth the Wanderer, by C. R. Mathurin, 1820.
2359: 8 Jean Sbogar, by Charles Nodier, 1818.
2360: 9  ``Lasciate  ogni  speranza, voi ch'entrate.  Our modest  author  has
2361: translated only the first part of the famous verse.'' Pushkin's note.
2362: 10 Magazine (1818) edited by A. Izmaylov.
2363: 11 Russian poet and translator from the French.
2364: 12 French poet (1755-1814). Author of Poésies Erotiques.
2365: 13 Evgeny Baratynsky (1800-1844). Poet and friend of Pushkin.
2366: --------
2367: Chapter Four
2368: La morale est dans la nature des choses.
2369: Necker
2370: (I, II, III, IV, V, VI,1) VII
2371: With womankind, the less we love them,
2372: the easier they become to charm,
2373: the tighter we can stretch above them
2374: enticing nets to do them harm.
2375: There was a period when cold-blooded
2376: debauchery was praised, and studied
2377: as love's technique, when it would blare
2378: its own perfection everywhere,
2379: and heartless pleasure was up-graded;
2380: yes, these were our forefathers' ways,
2381: those monkeys of the good old days:
2382: now Lovelace's renown has faded
2383: as scarlet heels have lost their name
2384: and stately periwigs, their fame.
2385: {109}
2386: VIII
2387: How dull are acting and evasion,
2388: diversely urging the same plea,
2389: earnestly striving for persuasion
2390: on points that all long since agree --
2391: and always the self-same objection;
2392: how dull to work for the correction
2393: of prejudice that's never been
2394: harboured by maidens of thirteen!
2395: Who's not disgusted by cajoling,
2396: threats, vows, and simulated fears,
2397: by six-page letters, rings and tears,
2398: gossip, and tricks, and the patrolling
2399: of aunts and mothers, and the thrall
2400: of husband's friendship -- worst of all!
2401: IX
2402: Evgeny thought in just this fashion.
2403: From his first youth he'd known the force,
2404: the sufferings of tempestuous passion;
2405: its winds had blown him far off course.
2406: Spoilt by the habit of indulgence,
2407: now dazzled by one thing's effulgence,
2408: now disenchanted with the next,
2409: more and more bored by yearning's text,
2410: bored by success' giddy trifle,
2411: he heard in stillness and in din
2412: a deathless murmur from within,
2413: found that in laughter yawns could stifle:
2414: he killed eight years in such a style,
2415: and wasted life's fine flower meanwhile.
2416: {110}
2417: X
2418: Though belles had lost his adoration,
2419: he danced attendance with the best;
2420: rebuffed, found instant consolation;
2421: deceived, was overjoyed to rest.
2422: He followed them without illusion,
2423: lost them without regret's contusion,
2424: scarcely recalled their love, their spite;
2425: just like a casual guest who might
2426: devote to whist an evening party,
2427: who'd sit, and at the end of play
2428: would say goodbye and drive away,
2429: go off to sleep quite hale and hearty,
2430: and in the morning wouldn't know
2431: that self-same evening where he'd go.
2432: XI
2433: Yet Tanya's note made its impression
2434: on Eugene, he was deeply stirred:
2435: that virgin dream and its confession
2436: filled him with thoughts that swarmed and whirred;
2437: the flower-like pallor of the maiden,
2438: her look, so sweetly sorrow-laden,
2439: all plunged his soul deep in the stream
2440: of a delicious, guiltless dream...
2441: and though perhaps old fires were thrusting
2442: and held him briefly in their sway,
2443: Eugene had no wish to betray
2444: a soul so innocent, so trusting.
2445: But to the garden, to the scene
2446: where Tanya now confronts Eugene.
2447: {111}
2448: XII
2449: Moments of silence, quite unbroken;
2450: then, stepping nearer, Eugene said:
2451: ``You wrote to me, and nothing spoken
2452: can disavow that. I have read
2453: those words where love, without condition,
2454: pours out its guiltless frank admission,
2455: and your sincerity of thought
2456: is dear to me, for it has brought
2457: feeling to what had long been heartless:
2458: but I won't praise you -- let me join
2459: and pay my debt in the same coin
2460: with an avowal just as artless;
2461: hear my confession as I stand
2462: I leave the verdict in your hand.
2463: XIII
2464: ``Could I be happy circumscribing
2465: my life in a domestic plot;
2466: had fortune blest me by prescribing
2467: husband and father as my lot;
2468: could I accept for just a minute
2469: the homely scene, take pleasure in it --
2470: then I'd have looked for you alone
2471: to be the bride I'd call my own.
2472: Without romance, or false insistence,
2473: I'll say: with past ideals in view
2474: I would have chosen none but you
2475: as helpmeet in my sad existence,
2476: as gage of all things that were good,
2477: and been as happy... as I could!
2478: {112}
2479: XIV
2480: ``But I was simply not intended
2481: for happiness -- that alien role.
2482: Should your perfections be expended
2483: in vain on my unworthy soul?
2484: Believe (as conscience is my warrant),
2485: wedlock for us would be abhorrent.
2486: I'd love you, but inside a day,
2487: with custom, love would fade away;
2488: your tears would flow -- but your emotion,
2489: your grief would fail to touch my heart,
2490: they'd just enrage it with their dart.
2491: What sort of roses, in your notion,
2492: would Hymen bring us -- blooms that might
2493: last many a day, and many a night!
2494: XV
2495: ``What in the world is more distressing
2496: than households where the wife must moan
2497: the unworthy husband through depressing
2498: daytimes and evenings passed alone?
2499: and where the husband, recognizing
2500: her worth (but anathematising
2501: his destiny) without a smile
2502: bursts with cold envy and with bile?
2503: For such am I. When you were speaking
2504: to me so simply, with the fires
2505: and force that purity inspires,
2506: is this the man that you were seeking?
2507: can it be true you must await
2508: from cruel fortune such a fate?
2509: {113}
2510: XVI
2511: ``I've dreams and years past resurrection;
2512: a soul that nothing can renew...
2513: I feel a brotherly affection,
2514: or something tenderer still, for you.
2515: Listen to me without resentment:
2516: girls often change to their contentment
2517: light dreams for new ones... so we see
2518: each springtime, on the growing tree,
2519: fresh leaves... for such is heaven's mandate.
2520: You'll love again, but you must teach
2521: your heart some self-restraint; for each
2522: and every man won't understand it
2523: as I have... learn from my belief
2524: that inexperience leads to grief.''
2525: XVII
2526: So went his sermon. Almost dying,
2527: blinded to everything about
2528: by mist of tears, without replying
2529: Tatyana heard Evgeny out.
2530: He gave his arm. In sad abstraction,
2531: by what's called machinal reaction,
2532: without a word Tatyana leant
2533: upon it, and with head down-bent
2534: walked homeward round the kitchen garden;
2535: together they arrived, and none
2536: dreamt of reproving what they'd done:
2537: by country freedom, rightful pardon
2538: and happy licence are allowed,
2539: as much as in Moscow the proud.
2540: {114}
2541: XVIII
2542: Agree, the way Eugene proceeded
2543: with our poor girl was kind and good;
2544: not for the first time he succeeded
2545: in manifesting, as he could,
2546: a truly noble disposition;
2547: yet people's malice and suspicion
2548: persisted and made no amends.
2549: By enemies, no less by friends
2550: (it's all the same -- you well correct us),
2551: he found all kinds of brickbat hurled.
2552: We each have enemies in this world,
2553: but from our friends, good Lord protect us!
2554: Those friends, those friends! it is, I fear,
2555: with cause that I've recalled them here.
2556: XIX
2557: What of it? Nothing. I'm just sending
2558: to sleep some black and empty dreams;
2559: but, inside brackets, I'm contending
2560: there's no ignoble tale that seems
2561: cooked-up where garret-vermin babble,
2562: endorsed by fashionable rabble,
2563: there's no absurdity as such,
2564: no vulgar epigram too much,
2565: which smilingly your friend, supported
2566: by decent company, has not,
2567: without a trace of spite or plot,
2568: a hundred times afresh distorted;
2569: yet he'd back you through thick and thin:
2570: he loves you... like your kith and kin!
2571: {115}
2572: XX
2573: Hm, hm. Distinguished reader, tell me
2574: how are your kith and kin today?
2575: And here my sentiments impel me
2576: for your enlightenment to say
2577: how I interpret this expression:
2578: our kin are folk whom by profession
2579: we have to cherish and admire
2580: with all our hearts, and who require
2581: that in the usual Christmas scrimmage
2582: we visit them, or without fail
2583: send them good wishes through the mail
2584: to ensure that till next time our image
2585: won't even cross their minds by stealth...
2586: God grant them years and years of health!
2587: XXI
2588: Of course, the love of tender beauties,
2589: surer than friendship or than kin,
2590: will loyally discharge its duties,
2591: in midst of trouble, storm or din.
2592: Of course. Yet fashion's wild rotation,
2593: yet a capricious inclination,
2594: yet floods of talk around the town...
2595: the darling sex is light as down.
2596: Then verdicts from her husband's quartet
2597: are bound, by every virtuous wife,
2598: to be respected all through life:
2599: and so your faithfullest supporter
2600: will disappear as fast as smoke:
2601: for Satan, love's a splendid joke.
2602: {116}
2603: XXII
2604: Whom then to credit? Whom to treasure?
2605: On whom alone can we depend?
2606: Who is there who will truly measure
2607: his acts and words to suit our end?
2608: Who'll sow no calumnies around us?
2609: Whose fond attentions will astound us?
2610: Who'll never fault our vices, or
2611: whom shall we never find a bore?
2612: Don't let a ghost be your bear-leader,
2613: don't waste your efforts on the air.
2614: Just let yourself be your whole care,
2615: your loved one, honourable reader!
2616: Deserving object: there can be
2617: nothing more lovable than he.
2618: XXIII
2619: Then what resulted from the meeting?
2620: Alas, it's not so hard to guess!
2621: Love's frantic torments went on beating
2622: and racking with their strain and stress
2623: that youthful soul, which pined for sadness;
2624: no, all devoured by passion's madness
2625: poor Tanya more intensely burns;
2626: sleep runs from her, she turns and turns...
2627: and health, life's sweetness and its shimmer,
2628: smiles, and a maiden's tranquil poise,
2629: have vanished, like an empty noise,
2630: while dear Tatyana's youth grows dimmer:
2631: so a storm-shadow wraps away
2632: in dark attire the new-born day.
2633: {117}
2634: XXIV
2635: Poor Tanya's bloom begins to languish,
2636: and pale, and fade without a word!
2637: there's nothing can employ her anguish,
2638: no sound by which her soul is stirred.
2639: Neighbours in whispered tones are taking
2640: council, and with profound head-shaking
2641: conclude that it's high time she wed!...
2642: But that's enough. At once, in stead,
2643: I'll gladden your imagination,
2644: reader, by painting you a scene
2645: of happy love. For I have been
2646: too long, against my inclination,
2647: held in constraint by pity's touch:
2648: I love my Tatyana too much!
2649: XXV
2650: From hour to hour a surer capture
2651: for Olga's beauty, Lensky gives
2652: his soul to a delicious rapture
2653: that fills him and in which he lives.
2654: He's always with her: either seated
2655: in darkness in her room, or treated
2656: to garden walks, as arm in arm
2657: they while away the morning's calm.
2658: What else? Quite drunk with love's illusion,
2659: he even dares, once in a while,
2660: emboldened by his Olga's smile,
2661: and plunged in tender shame's confusion,
2662: to play with a dishevelled tress,
2663: or kiss the border of her dress.
2664: {118}
2665: XXVI
2666: He reads to Olga on occasion,
2667: for her improvement, a roman,
2668: of moralistical persuasion,
2669: more searching than Chateaubriand;
2670: but in it there are certain pages
2671: (vain twaddle, fables of the ages,
2672: talk that might turn a young girl's head)
2673: which with a blush he leaves unread.
2674: As far removed as they were able
2675: from all the world, they sat and pored
2676: in deepest thought at the chess-board
2677: for hours, with elbows on the table --
2678: then Lensky moved his pawn, and took,
2679: deep in distraction, his own rook.
2680: XXVII
2681: Even at home his occupation
2682: is only Olga: he relieves
2683: with careful schemes of decoration
2684: an album's loose and floating sheaves.
2685: Sometimes a landscape's represented,
2686: a tomb, a Cyprian shrine's invented,
2687: a lyre, and on it perched, a dove --
2688: in ink with colour-wash above;
2689: then on the leaves of recollection,
2690: below the others who have signed
2691: he leaves a tender verse behind,
2692: a dream's mute monument, reflection
2693: of instant thoughts, a fleeting trace
2694: still after many years in place.
2695: {119}
2696: XXVIII
2697: Often of course you'll have inspected
2698: the album of a country miss
2699: where scribbling friends have interjected
2700: frontwise and back, that way and this.
2701: With spelling scrambled to perdition,
2702: the unmetric verses of tradition
2703: are entered here, in friendship's gage,
2704: shortened, or lengthened off the page.
2705: On the first sheet you'll find a question:
2706: ``Qu'écrirez-vous sur ces tablettes?''
2707: and, under, ``toute à vous Annette'';
2708: then, on the last page, the suggestion:
2709: ``who loves you more than I, let's see
2710: him prove it, writing after me.''
2711: XXIX
2712: There you're entirely sure of finding
2713: two hearts, a torch, and a nosegay;
2714: and there, love's protestations, binding
2715: until the tombstone; there one day
2716: some regimental bard has added
2717: a stanza villainously padded.
2718: In such an album, friends, I too
2719: am always glad to write, it's true,
2720: convinced at heart that my most zealous
2721: nonsense will earn indulgent looks,
2722: nor will my scribbling in such books
2723: attract the sneering of the jealous,
2724: or make men seriously discuss
2725: if I show wit in jesting thus.
2726: {120}
2727: XXX
2728: But you, grand tomes I loathe with passion,
2729: odd volumes from the devil's shelf,
2730: in which the rhymester-man-of-fashion
2731: is forced to crucify himself,
2732: portfolios nobly illustrated
2733: with Tolstoy's2 brush, or decorated
2734: by Baratynsky's3 wondrous pen,
2735: God's thunder burn you up! And when
2736: some splendid lady is referring
2737: to me her best in-quarto tome,
2738: the fear and rage with which I foam!
2739: Deep down, an epigram is stirring
2740: that I'm just longing to indite --
2741: but madrigals I've got to write!
2742: XXXI
2743: No madrigals were for inscribing
2744: by Lensky in his Olga's book;
2745: his style breathed love, and not the gibing
2746: coldness of wit; each note he took,
2747: each news of her he'd been imbibing --
2748: all was material for transcribing:
2749: with lively and pellucid look,
2750: his elegies flow like a brook.
2751: So you, inspired Yazýkov,4 sobbing
2752: with bursts of passion from the heart,
2753: sing God knows whom, compose with art
2754: a suite of elegies that, throbbing,
2755: sooner or later will relate
2756: the entire story of your fate.
2757: {121}
2758: XXXII
2759: But soft! You hear? A scowling critic,
2760: bidding us to reject for good
2761: the elegy, grown paralytic,
2762: commands our rhymester-brotherhood:
2763: ``oh, quit your stale, your tedious quacking,
2764: and your alas-ing and alack-ing
2765: about what's buried in the past:
2766: sing about something else at last!''
2767: All right, you want the resurrection
2768: of trumpet, dagger, mask and sword,
2769: and dead ideas from that old hoard,
2770: all brought to life at your direction.
2771: Not so? ``No, sirs, the ode's the thing,
2772: that's the refrain that you should sing,
2773: XXXIII
2774: ``as sung of old, in years of glory,
2775: as instituted long ago.''
2776: Only the ode, that solemn story!
2777: Enough, my friends; it's all so-so.
2778: Remember the retort satiric!
2779: Is Others' View,5 that clever lyric,
2780: really more bearable to you
2781: than what our sorrowing rhymesters do?
2782: ``The elegy's just vain protesting,
2783: empty the purpose it proclaims,
2784: while odes have high and noble aims...''
2785: That point I wouldn't mind contesting,
2786: but hold my tongue, lest it appears
2787: I'll set two ages by the ears.
2788: {122}
2789: XXXIV
2790: In love with fame, by freedom smitten,
2791: with storm and tumult in his head,
2792: what odes Vladimir might have written --
2793: but Olga would have never read!
2794: Bards of our tearful generation,
2795: have you read lines of your creation
2796: to your loved ones? They do maintain
2797: that this of all things for a swain
2798: is the supreme reward. Precisely,
2799: blest the poor lover who reads out
2800: his dreams, while she whom they're about,
2801: that languid beauty, listens nicely --
2802: blest... though perhaps her fancy's caught
2803: in fact by some quite different thought.
2804: XXXV
2805: But I myself read my bedizened
2806: fancies, my rhythmic search for truth,
2807: to nobody except a wizened
2808: nanny, companion of my youth;
2809: or, after some dull dinner's labour,
2810: I buttonhole a wandering neighbour
2811: and in a corner make him choke
2812: on tragedy; but it's no joke,
2813: when, utterly worn out by rhyming,
2814: exhausted and done up, I take
2815: a rambling walk beside my lake,
2816: and duck get up; with instant timing,
2817: alarmed by my melodious lay,
2818: they leave their shores and fly away.
2819: {123}
2820: XXXVI6
2821: < My gaze pursues them... but on station
2822: the hunter in the wood will swear
2823: at verse, and hiss an imprecation,
2824: and ease his catch with all due care.
2825: We each enjoy a special hobby,
2826: each of us has his favourite lobby:
2827: one sees a duck and aims his gun,
2828: one raves in verse like me, and one
2829: hunts cheeky flies, with swatter sweeping,
2830: one leads the multitude in thought,
2831: one finds in war amusing sport,
2832: one wallows in delicious weeping;
2833: the wine-addict adores the cup:
2834: and good and bad are all mixed up. >
2835: XXXVII
2836: But what about Eugene? With reason
2837: reader, you ask, and I'll expound --
2838: craving your tolerance in season --
2839: the programme of his daily round.
2840: In summertime -- for he was leading
2841: a hermit's life -- he'd be proceeding
2842: on foot, by seven o'clock, until
2843: he reached the stream below the hill;
2844: lightly attired, like the creator
2845: of Gulnare, he would play a card
2846: out of the hand of that same bard:
2847: he'd swim this Hellespont; then later
2848: he'd drink his coffee, flutter through
2849: the pages of some dull review,
2850: then dress...
2851: {124}
2852: (XXXVIII) XXXIX
2853: Books, riding, walks, sleep heavy-laden,
2854: the shady wood, the talking stream;
2855: sometimes from a fair, black-eyed maiden
2856: the kiss where youth and freshness gleam;
2857: a steed responsive to the bridle,
2858: and dinner with a touch of idle
2859: fancy, a wine serene in mood,
2860: tranquillity, and solitude --
2861: Onegin's life, you see, was holy;
2862: unconsciously he let it mount
2863: its grip on him, forgot to count
2864: bright summer days that passed so slowly,
2865: forgot to think of town and friends
2866: and tedious means to festive ends.
2867: XL
2868: Our evanescent northern summer
2869: parodies winter in the south;
2870: it's like a vanishing newcomer --
2871: but here we must control our mouth.
2872: The sky breathed autumn, time was flowing,
2873: and good old sun more seldom glowing;
2874: the days grew shorter, in the glade
2875: with mournful sound the secret shade
2876: was stripped away, and mists encroaching
2877: lay on the fields; in caravan
2878: the clamorous honking geese began
2879: their southward flight: one saw approaching
2880: the season which is such a bore --
2881: November stood outside the door.
2882: {125}
2883: XLI
2884: Dawn comes in mist and chill; no longer
2885: do fields echo with work and shout;
2886: in pairs, their hunger driving stronger,
2887: on the highroad the wolves come out;
2888: the horse gets wind of them and, snorting,
2889: sets the wise traveller cavorting
2890: up the hillside at breakneck pace;
2891: no longer does the herdsman chase
2892: his beasts outdoors at dawn, nor ringing
2893: at noontime does his horn resound
2894: as it assembles them around;
2895: while in the hut a girl is singing;
2896: she spins and, friend of winter nights,
2897: the matchwood chatters as it lights.
2898: XLII
2899: Hoar-frost that crackles with a will is
2900: already silvering all the plain...
2901: (the reader thinks the rhyme is lilies:
2902: here, seize it quick for this quatrain!)
2903: Like modish parquetry, the river
2904: glitters beneath its icing-sliver;
2905: boy-tribes with skates on loudly slice
2906: their joyous way across the ice;
2907: a red-foot goose, weight something fearful,
2908: anticipates a swim, in stead
2909: tries out the ice with cautious tread,
2910: and skids and tumbles down; the cheerful
2911: first flakes of snow whirl round and sink
2912: in stars upon the river-brink.
2913: {126}
2914: XLIII
2915: In backwoods, how d'you pass this season?
2916: Walking? The country that you roam
2917: is a compulsive bore by reason
2918: of its unvarnished monochrome.
2919: Riding on the lugubrious prairie?
2920: Your horse, blunt-shoed and all unwary,
2921: will find the ice elude his grip
2922: and, any moment, down he'll slip.
2923: Or, in your lonely homestead, moping,
2924: you'll read: here's Pradt,7 here's Walter Scott!
2925: to pass the evening. No? then tot
2926: up your accounts, and raging, toping,
2927: let evening pass, tomorrow too --
2928: in triumph you'll see winter through!
2929: XLIV
2930: Childe-Harold-like, Eugene's devoting
2931: his hours to dreaming them away:
2932: he wakes; a bath where ice is floating;
2933: and then, indoors the livelong day,
2934: alone, and sunk in calculation,
2935: with a blunt cue for the duration,
2936: from early morning on he will
2937: at two-ball billiards prove his skill;
2938: then, country evening fast arriving,
2939: billiards are dropped, cue put to bed:
2940: before the fire a table's spread;
2941: Evgeny waits: and here comes driving,
2942: with three roan horses in a line
2943: Vladimir Lensky. Quick, let's dine!
2944: {127}
2945: XLV
2946: From widow Clicquot and from Moët,
2947: the draught whose blessings are agreed,
2948: in frosted bottle, for the poet
2949: is brought to table at full speed.
2950: Bubbles like Hippocrene are spraying;
2951: once, with its foaming and its playing,
2952: (a simile of this and that)
2953: it held me captive; tit for tat,
2954: friends, recollect how I surrendered
2955: my last poor lepton for a sup!
2956: recall, by its bewitching cup,
2957: how many follies were engendered;
2958: how many lines of verse, and themes
2959: for jokes, and rows, and merry dreams!
2960: XLVI
2961: Yet hissing froth deals a malicious,
2962: perfidious blow to my inside,
2963: and now it's Bordeaux the Judicious
2964: that I prefer to Champagne's tide;
2965: to Aÿ's vintage in the sequel
2966: I find myself no longer equal;
2967: for, mistress-like, it's brilliant, vain,
2968: lively, capricious, and inane...
2969: But in misfortune or displeasure,
2970: Bordeaux, you're like a faithful friend,
2971: a true companion to the end,
2972: ready to share our quiet leisure
2973: with your good offices, and so
2974: long life to our dear friend, Bordeaux!
2975: {128}
2976: XLVII
2977: The fire was dying; cinders faintly
2978: covered the golden coal -- the steam
2979: tumbled and whirled and twisted quaintly
2980: its barely noticeable stream.
2981: The hearth was low beyond all stoking.
2982: Straight up the chimney, pipes were smoking.
2983: Still on the board, the beakers hissed,
2984: and evening now drew on in mist...
2985: (I like a friendly conversation,
2986: the enjoyment of a friendly drink,
2987: at hours, which, why I cannot think,
2988: somehow have got the designation
2989: of time between the wolf and dog.)
2990: Now hear the friends in dialogue:
2991: XLVIII
2992: ``Tell me, our neighbours, are they thriving?
2993: and how's Tatyana? Olga too,
2994: your dashing one, is she surviving?''
2995: ``Just half a glass more... that will do...
2996: All flourishing; they send their duty.
2997: Take Olga's shoulders now -- the beauty!
2998: What breasts! What soul!... We'll go one day
2999: visit the family, what d'you say?
3000: if you come with me, they'll be flattered;
3001: or else, my friend, how does it look?
3002: you called there twice, and since then took
3003: no notice of them. But I've chattered
3004: so much, I'm left no time to speak!
3005: of course! you're bidden there next week.''
3006: {129}
3007: XLIX
3008: ``I?'' ``Saturday. The invitation
3009: Olinka and her mother sent:
3010: Tatyana's name day celebration.
3011: It's right and proper that you went.''
3012: ``But there'll be such a rout and scrabble
3013: with every different kind of rabble...''
3014: ``No, no, I'm sure the party's small.
3015: Relations. No-one else at all.
3016: Let's go, our friendship's worth the labour!''
3017: ``All right, I'll come then...'' ``What a friend!''
3018: He drained his glass down to the end
3019: by way of toast to their fair neighbour;
3020: then he began to talk once more
3021: of Olga: love's that kind of bore!
3022: L
3023: Lensky rejoiced. His designated
3024: rapture was just two weeks ahead;
3025: love's crown, delectable, awaited
3026: his transports, and the marriage-bed
3027: in all its mystery. Hymen's teasing,
3028: the pain, the grief, the marrow-freezing
3029: onset of the incipient yawn,
3030: were from his vision quite withdrawn.
3031: While under the connubial banner
3032: I can see naught, as Hymen's foe,
3033: beyond a string of dull tableaux,
3034: a novel in Lafontaine's8 manner...
3035: my wretched Lensky in his heart
3036: was just created for the part.
3037: {130}
3038: LI
3039: And he was loved... at least he never
3040: doubted of it, so lived in bliss.
3041: Happy a hundredfold, whoever
3042: can lean on faith, who can dismiss
3043: cold reason, sleep in sensual welter
3044: like a drunk traveller in a shelter,
3045: or, sweeter, like a butterfly
3046: in flowers of spring it's drinking dry:
3047: but piteous he, the all-foreseeing,
3048: the sober head, detesting each
3049: human reaction, every speech
3050: in the expression of its being,
3051: whose heart experience has cooled
3052: and saved from being charmed or fooled!
3053: {131}
3054: Notes to Chapter Four
3055: 1 Stanzas I to VI were discarded by Pushkin.
3056: 2 Count F. P. Tolstoy (1783-1873), well-known artist.
3057: 3 See Chapter Three, note 13.
3058: 4 Poet and acquaintance of Pushkin.
3059: 5 Satiric poem by Ivan Dimitriev, 1795. The reference is -- summarizing
3060: very briefly -- to a  controversy between different literary  cliques  about
3061: the relative merits of the classic ode and the romantic elegy.
3062: 6 Stanza discarded by Pushkin, also stanza XXXVIII.
3063: 7 Dominique de Pradt (1759-1837), voluminous French political writer.
3064: 8 August Lafontaine (1758-1851), German novelist of family life.
3065: --------
3066: Chapter Five
3067: O, never know these frightful dreams,
3068: thou, my Svetlana!
3069: Zhukovsky
3070: I
3071: That year the season was belated
3072: and autumn lingered, long and slow;
3073: expecting winter, nature waited --
3074: only in January the snow,
3075: night of the second, started flaking.
3076: Next day Tatyana, early waking,
3077: saw through the window, morning-bright,
3078: roofs, flowerbeds, fences, all in white,
3079: panes patterned by the finest printer,
3080: with trees decked in their silvery kit,
3081: and jolly magpies on the flit,
3082: and hills that delicately winter
3083: had with its brilliant mantle crowned --
3084: and glittering whiteness all around.
3085: {132}
3086: II
3087: Winter!... The countryman, enchanted,
3088: breaks a new passage with his sleigh;
3089: his nag has smelt the snow, and planted
3090: a shambling hoof along the way;
3091: a saucy kibítka is slicing
3092: its furrow through the powdery icing;
3093: the driver sits and cuts a dash
3094: in sheepskin coat with scarlet sash.
3095: Here comes the yard-boy, who has chosen
3096: his pup to grace the sledge, while he
3097: becomes a horse for all to see;
3098: the rogue has got a finger frozen:
3099: it hurts, he laughs, and all in vain
3100: his mother taps the window-pane.
3101: III
3102: But you perhaps find no attraction
3103: in any picture of this kind:
3104: for nature's unadorned reaction
3105: has something low and unrefined.
3106: Fired by the god of inspiration,
3107: another bard1 in exaltation
3108: has painted for us the first snow
3109: with each nuance of wintry glow:
3110: he'll charm you with his fine invention,
3111: he'll take you prisoner, you'll admire
3112: secret sledge-rides in verse of fire;
3113: but I've not got the least intention
3114: just now of wrestling with his shade,
3115: nor his,2 who sings of Finland's maid.
3116: {133}
3117: IV
3118: Tanya (profoundly Russian being,
3119: herself not knowing how or why)
3120: in Russian winters thrilled at seeing
3121: the cold perfection of the sky,
3122: hoar-frost and sun in freezing weather,
3123: sledges, and tardy dawns together
3124: with the pink glow the snows assume
3125: and festal evenings in the gloom.
3126: The Larins kept the old tradition:
3127: maid-servants from the whole estate
3128: would on those evenings guess the fate
3129: of the two girls; their premonition
3130: pointed each year, for time to come,
3131: at soldier-husbands, and the drum.
3132: V
3133: Tatyana shared with full conviction
3134: the simple faith of olden days
3135: in dreams and cards and their prediction,
3136: and portents of the lunar phase.
3137: Omens dismayed her with their presage;
3138: each object held a secret message
3139: for her instruction, and her breast
3140: was by forebodings much oppressed.
3141: The tomcat, mannered and affected,
3142: that sat above the stove and purred
3143: and washed its face, to her brought word
3144: that visitors must be expected.
3145: If suddenly aloft she spied
3146: the new moon, horned, on her left side,
3147: {134}
3148: VI
3149: her face would pale, she'd start to quiver.
3150: In the dark sky, a shooting star
3151: that fell, and then began to shiver,
3152: would fill Tatyana from afar
3153: with perturbation and with worry;
3154: and while the star still flew, she'd hurry
3155: to whisper it her inmost prayer.
3156: And if she happened anywhere
3157: to meet a black monk, or if crossing
3158: her path a hare in headlong flight
3159: ran through the fields, sheer panic fright
3160: would leave her dithering and tossing.
3161: By dire presentiment awestruck,
3162: already she'd assume ill-luck.
3163: VII
3164: Yet -- fear itself she found presented
3165: a hidden beauty in the end:
3166: our disposition being invented
3167: by nature, contradiction's friend.
3168: Christmas came on. What joy, what gladness!
3169: Yes, youth divines, in giddy madness,
3170: youth which has nothing to regret,
3171: before which life's horizon yet
3172: lies bright, and vast beyond perceiving;
3173: spectacled age divines as well,
3174: although it's nearly heard the knell,
3175: and all is lost beyond retrieving;
3176: no matter: hope, in child's disguise,
3177: is there to lisp its pack of lies.
3178: {135}
3179: VIII
3180: Tatyana looks with pulses racing
3181: at sunken wax inside a bowl:
3182: beyond a doubt, its wondrous tracing
3183: foretells for her some wondrous role;
3184: from dish of water, rings are shifted
3185: in due succession; hers is lifted
3186: and at the very self-same time
3187: the girls sing out the ancient rhyme:
3188: ``The peasants there have wealth abounding,
3189: they heap up silver with a spade;
3190: and those we sing for will be paid
3191: in goods and fame!'' But the sad-sounding
3192: ditty portends a loss; more dear
3193: is ``Kit''3 to every maiden's ear.
3194: IX
3195: The sky is clear, the earth is frozen;
3196: the heavenly lights in glorious quire
3197: tread the calm, settled path they've chosen...
3198: Tatyana in low-cut attire
3199: goes out into the courtyard spaces
3200: and trains a mirror till it faces
3201: the moon; but in the darkened glass
3202: the only face to shake and pass
3203: is sad old moon's... Hark! snow is creaking...
3204: a passer-by; and on tiptoe
3205: she flies as fast as she can go;
3206: and ``what's your name?'' she asks him, speaking
3207: in a melodious, flute-like tone.
3208: He looks, and answers: ``Agafon.''4
3209: {136}
3210: X
3211: Prepared for prophecy and fable,
3212: she did what nurse advised she do
3213: and in the bath-house had a table
3214: that night, in secret, set for two;
3215: then sudden fear attacked Tatyana...
3216: I too -- when I recall Svetlana5
3217: I'm terrified -- so let it be...
3218: Tatyana's rites are not for me.
3219: She's dropped her sash's silken billow;
3220: Tanya's undressed, and lies in bed.
3221: Lel6 floats about above her head;
3222: and underneath her downy pillow
3223: a young girl's looking-glass is kept.
3224: Now all was still. Tatyana slept.
3225: XI
3226: She dreamt of portents. In her dreaming
3227: she walked across a snowy plain
3228: through gloom and mist; and there came streaming
3229: a furious, boiling, heaving main
3230: across the drift-encumbered acres,
3231: a raging torrent, capped with breakers,
3232: a flood on which no frosty band
3233: had been imposed by winter's hand;
3234: two poles that ice had glued like plaster
3235: were placed across the gulf to make
3236: a flimsy bridge whose every quake
3237: spelt hazard, ruin and disaster;
3238: she stopped at the loud torrent's bound,
3239: perplexed... and rooted to the ground.
3240: {137}
3241: XII
3242: As if before some mournful parting
3243: Tatyana groaned above the tide;
3244: she saw no friendly figure starting
3245: to help her from the other side;
3246: but suddenly a snowdrift rumbled,
3247: and what came out? a hairy, tumbled,
3248: enormous bear; Tatyana yelled,
3249: the bear let out a roar, and held
3250: a sharp-nailed paw towards her; bracing
3251: her nerves, she leant on it her weight,
3252: and with a halting, trembling gait
3253: above the water started tracing
3254: her way; she passed, then as she walked
3255: the bear -- what next? -- behind her stalked.
3256: XIII
3257: A backward look is fraught with danger;
3258: she speeds her footsteps to a race,
3259: but from her shaggy-liveried ranger
3260: she can't escape at any pace --
3261: the odious bear still grunts and lumbers.
3262: Ahead of them a pinewood slumbers
3263: in the full beauty of its frown;
3264: the branches all are weighted down
3265: with tufts of snow; and through the lifted
3266: summits of aspen, birch and lime,
3267: the nightly luminaries climb.
3268: No path to see: the snow has drifted
3269: across each bush, across each steep,
3270: and all the world is buried deep.
3271: {138}
3272: XIV
3273: She's in the wood, the bear still trails her.
3274: There's powdery snow up to her knees;
3275: now a protruding branch assails her
3276: and clasps her neck; and now she sees
3277: her golden earrings off and whipping;
3278: and now the crunchy snow is stripping
3279: her darling foot of its wet shoe,
3280: her handkerchief has fallen too;
3281: no time to pick it up -- she's dying
3282: with fright, she hears the approaching bear;
3283: her fingers shake, she doesn't dare
3284: to lift her skirt up; still she's flying,
3285: and he pursuing, till at length
3286: she flies no more, she's lost her strength.
3287: XV
3288: She's fallen in the snow -- alertly
3289: the bear has raised her in his paws;
3290: and she, submissively, inertly --
3291: no move she makes, no breath she draws;
3292: he whirls her through the wood... a hovel
3293: shows up through trees, all of a grovel
3294: in darkest forest depths and drowned
3295: by dreary snowdrifts piled around;
3296: there's a small window shining in it,
3297: and from within come noise and cheer;
3298: the bear explains: ``my cousin's here --
3299: come in and warm yourself a minute!''
3300: he carries her inside the door
3301: and sets her gently on the floor.
3302: {139}
3303: XVI
3304: Tatyana looks, her faintness passes:
3305: bear's gone; a hallway, no mistake;
3306: behind the door the clash of glasses
3307: and shouts suggest a crowded wake;
3308: so, seeing there no rhyme or reason,
3309: no meaning in or out of season,
3310: she peers discreetly through a chink
3311: and sees... whatever do you think?
3312: a group of monsters round a table,
3313: a dog with horns, a goatee'd witch,
3314: a rooster head, and on the twitch
3315: a skeleton jerked by a cable,
3316: a dwarf with tail, and a half-strain,
3317: a hybrid cross of cat and crane.
3318: XVII
3319: But ever stranger and more fearful:
3320: a crayfish rides on spider-back;
3321: on goose's neck, a skull looks cheerful
3322: and swaggers in a red calpack;
3323: with bended knees a windmill dances,
3324: its sails go flap-flap as it prances;
3325: song, laughter, whistle, bark and champ,
3326: and human words, and horse's stamp!
3327: But how she jumped, when in this hovel
3328: among the guests she recognized
3329: the man she feared and idolized --
3330: who else? -- the hero of our novel!
3331: Onegin sits at table too,
3332: he eyes the door, looks slyly through.
3333: {140}
3334: XVIII
3335: He nods -- they start to fuss and truckle;
3336: he drinks -- all shout and take a swill;
3337: he laughs -- they all begin to chuckle;
3338: he scowls -- and the whole gang are still;
3339: he's host, that's obvious. Thus enlightened
3340: Tanya's no longer quite so frightened
3341: and, curious now about the lot,
3342: opens the door a tiny slot...
3343: but then a sudden breeze surprises,
3344: puts out the lamps; the whole brigade
3345: of house-familiars stands dismayed...
3346: with eyes aflame Onegin rises
3347: from table, clattering on the floor;
3348: all stand. He walks towards the door.
3349: XIX
3350: Now she's alarmed; in desperate worry
3351: Tatyana struggles to run out --
3352: she can't; and in her panic hurry
3353: she flails around, she tries to shout --
3354: she can't; Evgeny's pushed the portal,
3355: and to the vision of those mortal
3356: monsters the maiden stood revealed.
3357: Wildly the fearful laughter pealed;
3358: the eyes of all, the hooves, the snozzles,
3359: the bleeding tongues, the tufted tails,
3360: the tusks, the corpse's finger-nails,
3361: the horns, and the moustachio'd nozzles --
3362: all point at her, and all combine
3363: to bellow out: ``she's mine, she's mine.''
3364: {141}
3365: XX
3366: ``She's mine!'' Evgeny's voice of thunder
3367: clears in a flash the freezing room;
3368: the whole thieves' kitchen flies asunder,
3369: the girl remains there in the gloom
3370: alone with him; Onegin takes her
3371: into a corner, gently makes her
3372: sit on a flimsy bench, and lays
3373: his head upon her shoulder... blaze
3374: of sudden brightness... it's too curious...
3375: Olga's appeared upon the scene,
3376: and Lensky follows her... Eugene,
3377: eyes rolling, arms uplifted, furious,
3378: damns the intruders; Tanya lies
3379: and almost swoons, and almost dies.
3380: XXI
3381: Louder and louder sounds the wrangle:
3382: Eugene has caught up, quick as quick,
3383: a carving-knife -- and in the tangle
3384: Lensky's thrown down. The murk is thick
3385: and growing thicker; then, heart-shaking,
3386: a scream rings out... the cabin's quaking...
3387: Tanya comes to in utter fright...
3388: she looks, the room is getting light --
3389: outside, the scarlet rays of dawning
3390: play on the window's frosted lace;
3391: in through the door, at swallow's pace,
3392: pinker than glow of Northern morning,
3393: flits Olga: ``now, tell me straight out,
3394: who was it that you dreamt about?''
3395: {142}
3396: XXII
3397: Deaf to her sister's intervention,
3398: Tatyana simply lay in bed,
3399: devoured a book with rapt attention,
3400: and kept quite silent while she read.
3401: The book displayed, not so you'd know it,
3402: no magic fancies of the poet,
3403: no brilliant truth, no vivid scene;
3404: and yet by Vergil or Racine
3405: by Scott, by Seneca, or Byron,
3406: even by Ladies' Fashion Post,
3407: no one was ever so engrossed:
3408: Martin Zadéka was the siren,
3409: dean of Chaldea's learned team,
3410: arch-commentator of the dream.
3411: XXIII
3412: This work of the profoundest learning
3413: was brought there by a huckster who
3414: one day came down that lonely turning,
3415: and to Tanya, when he was through,
3416: swapped it for odd tomes of Malvina,
3417: but just to make the bargain keener,
3418: he charged three roubles and a half,
3419: and took two Petriads in calf,
3420: a grammar, a digest of fable,
3421: and volume three of Marmontel.
3422: Since then Martin Zadéka's spell
3423: bewitches Tanya... he is able
3424: to comfort her in all her woes,
3425: and every night shares her repose.
3426: {143}
3427: XXIV
3428: Tatyana's haunted by her vision,
3429: plagued by her ghastly dream, and tries
3430: to puzzle out with some precision
3431: just what the nightmare signifies.
3432: Searching the table exegetic
3433: she finds, in order alphabetic:
3434: bear, blackness, blizzard, bridge and crow,
3435: fir, forest, hedgehog, raven, snow
3436: etcetera. But her trepidation
3437: Martin Zadéka fails to mend;
3438: the horrid nightmare must portend
3439: a hideous deal of tribulation.
3440: For several days she peaked and pined
3441: in deep anxiety of mind.
3442: XXV
3443: But now Aurora's crimson fingers
3444: from daybreak valleys lift the sun;
3445: the morning light no longer lingers,
3446: the festal name day has begun.
3447: Since dawn, whole families have been driving
3448: towards the Larins' and arriving
3449: in sledded coaches and coupés,
3450: in britzkas, kibítkas and sleighs.
3451: The hall is full of noise and hustle,
3452: in the salon new faces meet,
3453: and kisses smack as young girls greet;
3454: there's yap of pugs, and laughs, and bustle;
3455: the threshold's thronged, wet-nurses call,
3456: guests bow, feet scrape, and children squall.
3457: {144}
3458: XXVI
3459: Here with his wife, that bulging charmer,
3460: fat Pústyakov has driven in;
3461: Gvozdín, exemplary farmer,
3462: whose serfs are miserably thin;
3463: and the Skotínins, grizzled sages,
3464: with broods of children of all ages,
3465: from thirty down to two; and stop,
3466: here's Petushkóv, the local fop;
3467: and look, my cousin's come, Buyánov,
3468: in a peaked cap, all dust and fluff, --
3469: you'll recognize him soon enough, --
3470: and counsellor (retired) Flyánov,
3471: that rogue, backbiter, pantaloon,
3472: bribe-taker, glutton and buffoon.
3473: XXVII
3474: Here, in his red peruke and glasses,
3475: late of Tambov, Monsieur Triquet
3476: has come with Kharlikov; he passes
3477: for witty; in his Gallic way
3478: inside a pocket Triquet nurses,
3479: addressed to Tanya, certain verses
3480: set to well-known children's glee:
3481: ``réveillez-vous, belle endormie.''
3482: He found them in some old collection,
3483: printed among outmoded airs;
3484: Triquet, ingenious poet, dares
3485: to undertake their resurrection,
3486: and for belle Nina, as it read,
3487: he's put belle Tatiana instead.
3488: {145}
3489: XXVIII
3490: And from the nearby Army station
3491: the Major's here: he's all the rage
3492: with our Mamas, and a sensation
3493: with demoiselles of riper age;
3494: his news has set the party humming!
3495: the regimental band is coming,
3496: sent at the Colonel's own behest.
3497: A ball: the joy of every guest!
3498: Young ladies jump for future blisses...
3499: But dinner's served, so two by two
3500: and arm in arm they all go through;
3501: round Tanya congregate the misses,
3502: the men confront them, face to face:
3503: they sit, they cross themselves for grace.
3504: XXIX
3505: They buzz -- but then all talk's suspended --
3506: jaws masticate as minutes pass:
3507: the crash of plates and knives is blended
3508: with the resounding chime of glass.
3509: And now there's gradually beginning
3510: among the guests a general dinning:
3511: none listens when the others speak,
3512: all shout and argue, laugh and squeak.
3513: Then doors are opened, Lensky enters,
3514: Onegin too. ``Good Lord, at last!''
3515: the hostess cries and, moving fast,
3516: the guests squeeze closer to the centres;
3517: they shove each plate, and every chair,
3518: and shout, and make room for the pair.
3519: {146}
3520: XXX
3521: Just facing Tanya's where they're sitting;
3522: and paler than the moon at dawn,
3523: she lowers darkened eyes, unwitting,
3524: and trembles like a hunted fawn.
3525: From violent passions fast pulsating
3526: she's nearly swooned, she's suffocating;
3527: the friends' salute she never hears
3528: and from her eyes the eager tears
3529: are almost bursting; she's quite ready,
3530: poor girl, to drop into a faint,
3531: but will, and reason's strong constraint,
3532: prevailed, and with composure steady
3533: she sat there; through her teeth a word
3534: came out so soft, it scarce was heard.
3535: XXXI
3536: The nervous-tragical reaction,
3537: girls' tears, their swooning, for Eugene
3538: had long proved tedious to distraction:
3539: he knew too well that sort of scene.
3540: Now, faced with this enormous revel,
3541: he'd got annoyed, the tricky devil.
3542: He saw the sad girl's trembling state,
3543: looked down in an access of hate,
3544: pouted, and swore in furious passion
3545: to wreak, by stirring Lensky's ire,
3546: the best revenge one could desire.
3547: Already, in exultant fashion,
3548: he watched the guests and, as he dined,
3549: caricatured them in his mind.
3550: {147}
3551: XXXII
3552: Tanya's distress had risked detection
3553: not only by Evgeny's eye;
3554: but looks and talk took the direction,
3555: that moment, of a luscious pie
3556: (alas, too salted); now they're bringing
3557: bottles to which some pitch is clinging:
3558: Tsimlyansky wine, between the meat
3559: and the blancmanger, then a fleet
3560: of goblets, tall and slender pretties;
3561: how they remind me of your stem,
3562: Zizi, my crystal and my gem,
3563: you object of my guileless ditties!
3564: with draughts from love's enticing flask,
3565: you made me drunk as one could ask!
3566: XXXIII
3567: Freed from its dripping cork, the bottle
3568: explodes; wine fizzes up... but stay:
3569: solemn, too long compelled to throttle
3570: his itching verse, Monsieur Triquet
3571: is on his feet -- in utter stillness
3572: the party waits. Seized with an illness
3573: of swooning, Tanya nearly dies;
3574: and, scroll in hand, before her eyes
3575: Triquet sings, out of tune. Loud clapping
3576: and cheers salute him. Tanya must
3577: thank him by curtseying to the dust;
3578: great bard despite his modest trapping,
3579: he's first to toast her in the bowl,
3580: then he presents her with the scroll.
3581: {148}
3582: XXXIV
3583: Compliment and congratulation;
3584: Tanya thanks each one with a phrase.
3585: When Eugene's turn for salutation
3586: arrives, the girl's exhausted gaze,
3587: her discomposure, her confusion,
3588: expose his soul to an intrusion
3589: of pity: in his silent bow,
3590: and in his look there shows somehow
3591: a wondrous tenderness. And whether
3592: it was that he'd been truly stirred,
3593: or half-unwittingly preferred
3594: a joking flirt, or both together,
3595: there was a softness in his glance:
3596: it brought back Tanya from her trance.
3597: XXXV
3598: Chairs are pushed outward, loudly rumbling,
3599: and all into the salon squeeze,
3600: as from their luscious hive go tumbling
3601: fieldward, in noisy swarm, the bees.
3602: The banquet's given no cause for sneezing,
3603: neighbours in high content are wheezing;
3604: ladies at the fireside confer,
3605: in corners whispering girls concur;
3606: now, by green tablecloths awaited,
3607: the eager players are enrolled --
3608: Boston and ombre for the old,
3609: and whist, that's now so keenly fêted --
3610: pursuits of a monotonous breed
3611: begot by boredom out of greed.
3612: {149}
3613: XXXVI
3614: By now whist's heroes have completed
3615: eight rubbers; and by now eight times
3616: they've moved around and been reseated;
3617: and tea's brought in. Instead of chimes
3618: I like to tell the time by dinner
3619: and tea and supper; there's an inner
3620: clock in the country rings the hour;
3621: no fuss; our belly has the power
3622: of any Bréguet: and in passing
3623: I'll just remark, my verses talk
3624: as much of banquets and the cork
3625: and eatables beyond all classing
3626: as yours did, Homer, godlike lord,
3627: whom thirty centuries have adored!
3628: < XXXVII7
3629: At feasts, though, full of pert aggression,
3630: I put your genius to the test,
3631: I make magnanimous confession,
3632: in other things you come off best:
3633: your heroes, raging and ferocious,
3634: your battles, lawless and atrocious,
3635: your Zeus, your Cypris, your whole band
3636: have clearly got the upper hand
3637: of Eugene, cold as all creation,
3638: of plains where boredom reigns complete,
3639: or of Istómina, my sweet,
3640: and all our modish education;
3641: but your vile Helen's not my star --
3642: no, Tanya's more endearing far.
3643: {150}
3644: XXXVIII
3645: No one will think that worth gainsaying,
3646: though Menelaus, in Helen's name,
3647: may spend a century in flaying
3648: the hapless Phrygians all the same,
3649: and although Troy's greybeards, collected
3650: around Priam the much-respected,
3651: may chorus, when she comes in sight,
3652: that Menelaus was quite right --
3653: and Paris too. But hear my pleading:
3654: as battles go, I've not begun;
3655: don't judge the race before it's run --
3656: be good enough to go on reading:
3657: there'll be a fight. For that I give
3658: my word; no welshing, as I live. >
3659: XXXIX
3660: Here's tea: the girls have just, as bidden,
3661: taken the saucers in their grip,
3662: when, from behind the doorway, hidden
3663: bassoons and flutes begin to trip.
3664: Elated by the music's blaring,
3665: Petushkóv, local Paris, tearing,
3666: his tea with rum quite left behind,
3667: approaches Olga; Lensky's signed
3668: Tatyana on; Miss Kharlikova,
3669: that nubile maid of riper age,
3670: is seized by Tambov's poet-sage;
3671: Buyánov whirls off Pustyakova;
3672: they all have swarmed into the hall,
3673: and in full brilliance shines the ball.
3674: {151}
3675: XL
3676: Right at the outset of my story
3677: (if you'll turn back to chapter one)
3678: I meant to paint, with Alban's8 glory,
3679: a ball in Petersburg; but fun
3680: and charming reverie's vain deflection
3681: absorbed me in the recollection
3682: of certain ladies' tiny feet.
3683: Enough I've wandered in the suite
3684: of your slim prints! though this be treason
3685: to my young days, it's time I turned
3686: to wiser words and deeds, and learned
3687: to demonstrate some signs of reason:
3688: let no more such digressions lurk
3689: in this fifth chapter of my work.
3690: XLI
3691: And now, monotonously dashing
3692: like mindless youth, the waltz goes by
3693: with spinning noise and senseless flashing
3694: as pair by pair the dancers fly.
3695: Revenge's hour is near, and after
3696: Evgeny, full of inward laughter,
3697: has gone to Olga, swept the girl
3698: past all the assembly in a whirl,
3699: he takes her to a chair, beginning
3700: to talk of this and that, but then
3701: after two minutes, off again,
3702: they're on the dance-floor, waltzing, spinning.
3703: All are dumbfounded. Lensky shies
3704: away from trusting his own eyes.
3705: {152}
3706: XLII
3707: Now the mazurka sounds. Its thunder
3708: used in times past to ring a peal
3709: that huge ballrooms vibrated under,
3710: while floors would split from crash of heel,
3711: and frames would shudder, windows tremble;
3712: now things are changed, now we resemble
3713: ladies who glide on waxed parquet.
3714: Yet the mazurka keeps today
3715: in country towns and suchlike places
3716: its pristine charm: heeltaps, and leaps,
3717: and whiskers -- all of this it keeps
3718: as fresh as ever, for its graces
3719: are here untouched by fashion's reign,
3720: our modern Russia's plague and bane.
3721: XLIII7
3722: ... ...
3723: < Petushkóv's nails and spurs are sounding
3724: (that half-pay archivist); and bounding
3725: Buyánov's heels have split the wood
3726: and wrecked the flooring-boards for good;
3727: there's crashing, rumbling, pounding, trotting,
3728: the deeper in the wood, the more
3729: the logs; the wild ones have the floor;
3730: they're plunging, whirling, all but squatting.
3731: Ah, gently, gently, easy goes --
3732: your heels will squash the ladies' toes! >
3733: {153}
3734: XLIV
3735: Buyánov, my vivacious cousin,
3736: leads Olga and Tatyana on
3737: to Eugene; nineteen to the dozen,
3738: Eugene takes Olga, and is gone;
3739: he steers her, nonchalantly gliding,
3740: he stoops and, tenderly confiding,
3741: whispers some ballad of the hour,
3742: squeezes her hand -- and brings to flower
3743: on her smug face a flush of pleasure.
3744: Lensky has watched: his rage has blazed,
3745: he's lost his self-command, and crazed
3746: with jealousy beyond all measure
3747: insists, when the mazurka ends,
3748: on the cotillion, as amends.
3749: XLV
3750: He asks. She can't accept. Why ever?
3751: No, she's already pledged her word
3752: to Evgeny. Oh, God, she'd never...
3753: How could she? why, he'd never heard...
3754: scarce out of bibs, already fickle,
3755: fresh from the cot, an infant pickle,
3756: already studying to intrigue,
3757: already high in treason's league!
3758: He finds the shock beyond all bearing:
3759: so, cursing women's devious course,
3760: he leaves the house, calls for his horse
3761: and gallops. Pistols made for pairing
3762: and just a double charge of shot
3763: will in a flash decide his lot.
3764: {154}
3765: Notes to Chapter Five
3766: 1  ``See First Snow,  a poem by Prince Vyazemsky.'' Pushkin's note. For
3767: Prince P. Vyazemsky (1791--1878), poet, critic and close friend of  Pushkin,
3768: see also Chapter Seven, XLIX.
3769: 2 ``See the descriptions  of the Finnish winter in  Baratynsky's Eda''.
3770: Pushkin's note.
3771: 3  ``"Tomcat calls  Kit"  -- a song  foretelling marriage.''  Pushkin's
3772: note.
3773: 4  This Russianized version of  the Greek Agatho  is  ``elephantine and
3774: rustic to the Russian ear''. Nabokov. See note 3 to Chapter Two.
3775: 5 Girl in Zhukovsky's  poem who practises divination,  with frightening
3776: results. See note 2 to Chapter Three.
3777: 6 Slavonic god of love.
3778: 7 Stanzas XXXVII, XXXVIII and XLIII were discarded by Pushkin.
3779: 8 Francesco Albani, Italian painter (1578-1660).

3781: Chapter Six
3782: La, sotto giorni nubilosi e brevi.
3783: Nasce una gente a cui 'l morir non dole.
3784: Petrarch
3785: I
3786: Seeing Vladimir had defected,
3787: Eugene, at Olga's side, was racked
3788: by fresh ennui as he reflected
3789: with pleasure on his vengeful act.
3790: Olinka yawned, just like her neighbour,
3791: and looked for Lensky, while the labour
3792: of the cotillion's endless theme
3793: oppressed her like a heavy dream.
3794: It's over. Supper is proceeding.
3795: Beds are made up; the guests are all
3796: packed from the maids' wing to the hall.
3797: Each one by now is badly needing
3798: a place for rest. Eugene alone
3799: has driven off, to find his own.
3800: {155}
3801: II
3802: All sleep: from the saloon a roaring
3803: proclaims where ponderous Pústyakov
3804: beside his heavier half is snoring.
3805: Gvozdín, Buyánov, Petushkóv
3806: and Flyánov, amply lubricated,
3807: on dining-chairs are all prostrated;
3808: the floor serves Triquet for his nap,
3809: in flannel, and an old fur cap.
3810: In the two sisters' rooms extended,
3811: the maidens all are slumbering deep.
3812: Only Tatyana does not sleep,
3813: but at the window, in the splendid
3814: radiance of Dian, sits in pain
3815: and looks out on the darkened plain.
3816: III
3817: His unexpected apparition,
3818: the fleeting tenderness that stole
3819: into his look, the exhibition
3820: with Olga, all have pierced her soul;
3821: she can't make out a single fraction
3822: of his intent; and a reaction
3823: of jealousy has made her start,
3824: as if a cold hand squeezed her heart,
3825: as if beneath her, dark and rumbling,
3826: a gulf has gaped... Says Tanya: ``I
3827: am doomed to perish, yet to die
3828: through him is sweetness' self. In grumbling
3829: I find no sense; the truth is this,
3830: it's not in him to bring me bliss.''
3831: {156}
3832: IV
3833: But onward, onward with my story!
3834: A new acquaintance claims our quill.
3835: Five versts or so from Krasnogórie,
3836: Lensky's estate, there lives and still
3837: thrives to this moment, in a station
3838: of philosophic isolation,
3839: Zarétsky, sometime king of brawls
3840: and hetman of the gambling-halls,
3841: arch-rake, pothouse tribune-persona,
3842: but now grown plain and kind in stead,
3843: paterfamilias (unwed),
3844: unswerving friend, correct landowner,
3845: and even honourable man:
3846: so, if we want to change, we can!
3847: V
3848: The world of fashion, prone to flatter,
3849: praised his fierce courage in its day:
3850: true, with a pistol he could shatter
3851: an ace a dozen yards away;
3852: it's also true, in battle's rapture,
3853: the circumstances of his capture
3854: had made his name, when, bold as bold,
3855: down from his Kalmuck steed he rolled
3856: into the mud, a drunken goner,
3857: and taken by the French -- some prize! --
3858: resigned himself to prison's ties,
3859: like Regulus, that god of honour,
3860: in order daily, chez Véry,1
3861: to drain, on credit, bottles three.
3862: {157}
3863: VI
3864: Time was, he'd been the wittiest ever,
3865: so brilliantly he'd hoax the fools,
3866: so gloriously he'd fool the clever,
3867: using overt or covert rules.
3868: Sometimes his tricks would earn him trouble,
3869: or cause the bursting of his bubble,
3870: sometimes he'd fall into a trap
3871: himself just like a simple chap.
3872: But he could draw a joking moral,
3873: return an answer, blunt or keen,
3874: use cunning silence as a screen,
3875: or cunningly create a quarrel,
3876: get two young friends to pick a fight,
3877: and put them on a paced-out site.
3878: VII
3879: Or he knew how to reconcile them
3880: so that all three went off to lunch,
3881: then later slyly he'd revile them
3882: with lies and jokes that packed a punch:
3883: sed alia tempora! The devil
3884: (like passion's dream, that other revel)
3885: goes out of us when youth is dead.
3886: So my Zaretsky, as I said,
3887: beneath bird-cherries and acacias
3888: has found a port for his old age,
3889: and lives, a veritable sage,
3890: for planting cabbage, like Horatius,
3891: and breeding ducks and geese as well,
3892: and teaching children how to spell.
3893: {158}
3894: VIII
3895: He was no fool; appreciated
3896: by my Eugene, not for his heart,
3897: but for the effect that he created
3898: of sense and judgement. For his part
3899: his converse gave Onegin pleasure;
3900: so it was not in any measure,
3901: the morning after, a surprise
3902: when our Zaretsky met his eyes.
3903: His visitor from the beginning
3904: broke greetings off, and gave Eugene
3905: a note from Lensky; in between
3906: Zaretsky watched, and stood there grinning.
3907: Onegin without more ado
3908: crossed to the window, read it through.
3909: IX
3910: Pleasant, in spite of its compression,
3911: gentlemanly, quite precise,
3912: Vladimir's challenge found expression
3913: that, though polite, was clear as ice.
3914: Eugene's response was automatic;
3915: he informed this envoy diplomatic
3916: in terms where not a word was spared:
3917: at any time he'd be prepared.
3918: Zaretsky rose without discussion;
3919: he saw no point in staying on,
3920: with work at home; but when he'd gone,
3921: Evgeny, whom the repercussion
3922: left quite alone with his own soul,
3923: was far from happy with his role.
3924: {159}
3925: X
3926: With reason, too: for when he'd vetted
3927: in secret judgement what he'd done,
3928: he found too much that he regretted:
3929: last night he'd erred in making fun,
3930: so heartless and so detrimental,
3931: of love so timorous and gentle.
3932: In second place the poet might
3933: have been a fool; yet he'd a right,
3934: at eighteen years, to some compassion.
3935: Evgeny loved him from his heart,
3936: and should have played a different part:
3937: no softball for the winds of fashion,
3938: no boy, to fight or take offence --
3939: the man of honour and of sense.
3940: XI
3941: He could have spoken without harming,
3942: need not have bristled like a beast;
3943: he should have settled for disarming
3944: that youthful heart. ``But now at least
3945: it's late, time's passing... not to mention,
3946: in our affair, the intervention
3947: of that old duellistic fox,
3948: that wicked, loose-tongue chatterbox...
3949: True, scorn should punish and should bridle
3950: his wit, according to the rules
3951: but whispers, the guffaw of fools...''
3952: Public opinion -- here's our idol,
3953: the spring of honour, and the pin
3954: on which the world is doomed to spin.
3955: {160}
3956: XII
3957: Lensky at home awaits the answer,
3958: impatient, hatred flaming high;
3959: but here comes our loud-talking prancer
3960: who swaggers in with the reply.
3961: The jealous poet's gloom is lightened!
3962: knowing the offender, he'd been frightened
3963: lest he should by some clever trick
3964: avert his chest from pistol's click,
3965: smoothe his way out with humour's ointment.
3966: But now Vladimir's doubts are still:
3967: early tomorrow at the mill
3968: before first light they have appointment,
3969: to raise the safety catch and strain
3970: to hit the target: thigh or brain.
3971: XIII
3972: Still blazing with resentment's fuel,
3973: and set on hating the coquette,
3974: Lensky resolved before the duel
3975: not to see Olga; in a fret
3976: watched sun and clock -- then by such labours
3977: defeated, turned up at his neighbour's.
3978: He thought that Olga'd be confused,
3979: struck down as if she'd been accused,
3980: when he arrived; not in the slightest:
3981: just as she'd always been, she tripped
3982: to meet the unhappy poet, skipped
3983: down from the porch, light as the lightest,
3984: the giddiest hope, carefree and gay,
3985: the same as any other day.
3986: {161}
3987: XIV
3988: ``Last night, what made you fly so early?''
3989: was the first thing that Olga said.
3990: All Lensky's thoughts went hurly-burly,
3991: and silently he hung his head.
3992: Rage died, and jealousy's obsession,
3993: before such candour of expression,
3994: such frank tendresse; away they stole
3995: before such playfulness of soul!...
3996: he looks, in sweet irresolution,
3997: and then concludes: she loves him yet!
3998: Already borne down by regret,
3999: he almost begs for absolution,
4000: he trembles, knows not what to tell;
4001: he's happy, yes, he's almost well...
4002: (XV, XVI,2) XVII
4003: Now brooding thoughts hold his attention
4004: once more, at that beloved sight,
4005: and so he lacks the strength to mention
4006: the happenings of the previous night;
4007: he murmurs: ``Olga's mine for saving;
4008: I'll stop that tempter from depraving
4009: her youth with all his repertoire
4010: of sighs, and compliments, and fire;
4011: that poisonous worm, despised, degrading,
4012: shall not attack my lily's root;
4013: I'll save this blossom on the shoot,
4014: still hardly opened up, from fading.''
4015: Friends, all this meant was: I've a date
4016: for swapping bullets with my mate.
4017: {162}
4018: XVIII
4019: If only Lensky'd known the burning
4020: wound that had seared my Tanya's heart!
4021: If Tanya'd had the chance of learning
4022: that Lensky and Eugene, apart,
4023: would settle, on the morrow morning,
4024: for which of them the tomb was yawning,
4025: perhaps her love could in the end
4026: have reunited friend to friend!
4027: But, even by accident, her passion
4028: was undiscovered to that day.
4029: Onegin had no word to say;
4030: Tatyana pined in secret fashion:
4031: of the whole world, her nurse alone,
4032: if not slow-witted, might have known.
4033: XIX
4034: Lensky all evening, in distraction,
4035: would talk, keep silent, laugh, then frown --
4036: the quintessential reaction
4037: of Muses' offspring; sitting down
4038: before the clavichord with knitted
4039: forehead, he strummed, his vision flitted
4040: to Olga's face, he whispered low
4041: ``I think I'm happy.'' Time to go,
4042: the hour was late. And now from aching
4043: the heart inside him seemed to shrink;
4044: parting with Olga made him think
4045: it was quite torn in half and breaking.
4046: She faced him, questioning: ``But you?...''
4047: ``It's nothing.'' And away he flew.
4048: {163}
4049: XX
4050: Once home, he brought out and inspected
4051: his pistols, laid them in their case,
4052: undressed, by candlelight selected
4053: and opened Schiller... but the embrace
4054: of one sole thought holds him in keeping
4055: and stops his doleful heart from sleeping:
4056: Olga is there, he sees her stand
4057: in untold beauty close at hand.
4058: Vladimir shuts the book, for writing
4059: prepares himself; and then his verse,
4060: compact of amorous trash, and worse,
4061: flows and reverberates. Reciting,
4062: he sounds, in lyric frenzy sunk,
4063: like Delvig3 when he's dining drunk.
4064: XXI
4065: By chance those verses haven't vanished;
4066: I keep them, and will quote them here:
4067: ``Whither, oh whither are ye banished,
4068: my golden days when spring was dear?
4069: What fate is my tomorrow brewing?
4070: the answer's past all human viewing,
4071: it's hidden deep in gloom and dust.
4072: No matter; fate's decree is just.
4073: Whether the arrow has my number,
4074: whether it goes careering past,
4075: all's well; the destined hour at last
4076: comes for awakening, comes for slumber;
4077: blessed are daytime's care and cark,
4078: blest is the advent of the dark!
4079: {164}
4080: XXII
4081: ``The morning star will soon be shining,
4082: and soon will day's bright tune be played;
4083: but I perhaps will be declining
4084: into the tomb's mysterious shade;
4085: the trail the youthful poet followed
4086: by sluggish Lethe may be swallowed,
4087: and I be by the world forgot;
4088: but, lovely maiden, wilt thou not
4089: on my untimely urn be weeping,
4090: thinking: he loved me, and in strife
4091: the sad beginnings of his life
4092: he consecrated to my keeping?...
4093: Friend of my heart, be at my side,
4094: beloved friend, thou art my bride!''
4095: XXIII
4096: So Lensky wrote, obscurely, limply
4097: (in the romantic style, we say,
4098: though what's romantic here I simply
4099: fail to perceive -- that's by the way).
4100: At last, with dawn upon him, stooping
4101: his weary head, and softly drooping
4102: over the modish word ideal,
4103: he dozed away; but when the real
4104: magic of sleep had started claiming
4105: its due oblivion, in the hush
4106: his neighbour entered at a rush
4107: and wakened Lensky by exclaiming:
4108: ``Get up: it's gone six! I'll be bound,
4109: Onegin's waiting on the ground.''
4110: {165}
4111: XXIV
4112: But he's mistaken: Eugene's lying
4113: and sleeping sounder than a rock.
4114: By now the shades of night are flying,
4115: Vesper is met by crow of cock --
4116: Onegin still is slumbering deeply.
4117: By now the sun is climbing steeply,
4118: and little dancing whirls of snow
4119: glitter and tumble as they go,
4120: but Eugene hasn't moved; for certain
4121: slumber still floats above his head.
4122: At last he wakes, and stirs in bed,
4123: and parts the fringes of his curtain;
4124: he looks, and sees the hour of day --
4125: high time he should be on his way.
4126: XXV
