4127: He rings at once, and what a scurry!
4128: his French valet, Guillot, is there
4129: with gown and slippers; tearing hurry,
4130: as linen's brought for him to wear.
4131: And while with all despatch he's dressing
4132: he warns his man for duty, stressing
4133: that with him to the trysting-place
4134: he has to bring the battle-case.
4135: By now the sledge is at the portal --
4136: he's racing millward like a bird.
4137: Arrived apace, he gives the word
4138: to bring across Lepage's4 mortal
4139: barrels, and then to drive aside
4140: by two small oaktrees in a ride.
4141: {166}
4142: XXVI
4143: While Lensky'd long been meditating
4144: impatiently on the mill-dam,
4145: Zaretsky, engineer-in-waiting,
4146: condemned the millstones as a sham.
4147: Onegin comes, and makes excuses;
4148: but in Zaretsky he induces
4149: amazement: ``Where's your second gone?''
4150: In duels a pedantic don,
4151: methodical by disposition,
4152: a classicist, he'll not allow
4153: that one be shot just anyhow --
4154: only by rule, and strict tradition
4155: inherited from earlier days
4156: (for which he must receive due praise).
4157: XXVII
4158: Evgeny echoed him: ``My second?
4159: He's here -- Monsieur Guillot, my friend.
4160: I had most surely never reckoned
4161: his choice could shock or might offend;
4162: though he's unknown, there's no suggestion
4163: that he's not honest past all question.''
4164: Zaretsky bit his lip. Eugene
4165: asked Lensky: ``Should we start, I mean?''
4166: Vladimir to this casual mention
4167: replies: ``We might as well.'' They walk
4168: behind the mill. In solemn talk,
4169: Zaretsky draws up a convention
4170: with Guillot; while pourparlers last
4171: the two foes stand with eyes downcast.
4172: {167}
4173: XXVIII
4174: Foes! Is it long since from each other
4175: the lust for blood drew them apart?
4176: long since, like brother linked to brother,
4177: they shared their days in deed and heart,
4178: their table, and their hours of leisure?
4179: But now, in this vindictive pleasure
4180: hereditary foes they seem,
4181: and as in some appalling dream
4182: each coldly plans the other's slaughter...
4183: could they not laugh out loud, before
4184: their hands are dipped in scarlet gore,
4185: could they not give each other quarter
4186: and part in kindness? Just the same,
4187: all modish foes dread worldly shame.
4188: XXIX
4189: Pistols are out, they gleam, the hammer
4190: thumps as the balls are pressed inside
4191: faceted muzzles by the rammer;
4192: with a first click, the catch is tried.
4193: Now powder's greyish stream is slipping
4194: into the pan. Securely gripping,
4195: the jagged flint's pulled back anew.
4196: Guillot, behind a stump in view,
4197: stands in dismay and indecision.
4198: And now the two opponents doff
4199: their cloaks; Zaretsky's measured off
4200: thirty-two steps with great precision,
4201: and on their marks has made them stand;
4202: each grips his pistol in his hand.
4203: {168}
4204: XXX
4205: ``Now march.'' And calmly, not yet seeking
4206: to aim, at steady, even pace
4207: the foes, cold-blooded and unspeaking,
4208: each took four steps across the space,
4209: four fateful stairs. Then, without slowing
4210: the level tenor of his going,
4211: Evgeny quietly began
4212: to lift his pistol up. A span
4213: of five more steps they went, slow-gaited,
4214: and Lensky, left eye closing, aimed --
4215: but just then Eugene's pistol flamed...
4216: The clock of doom had struck as fated;
4217: and the poet, without a sound,
4218: let fall his pistol on the ground.
4219: XXXI
4220: Vladimir drops, hand softly sliding
4221: to heart. And in his misted gaze
4222: is death, not pain. So gently gliding
4223: down slopes of mountains, when a blaze
4224: of sunlight makes it flash and crumble,
4225: a block of snow will slip and tumble.
4226: Onegin, drenched with sudden chill,
4227: darts to the boy, and looks, and still
4228: calls out his name... All unavailing:
4229: the youthful votary of rhyme
4230: has found an end before his time.
4231: The storm is over,5 dawn is paling,
4232: the bloom has withered on the bough;
4233: the altar flame's extinguished now.
4234: {169}
4235: XXXII
4236: He lay quite still, and strange as dreaming
4237: was that calm brow of one who swooned.
4238: Shot through below the chest -- and streaming
4239: the blood came smoking from the wound.
4240: A moment earlier, inspiration
4241: had filled this heart, and detestation
4242: and hope and passion; life had glowed
4243: and blood had bubbled as it flowed;
4244: but now the mansion is forsaken;
4245: shutters are up, and all is pale
4246: and still within, behind the veil
4247: of chalk the window-panes have taken.
4248: The lady of the house has fled.
4249: Where to, God knows. The trail is dead.
4250: XXXIII
4251: With a sharp epigram it's pleasant
4252: to infuriate a clumsy foe;
4253: and, as observer, to be present
4254: and watch him stubbornly bring low
4255: his thrusting horns, and as he passes
4256: blush to descry in looking-glasses
4257: his foolish face; more pleasant yet
4258: to hear him howl: ``that's me!'' You'll get
4259: more joy still when with mute insistence
4260: you help him to an honoured fate
4261: by calmly aiming at his pate
4262: from any gentlemanly distance;
4263: but when you've managed his despatch
4264: you won't find that quite so much catch...
4265: {170}
4266: XXXIV
4267: What if your pistol-shot has smitten
4268: a friend of yours in his first youth
4269: because some glance of his has bitten
4270: your pride, some answer, or in truth
4271: some nonsense thrown up while carousing,
4272: or if himself, with rage arousing,
4273: he's called you out -- say, in your soul
4274: what feelings would assume control
4275: if, motionless, no life appearing,
4276: death on his brow, your friend should lie,
4277: stiffening as the hours go by,
4278: before you on the ground, unhearing,
4279: unspeaking, too, but stretched out there
4280: deaf to the voice of your despair?
4281: XXXV
4282: Giving his pistol-butt a squeezing,
4283: Evgeny looks at Lensky, chilled
4284: at heart by grim remorse's freezing.
4285: ``Well, what?'' the neighbour says, ``he's killed.''
4286: Killed!... At this frightful word a-quiver,
4287: Onegin turns, and with a shiver
4288: summons his people. On the sleigh
4289: with care Zaretsky stows away
4290: the frozen corpse, drives off, and homing
4291: vanishes with his load of dread.
4292: The horses, as they sense the dead,
4293: have snorted, reared, and whitely foaming
4294: have drenched the steel bit as they go
4295: and flown like arrows from a bow.
4296: {171}
4297: XXXVI
4298: My friends, the bard stirs your compassion:
4299: right in the flower of joyous hope,
4300: hope that he's had no time to fashion
4301: for men to see, still in the scope
4302: of swaddling clothes -- already blighted!
4303: Where is the fire that once ignited,
4304: where's the high aim, the ardent sense
4305: of youth, so tender, so intense?
4306: and where is love's tempestuous yearning,
4307: where are the reveries this time,
4308: the horror of disgrace and crime,
4309: the thirst for work, the lust for learning,
4310: and life celestial's phantom gleams,
4311: stuff of the poet's hallowed dreams!
4312: XXXVII
4313: Perhaps to improve the world's condition,
4314: perhaps for fame, he was endowed;
4315: his lyre, now stilled, in its high mission
4316: might have resounded long and loud
4317: for aeons. Maybe it was fated
4318: that on the world's staircase there waited
4319: for him a lofty stair. His shade,
4320: after the martyr's price it paid,
4321: maybe bore off with it for ever
4322: a secret truth, and at our cost
4323: a life-creating voice was lost;
4324: to it the people's blessing never
4325: will reach, and past the tomb's compound
4326: hymns of the ages never sound.
4327: {172}
4328: (XXXVIII,2) XXXIX
4329: Perhaps however, to be truthful,
4330: he would have found a normal fate.
4331: The years would pass; no longer youthful,
4332: he'd see his soul cool in its grate;
4333: his nature would be changed and steadied,
4334: he'd sack the Muses and get wedded;
4335: and in the country, blissful, horned,
4336: in quilted dressing-gown adorned,
4337: life's real meaning would have found him;
4338: at forty he'd have got the gout,
4339: drunk, eaten, yawned, grown weak and stout,
4340: at length, midst children swarming round him,
4341: midst crones with endless tears to shed,
4342: and doctors, he'd have died in bed.
4343: XL
4344: Reader, whatever fate's direction,
4345: we weep for the young lover's end,
4346: the man of reverie and reflection,
4347: the poet struck down by his friend!
4348: Left-handed from the habitation
4349: where dwelt this child of inspiration,
4350: two pines have tangled at the root;
4351: beneath, a brook rolls its tribute
4352: toward the neighbouring valley's river.
4353: The ploughman there delights to doze,
4354: girl reapers as the streamlet flows
4355: dip in their jugs; where shadows quiver
4356: darkly above the water's lilt,
4357: a simple monument is built.
4358: {173}
4359: XLI
4360: Below it, when sprang rains are swishing,
4361: when, on the plain, green herbs are massed,
4362: the shepherd sings of Volga's fishing
4363: and plaits a piebald shoe of bast;
4364: and the young city-bred newcomer,
4365: who in the country spends her summer,
4366: when galloping at headlong pace
4367: alone across the fields of space,
4368: will halt her horse and, gripping tightly
4369: the leather rein, to learn the tale,
4370: lift up the gauzes of her veil,
4371: with a quick look perusing lightly
4372: the simple legend -- then a haze
4373: of tears will cloud her tender gaze.
4374: XLII
4375: Walking her horse in introspection
4376: across the plain's enormous room,
4377: what holds her in profound reflection,
4378: despite herself, is Lensky's doom;
4379: ``Olga,'' she thinks, ``what fate befell her?
4380: her heartache, did it long compel her,
4381: or did her grief soon find repair?
4382: and where's her sister now? and where,
4383: flown from society as we know it,
4384: of modish belles the modish foe,
4385: where did that glum eccentric go,
4386: the one who killed the youthful poet?''
4387: All in good time, on each point I
4388: will give you a complete reply.
4389: {174}
4390: XLIII
4391: But not today. Although I dearly
4392: value the hero of my tale,
4393: though I'll come back to him, yet clearly
4394: to face him now I feel too frail...
4395: The years incline to gloom and prosing,
4396: they kill the zest of rhymed composing,
4397: and with a sigh I now admit
4398: I have to drag my feet to it.
4399: My pen, as once, no longer hurries
4400: to spoil loose paper by the ream;
4401: another, a more chilling dream,
4402: and other, more exacting worries,
4403: in fashion's din, at still of night,
4404: come to disturb me and affright.
4405: XLIV
4406: I've learnt the voice of new ambition,
4407: I've learnt new sadness; but in this
4408: the first will never find fruition,
4409: the earlier griefs are what I miss.
4410: O dreams, o dreams, where is your sweetness?
4411: where (standard rhyme) are youth and fleetness?
4412: can it be true, their crown at last
4413: has felt time's desiccating blast?
4414: can it be true, and firmly stated
4415: without an elegiac frill,
4416: that spring with me has had its fill
4417: (as I've so oft in jest related)?
4418: Can it be true, it won't come twice --
4419: and I'll be thirty in a trice?
4420: {175}
4421: XLV
4422: Well, I must make a frank confession,
4423: my noon is here, and that's the truth.
4424: So let me with a kind expression
4425: take leave of my lightheaded youth!
4426: Thank you for all the gifts I treasure,
4427: thank you for sorrow and for pleasure,
4428: thank you for suffering and its joys,
4429: for tempests and for feasts and noise;
4430: thank you indeed. Alike in sorrow
4431: and in flat calm I've found the stuff
4432: of perfect bliss in you. Enough!
4433: My soul's like crystal, and tomorrow
4434: I shall set out on brand-new ways
4435: and rest myself from earlier days.
4436: XLVI
4437: Let me look back. Farewell, umbrageous
4438: forests where my young age was passed
4439: in indolence and in rampageous
4440: passion and dreams of pensive cast.
4441: But come, thou youthful inspiration,
4442: come, trouble my imagination,
4443: liven the drowsing of my heart,
4444: fly to my corner like a dart,
4445: let not the poet's soul of passion
4446: grow cold, and hard, and stiff as stock,
4447: and finally be turned to rock
4448: amid the deadening joys of fashion,
4449: < amongst the soulless men of pride,
4450: the fools who sparkle far and wide,6
4451: {176}
4452: XLVII
4453: amongst the crafty and small-minded,
4454: the children spoilt, the mad, the rogues
4455: both dull and ludicrous, the bunded
4456: critics and their capricious vogues,
4457: amongst devout coquettes, appalling
4458: lickspittles who adore their crawling,
4459: and daily scenes of modish life
4460: where civil treacheries are rife,
4461: urbane betrayals, and the chilling
4462: verdicts of vanity the bleak,
4463: men's thoughts, their plots, the words they speak,
4464: all of an emptiness so killing -- >
4465: that's the morass, I beg you note,
4466: in which, dear friends, we're all afloat!
4467: {177}
4468: Notes to Chapter Six
4469: 1 Café-restaurant in Paris.
4470: 2 Stanzas XV, XVI and XXXVIII were discarded by Pushkin.
4471: 3 Anton Delvig, poet and close friend of Pushkin.
4472: 4 Jean Lepage, Parisian gunsmith.
4473: 5  ``A  deliberate  accumulation of  conventional poetical  formulae by
4474: means of  which Pushkin mimics  poor Lensky's own style... but  the rich and
4475: original  metaphor  of the deserted house, closed  inner shutters,  whitened
4476: window-panes, departed  female owner (the soul being  feminine  in Russian),
4477: with which XXXII ends, is Pushkin's own contribution, a sample as it were of
4478: what he can do.'' Nabokov.
4479: 6 These lines and the first twelve lines of stanza XLVII were discarded
4480: by Pushkin.
4481: --------
4482: Chapter Seven
4483: Moscow, loved daughter of Russia,
4484: where can we find your equal?
4485: Dmitriev
4486: ``How can one not love mother Moscow?''
4487: Baratynsky
4488: ``You criticize Moscow? why make such a fuss
4489: of seeing the world? what on earth could be better?''
4490: ``A place where you'll find none of us.''
4491: Griboedov
4492: I
4493: By now the rays of spring are chasing
4494: the snow from all surrounding hills;
4495: it melts, away it rushes, racing
4496: down to the plain in turbid rills.
4497: Smiling through sleep, nature is meeting
4498: the infant year with cheerful greeting:
4499: the sky is brilliant in its blue
4500: and, still transparent to the view,
4501: the downy woods are greener-tinted;
4502: from waxen cell the bees again
4503: levy their tribute on the plain;
4504: the vales dry out, grow brightly printed;
4505: cows low, in the still nights of spring
4506: the nightingale's begun to sing.
4507: {178}
4508: II
4509: O spring! o time for love! how sadly
4510: your advent swamps me in its flood!
4511: and in my soul, o spring, how madly
4512: your presence aches, and in my blood!
4513: How heavy, and how near to sobbing,
4514: the bliss that fills me when your throbbing,
4515: caressing breath has fanned my face
4516: in rural calm's most secret place!
4517: Or from all notion of enjoyment
4518: am I estranged, does all that cheers,
4519: that lives, and glitters, and endears,
4520: now crush with sorrow's dull deployment
4521: a soul that perished long ago,
4522: and finds the world a darkling show?
4523: III
4524: Or, unconsoled by the returning
4525: of leaves that autumn killed for good,
4526: are we recalled to grief still burning
4527: by the new whisper in the wood?
4528: or else does nature, fresh and staring,
4529: set off our troubled mind comparing
4530: its newness with our faded days,
4531: with years no more to meet our gaze?
4532: Perhaps, when thoughts are all a-quiver
4533: in midst of a poetic dream,
4534: some other, older spring will gleam,
4535: and put our heart into a shiver
4536: with visions of enchanted night,
4537: of distant countries, of moonlight...
4538: {179}
4539: IV
4540: It's time: kind-hearted, idle creatures,
4541: dons of Epicurean rule,
4542: calm men with beatific features,
4543: graduates of the Levshin1 school,
4544: Priam-like agricultural sages,
4545: sensitive ladies of all ages --
4546: the spring invites you to the land
4547: now warmth and blossom are on hand,
4548: field-work, and walks with inspiration,
4549: and magic nights. In headlong course
4550: come to the fields, my friends! To horse!
4551: With mounts from home, or postal station,
4552: in loaded carriages, migrate,
4553: leave far behind that city-gate.
4554: V
4555: Forsake, indulgent reader -- driven
4556: in your calèche of foreign cast --
4557: the untiring city, where you've given
4558: to feasts and fun this winter past;
4559: and though my muse may be capricious,
4560: we'll go with her to that delicious
4561: and nameless rivulet, that scene
4562: of whispering woods where my Eugene,
4563: an idle monk in glum seclusion,
4564: has lately wintered, just a space
4565: from young Tatyana's dwelling-place,
4566: dear Tanya, lover of illusion;
4567: though there he's no more to be found,
4568: he's left sad footprints on the ground.
4569: {180}
4570: VI
4571: Amidst the hills, down in that valley,
4572: let's go where, winding all the time
4573: across green meadows, dilly-dally,
4574: a brook flows through a grove of lime.
4575: There sings the nightingale, spring's lover,
4576: the wild rose blooms, and in the covert
4577: the source's chattering voice is heard;
4578: and there a tombstone says its word
4579: where two old pinetrees stand united:
4580: ``This is Vladimir Lensky's grave
4581: who early died as die the brave'' --
4582: the headpiece-text is thus indited --
4583: the year, his age, then: ``may your rest,
4584: young poet, be for ever blest!''
4585: VII
4586: There was a pine-branch downward straying
4587: towards the simple urn beneath;
4588: time was when morning's breeze was swaying
4589: over it a mysterious wreath:
4590: time was, in evening hours of leisure,
4591: by moonlight two young girls took pleasure,
4592: closely embraced, in wending here,
4593: to see the grave, and shed a tear.
4594: Today... the sad memorial's lonely,
4595: forgot. Its trodden path is now
4596: choked up. There's no wreath on the bough;
4597: grey-haired and weak, beneath it only
4598: the shepherd, as he used to do,
4599: sings as he plaits a humble shoe.
4600: {181}
4601: (VIII,2 IX,) X
4602: Poor Lensky! Set aside for weeping,
4603: or pining, Olga's hours were brief.
4604: Alas for him! there was no keeping
4605: his sweetheart faithful to her grief.
4606: Another had the skill to ravish
4607: her thoughts away, knew how to lavish
4608: sweet words by which her pain was banned --
4609: a Lancer wooed and won her hand,
4610: a Lancer -- how she deified him!
4611: and at the altar, with a crown,
4612: her head in modesty cast down,
4613: already there she stands beside him;
4614: her eyes are lowered, but ablaze,
4615: and on her lips a light smile plays.
4616: XI
4617: Poor Lensky! where the tomb is bounded
4618: by dull eternity's purlieus,
4619: was the sad poet not confounded
4620: at this betrayal's fateful news?
4621: Or, as by Lethe's bank he slumbered,
4622: perhaps no more sensations lumbered
4623: the lucky bard, and as he dozed
4624: the earth for him grew dumb and closed?...
4625: On such indifference, such forgetting
4626: beyond the grave we all must build --
4627: foes, friends and loves, their voice is stilled.
4628: Only the estate provides a setting
4629: for angry heirs, as one, to fall
4630: into an unbecoming brawl.
4631: {182}
4632: XII
4633: Presently Olga's ringing answer
4634: inside the Larins' house fell mute.
4635: Back to his regiment the Lancer,
4636: slave of the service, was en route.
4637: Weltered in tears, and sorely smarting,
4638: the old dame wept her daughter's parting,
4639: and in her grief seemed fit to die;
4640: but Tanya found she couldn't cry:
4641: only the pallor of heart-breaking
4642: covered her face. When all came out
4643: onto the porch, and fussed about
4644: over the business of leave-taking,
4645: Tatyana went with them, and sped
4646: the carriage of the newly-wed.
4647: XIII
4648: And long, as if through mists that spurted,
4649: Tanya pursued them with her gaze...
4650: So there she stood, forlorn, deserted!
4651: The comrade of so many days,
4652: oh! her young dove, the natural hearer
4653: of secrets, like a friend but dearer,
4654: had been for ever borne off far
4655: and parted from her by their star.
4656: Shade-like, in purposeless obsession
4657: she roams the empty garden-plot...
4658: in everything she sees there's not
4659: a grain of gladness; tears' repression
4660: allows no comfort to come through --
4661: Tatyana's heart is rent in two.
4662: {183}
4663: XIV
4664: Her passion burns with stronger powder
4665: now she's bereft, and just the same
4666: her heart speaks to her even louder
4667: of far-away Onegin's name.
4668: She'll not see him, her obligation
4669: must be to hold in detestation
4670: the man who laid her brother low.
4671: The poet's dead... already though
4672: no one recalls him or his verses;
4673: by now his bride-to-be has wed
4674: another, and his memory's fled
4675: as smoke in azure sky disperses.
4676: Two hearts there are perhaps that keep
4677: a tear for him... but what's to weep?
4678: XV
4679: Evening, and darkening sky, and waters
4680: in quiet flood. A beetle whirred.
4681: The choirs of dancers sought their quarters.
4682: Beyond the stream there smoked and stirred
4683: a fisher's fire. Through country gleaming
4684: silver with moonlight, in her dreaming
4685: profoundly sunk, Tatyana stalked
4686: for hours alone; she walked and walked...
4687: Suddenly, from a crest, she sighted
4688: a house, a village, and a wood
4689: below a hill; a garden stood
4690: above a stream the moon had lighted.
4691: She looked across, felt in her heart
4692: a faster, stronger pulsing start.
4693: {184}
4694: XVI
4695: She hesitates, and doubts beset her:
4696: forward or back? it's true that he
4697: has left, and no one here has met her...
4698: ``The house, the park... I'll go and see!''
4699: So down came Tanya, hardly daring
4700: to draw a breath, around her staring
4701: with puzzled and confused regard...
4702: She entered the deserted yard.
4703: Dogs, howling, rushed in her direction...
4704: Her frightened cry brought running out
4705: the household boys in noisy rout;
4706: giving the lady their protection,
4707: by dint of cuff and kick and smack
4708: they managed to disperse the pack.
4709: XVII
4710: ``Could I just see the house, I wonder?''
4711: Tatyana asked. The children all
4712: rushed to Anisia's room, to plunder
4713: the keys that opened up the hall.
4714: At once Anisia came to greet her,
4715: the doorway opened wide to meet her,
4716: she went inside the empty shell
4717: in which our hero used to dwell.
4718: She looks: forgotten past all chalking
4719: on billiard-table rests a cue,
4720: and on the crumpled sofa too
4721: a riding whip. Tanya keeps walking...
4722: ``And here's the hearth,'' explains the crone,
4723: ``where master used to sit alone.
4724: {185}
4725: XVIII
4726: ``Here in the winter he'd have dinner
4727: with neighbour Lensky, the deceased.
4728: Please follow me. And here's the inner
4729: study where he would sleep and feast
4730: on cups of coffee, and then later
4731: he'd listen to the administrator;
4732: in morning time he'd read a book...
4733: And just here, in the window-nook,
4734: is where old master took up station,
4735: and put his glasses on to see
4736: his Sunday game of cards with me.
4737: I pray God grant his soul salvation,
4738: and rest his dear bones in the tomb,
4739: down in our damp earth-mother's womb!''
4740: XIX
4741: Tatyana in a deep emotion
4742: gazes at all the scene around;
4743: she drinks it like a priceless potion;
4744: it stirs her drooping soul to bound
4745: in fashion that's half-glad, half-anguished:
4746: that table where the lamp has languished,
4747: beside the window-sill, that bed
4748: on which a carpet has been spread,
4749: piled books, and through the pane the sable
4750: moonscape, the half-light overall,
4751: Lord Byron's portrait on the wall,
4752: the iron figure3 on the table,
4753: the hat, the scowling brow, the chest
4754: where folded arms are tightly pressed.
4755: {186}
4756: XX
4757: Longtime inside this modish cloister,
4758: as if spellbound, Tatyana stands.
4759: It's late. A breeze begins to roister,
4760: the valley's dark. The forest lands
4761: round the dim river sleep; the curtain
4762: of hills has hid the moon; for certain
4763: the time to go has long since passed
4764: for the young pilgrim. So at last
4765: Tatyana, hiding her condition,
4766: and not without a sigh, perforce
4767: sets out upon her homeward course;
4768: before she goes, she seeks permission
4769: to come back to the hall alone
4770: and read the books there on her own.
4771: XXI
4772: Outside the gate Tatyana parted
4773: with old Anisia. The next day
4774: at earliest morning out she started,
4775: to the empty homestead made her way,
4776: then in the study's quiet setting,
4777: at last alone, and quite forgetting
4778: the world and all its works, she wept
4779: and sat there as the minutes crept;
4780: the books then underwent inspection...
4781: at first she had no heart to range;
4782: but then she found their choice was strange.
4783: To reading from this odd collection
4784: Tatyana turned with thirsting soul:
4785: and watched a different world unroll.
4786: {187}
4787: XXII
4788: Though long since Eugene's disapproval
4789: had ruled out reading, in their place
4790: and still exempted from removal
4791: a few books had escaped disgrace:
4792: Don Juan's and the Giaour's creator,
4793: two or three novels where our later
4794: epoch's portrayed, survived the ban,
4795: works where contemporary man
4796: is represented rather truly,
4797: that soul without a moral tie,
4798: all egoistical and dry,
4799: to dreaming given up unduly,
4800: and that embittered mind which boils
4801: in empty deeds and futile toils.
4802: XXIII
4803: There many pages keep the impression
4804: where a sharp nail has made a dent.
4805: On these, with something like obsession,
4806: the girl's attentive eyes are bent.
4807: Tatyana sees with trepidation
4808: what kind of thought, what observation,
4809: had drawn Eugene's especial heed
4810: and where he'd silently agreed.
4811: Her eyes along the margin flitting
4812: pursue his pencil. Everywhere
4813: Onegin's soul encountered there
4814: declares itself in ways unwitting --
4815: terse words or crosses in the book,
4816: or else a query's wondering hook.
4817: {188}
4818: XXIV
4819: And so, at last, feature by feature,
4820: Tanya begins to understand
4821: more thoroughly, thank God, the creature
4822: for whom her passion has been planned
4823: by fate's decree: this freakish stranger,
4824: who walks with sorrow, and with danger,
4825: whether from heaven or from hell,
4826: this angel, this proud devil, tell,
4827: what is he? Just an apparition,
4828: a shadow, null and meaningless,
4829: a Muscovite in Harold's dress,
4830: a modish second-hand edition,
4831: a glossary of smart argot...
4832: a parodistic raree-show?
4833: XXV
4834: Can she have found the enigma's setting?
4835: is this the riddle's missing clue?
4836: Time races, and she's been forgetting
4837: her journey home is overdue.
4838: Some neighbours there have come together;
4839: they talk of her, of how and whether:
4840: ``Tanya's no child -- it's past a joke,''
4841: says the old lady in a croak:
4842: ``why, Olga's younger, and she's bedded.
4843: It's time she went. But what can I
4844: do with her when a flat reply
4845: always comes back: I'll not be wedded.
4846: And then she broods and mopes for good,
4847: and trails alone around the wood.''
4848: {189}
4849: XXVI
4850: ``She's not in love?'' ``There's no one, ever.
4851: Buyánov tried -- got flea in ear.
4852: And Ivan Petushkóv; no, never.
4853: Pikhtín, of the Hussars, was here;
4854: he found Tatyana so attractive,
4855: bestirred himself, was devilish active!
4856: I thought, she'll go this time, perhaps;
4857: far from it! just one more collapse.''
4858: ``You don't see what to do? that's funny:
4859: Moscow's the place, the marriage-fair!
4860: There's vacancies in plenty there.''
4861: ``My dear good sir, I'm short of money.''
4862: ``One winter's worth, you've surely got;
4863: or borrow, say, from me, if not.''
4864: XXVII
4865: The old dame had no thought of scouring
4866: such good and sensible advice;
4867: accounts were done, a winter outing
4868: to Moscow settled in a trice.
4869: Then Tanya hears of the decision.
4870: To face society's derision
4871: with the unmistakeable sideview
4872: of a provincial ingénue,
4873: to expose to Moscow fops and Circes
4874: her out-of-fashion turns of phrase,
4875: parade before their mocking gaze
4876: her out-of-fashion clothes!... oh, mercies!
4877: no, forests are the sole retreat
4878: where her security's complete.
4879: {190}
4880: XXVIII
4881: Risen with earliest rays of dawning,
4882: Tanya today goes hurrying out
4883: into the fields, surveys the morning,
4884: with deep emotion looks about
4885: and says: ``Farewell, you vales and fountains!
4886: farewell you too, familiar mountains!
4887: Farewell, familiar woods! Farewell,
4888: beauty with all its heavenly spell,
4889: gay nature and its sparkling distance!
4890: This dear, still world I must forswear
4891: for vanity, and din, and glare!...
4892: Farewell to you, my free existence!
4893: whither does all my yearning tend?
4894: my fate, it leads me to what end?''
4895: XXIX
4896: She wanders on without direction.
4897: Often she halts against her will,
4898: arrested by the sheer perfection
4899: she finds in river and in hill.
4900: As with old friends, she craves diversion
4901: in gossip's rambling and discursion
4902: with her own forests and her meads...
4903: But the swift summer-time proceeds --
4904: now golden autumn's just arriving.
4905: Now Nature's tremulous, pale effect
4906: suggests a victim richly decked...
4907: The north wind blows, the clouds are driving --
4908: amidst the howling and the blast
4909: sorceress-winter's here at last.
4910: {191}
4911: XXX
4912: She's here, she spreads abroad; she stipples
4913: the branches of the oak with flock;
4914: lies in a coverlet that ripples
4915: across the fields, round hill and rock;
4916: the bank, the immobile stream are levelled
4917: beneath a shroud that's all dishevelled;
4918: frost gleams. We watch with gleeful thanks
4919: old mother winter at her pranks.
4920: Only from Tanya's heart, no cheering --
4921: for her, no joy from winter-time,
4922: she won't inhale the powdered rime,
4923: nor from the bath-house roof be clearing
4924: first snow for shoulders, breast and head:
4925: for Tanya, winter's ways are dread.
4926: XXXI
4927: Departure date's long overtaken;
4928: at last the final hours arrive.
4929: A sledded coach, for years forsaken,
4930: relined and strengthened for the drive;
4931: three carts -- traditional procession --
4932: with every sort of home possession:
4933: pans, mattresses, and trunks, and chairs,
4934: and jam in jars, and household wares,
4935: and feather-beds, and birds in cages,
4936: with pots and basins out of mind,
4937: and useful goods of every kind.
4938: There's din of parting now that rages,
4939: with tears, in quarters of the maids:
4940: and, in the yard, stand eighteen jades.
4941: {192}
4942: XXXII
4943: Horses and coach are spliced in marriage;
4944: the cooks prepare the midday meal;
4945: mountains are piled on every carriage,
4946: and coachmen swear, and women squeal.
4947: The bearded outrider is sitting
4948: his spindly, shaggy nag. As fitting,
4949: to wave farewell the household waits
4950: for the two ladies at the gates.
4951: They're settled in; and crawling, sliding,
4952: the grand barouche is on its way.
4953: ``Farewell, you realms that own the sway
4954: of solitude, and peace abiding!
4955: shall I see you?'' As Tanya speaks
4956: the tears in stream pour down her cheeks.
4957: XXXIII
4958: When progress and amelioration
4959: have pushed their frontiers further out,
4960: in time (to quote the calculation
4961: of philosophic brains, about
4962: five hundred years) for sure our byways
4963: will blossom into splendid highways:
4964: paved roads will traverse Russia's length
4965: bringing her unity and strength;
4966: and iron bridges will go arching
4967: over the waters in a sweep;
4968: mountains will part; below the deep,
4969: audacious tunnels will be marching:
4970: Godfearing folk will institute
4971: an inn at each stage of the route.
4972: {193}
4973: XXXIV
4974: But now our roads are bad, the ages
4975: have gnawed our bridges, and the flea
4976: and bedbug that infest the stages
4977: allow no rest to you or me;
4978: inns don't exist; but in a freezing
4979: log cabin a pretentious-teasing
4980: menu, hung up for show, excites
4981: all sorts of hopeless appetites;
4982: meanwhile the local Cyclops, aiming
4983: a Russian hammer-blow, repairs
4984: Europe's most finely chiselled wares
4985: before a fire too slowly flaming,
4986: and blesses the unrivalled brand
4987: of ruts that grace our fatherland.
4988: XXXV
4989: By contrast, in the frozen season,
4990: how pleasantly the stages pass.
4991: Like modish rhymes that lack all reason,
4992: the winter's ways are smooth as glass.
4993: Then our Automedons are flashing,
4994: our troikas effortlessly dashing,
4995: and mileposts grip the idle sense
4996: by flickering past us like a fence.
4997: Worse luck, Larina crawled; the employment
4998: of her own horses, not the post,
4999: spared her the expense she dreaded most --
5000: and gave our heroine enjoyment
5001: of traveller's tedium at its peak:
5002: their journey took them a full week.
5003: {194}
5004: XXXVI
5005: But now they're near. Already gleaming
5006: before their eyes they see unfold
5007: the towers of whitestone Moscow beaming
5008: with fire from every cross of gold.
5009: Friends, how my heart would leap with pleasure
5010: when suddenly I saw this treasure
5011: of spires and belfries, in a cup
5012: with parks and mansions, open up.
5013: How often would I fall to musing
5014: of Moscow in the mournful days
5015: of absence on my wandering ways!
5016: Moscow... how many strains are fusing
5017: in that one sound, for Russian hearts!
5018: what store of riches it imparts!
5019: XXXVII
5020: Here stands, with shady park surrounded,
5021: Petrovsky Castle; and the fame
5022: in which so lately it abounded
5023: rings proudly in that sombre name.
5024: Napoleon here, intoxicated
5025: with recent fortune, vainly waited
5026: till Moscow, meekly on its knees,
5027: gave up the ancient Kremlin-keys:
5028: but no, my Moscow never stumbled
5029: nor crawled in suppliant attire.
5030: No feast, no welcome-gifts -- with fire
5031: the impatient conqueror was humbled!
5032: From here, deep-sunk in pensive woe,
5033: he gazed out on the threatening glow.
5034: {195}
5035: XXXVIII
5036: Farewell, Petrovsky Castle, glimmer
5037: of fallen glory. Well! don't wait,
5038: drive on! And now we see a-shimmer
5039: the pillars of the turnpike-gate;
5040: along Tverskaya Street already
5041: the potholes make the coach unsteady.
5042: Street lamps go flashing by, and stalls,
5043: boys, country women, stately halls,
5044: parks, monasteries, towers and ledges,
5045: Bokharans, orchards, merchants, shacks,
5046: boulevards, chemists, and Cossacks,
5047: peasants, and fashion-shops, and sledges,
5048: lions adorning gateway posts
5049: and, on the crosses, jackdaw hosts.
5050: (XXXIX,2) XL
5051: This wearisome perambulation
5052: takes up an hour or two; at last
5053: the coach has reached its destination;
5054: after Saint Chariton's gone past
5055: a mansion stands just round a turning.
5056: On an old aunt, who's long been burning
5057: with a consumption, they've relied.
5058: And now the door is opened wide,
5059: a grizzled Calmuck stands to meet them,
5060: bespectacled, in tattered dress;
5061: and from the salon the princess,
5062: stretched on a sofa, calls to greet them.
5063: The two old ladies kiss and cry;
5064: thickly the exclamations fly.
5065: {196}
5066: XLI
5067: ``Princess, mon ange!'' ``Pachette!'' ``Alina!''
5068: ``Who would have thought it?'' ``What an age!''
5069: ``How long can you... ?'' ``Dearest kuzina!''
5070: ``Sit down! how strange! it's like the stage
5071: or else a novel.'' ``And my daughter
5072: Tatyana's here, you know I've brought her...''
5073: ``Ah, Tanya, come to me, it seems
5074: I'm wandering in a world of dreams...
5075: Grandison, cousin, d'you remember?''
5076: ``What, Grandison? oh, Grandison!
5077: I do, I do. Well, where's he gone?''
5078: ``Here, near Saint Simeon; in December,
5079: on Christmas Eve, he wished me joy:
5080: lately he married off his boy.''
5081: XLII
5082: ``As for the other one... tomorrow
5083: we'll talk, and talk, and then we'll show
5084: Tanya to all her kin. My sorrow
5085: is that my feet lack strength to go
5086: outside the house. But you'll be aching
5087: after your drive, it's quite back-breaking;
5088: let's go together, take a rest...
5089: Oh, I've no strength... I'm tired, my chest...
5090: These days I'm finding even gladness,
5091: not only pain, too much to meet...
5092: I'm good for nothing now, my sweet...
5093: you age, and life's just grief and sadness...''
5094: With that, in tears, and quite worn out,
5095: she burst into a coughing-bout.
5096: {197}
5097: XLIII
5098: The invalid's glad salutation,
5099: her kindness, move Tatyana; yet
5100: the strangeness of her habitation,
5101: after her own room, makes her fret.
5102: No sleep, beneath that silken curtain,
5103: in that new couch, no sleep for certain;
5104: the early pealing of the bells
5105: lifts her from bed as it foretells
5106: the occupations of the morning.
5107: She sits down by the window-sill.
5108: The darkness thins away; but still
5109: no vision of her fields is dawning.
5110: An unknown yard, she sees from thence,
5111: a stall, a kitchen and a fence.
5112: XLIV
5113: The kinsfolk in concerted action
5114: ask Tanya out to dine, and they
5115: present her languor and distraction
5116: to fresh grandparents every day.
5117: For cousins from afar, on meeting
5118: there never fails a kindly greeting,
5119: and exclamations, and good cheer.
5120: ``How Tanya's grown! I pulled your ear
5121: just yesterday.'' ``And since your christening
5122: how long is it?'' ``And since I fed
5123: you in my arms on gingerbread?''
5124: And all grandmothers who are listening
5125: in unison repeat the cry:
5126: ``My goodness, how the years do fly!''
5127: {198}
5128: XLV
5129: Their look, though, shows no change upon it --
5130: they all still keep their old impress:
5131: still made of tulle, the self-same bonnet
5132: adorns Aunt Helen, the princess;
5133: still powdered is Lukérya Lvovna,
5134: a liar still, Lyubóv Petrovna,
5135: Iván Petróvich still is dumb,
5136: Semyón Petróvich, mean and glum,
5137: and then old cousin Pelagéya
5138: still has Monsieur Finemouche for friend,
5139: same Pom, same husband to the end;
5140: he's at the club, a real stayer,
5141: still meek, still deaf as howd'youdo,
5142: still eats and drinks enough for two.
5143: XLVI
5144: And in their daughters' close embraces
5145: Tanya is gripped. No comment's made
5146: at first by Moscow's youthful graces
5147: while she's from top to toe surveyed;
5148: they find her somewhat unexpected,
5149: a bit provincial and affected,
5150: too pale, too thin, but on the whole
5151: not bad at all; and then each soul
5152: gives way to nature's normal passion:
5153: she's their great friend, asked in, caressed,
5154: her hands affectionately pressed;
5155: they fluff her curls out in the fashion,
5156: and in a singsong voice confide
5157: the inmost thoughts that girls can hide.
5158: {199}
5159: XLVII
5160: Each others' and their own successes,
5161: their hopes, their pranks, their dreams at night --
5162: and so the harmless chat progresses
5163: coated with a thin layer of spite.
5164: Then in return for all this twaddle,
5165: from her they strive to coax and coddle
5166: a full confession of the heart.
5167: Tatyana hears but takes no part;
5168: as if she'd been profoundly sleeping,
5169: there's not a word she's understood;
5170: she guards, in silence and for good,
5171: her sacred store of bliss and weeping
5172: as something not to be declared,
5173: a treasure never to be shared.
5174: XLVIII
5175: To talk, to general conversation
5176: Tatyana seeks to attune her ear,
5177: but the salon's preoccupation
5178: is with dull trash that can't cohere:
5179: everything's dim and unenthusing;
5180: even the scandal's not amusing;
5181: in talk, so fruitless and so stale,
5182: in question, gossip, news and tale,
5183: not once a day a thought will quiver,
5184: not even by chance, once in a while,
5185: will the benighted reason smile,
5186: even in joke the heart won't shiver.
5187: This world's so vacuous that it's got
5188: no spark of fun in all its rot!
5189: {200}
5190: XLIX
5191: In swarms around Tatyana ranging,
5192: the modish Record Office clerks
5193: stare hard at her before exchanging
5194: some disagreeable remarks.
5195: One melancholy fop, declaring
5196: that she's ``ideal'', begins preparing
5197: an elegy to her address,
5198: propped in the door among the press.
5199: Once Vyázemsky,4 who chanced to find her
5200: at some dull aunt's, sat down and knew
5201: how to engage in talk that drew
5202: her soul's attention; just behind her
5203: an old man saw her as she came,
5204: straightened his wig, and asked her name.
5205: L
5206: But where, mid tragic storms that rend her,
5207: Melpomene wails long and loud,
5208: and brandishes her tinsel splendour
5209: before a cold, indifferent crowd,
5210: and where Thalia, gently napping,
5211: ignores approval's friendly clapping,
5212: and where Terpsichore alone
5213: moves the young watcher (as was known
5214: to happen long ago, dear readers,
5215: in our first ages), from no place
5216: did any glasses seek her face,
5217: lorgnettes of jealous fashion-leaders,
5218: or quizzing-glasses of know-alls
5219: in boxes or the rows of stalls.
5220: {201}
5221: LI
5222: They take her too to the Assembly.
5223: The crush, the heat, as music blares,
5224: the blaze of candles, and the trembly
5225: flicker of swiftly twirling pairs,
5226: the beauties in their flimsy dresses,
5227: the swarm, the glittering mob that presses,
5228: the ring of marriageable girls --
5229: bludgeon the sense; it faints and whirls.
5230: Here insolent prize-dandies wither
5231: all others with a waistcoat's set
5232: and an insouciant lorgnette.
5233: Hussars on leave are racing hither
5234: to boom, to flash across the sky,
5235: to captivate, and then to fly.
5236: LII
5237: The night has many stars that glitter,
5238: Moscow has beauties and to spare:
5239: but brighter than the heavenly litter,
5240: the moon in its azure of air.
5241: And yet that goddess whom I'd never
5242: importune with my lyre, whenever
5243: like a majestic moon, she drives
5244: among the maidens and the wives,
5245: how proudly, how divinely gleaming,
5246: she treads our earth, and how her breast
5247: is in voluptuous languor dressed,
5248: how sensuously her eyes are dreaming!
5249: Enough, I tell you, that will do --
5250: you've paid insanity its due.
5251: {202}
5252: LIII
5253: Noise, laughter, bowing, helter-skelter
5254: galop, mazurka, waltz... Meanwhile
5255: between two aunts, in pillared shelter,
5256: unnoticed, in unseeing style,
5257: Tanya looks on; her own indictment
5258: condemns the monde and its excitement;
5259: she finds it stifling here... she strains
5260: in dream toward the woods and plains,
5261: the country cottages and hovels,
5262: and to that far and lonely nook
5263: where flows a little glittering brook,
5264: to her flower-garden, to her novels, --
5265: to where he came to her that time
5266: in twilight of allées of lime.
5267: LIV
5268: But while she roams in thought, not caring
5269: for dance, and din, and worldly ways,
5270: a general of majestic bearing
5271: has fixed on her a steady gaze.
5272: The aunts exchanged a look, they fluttered,
5273: they nudged Tatyana, and each muttered
5274: at the same moment in her ear:
5275: ``Look quickly to the left, d'you hear?''
5276: ``Look to the left? where? what's the matter?''
5277: ``There, just in front of all that swarm,
5278: you see the two in uniform...
5279: just look, and never mind the chatter...
5280: he's moved... you see him from the side.''
5281: ``Who? that fat general?'' Tanya cried.
5282: {203}
5283: LV
5284: But here, with our congratulation
5285: on her conquest, we leave my sweet;
5286: I'm altering my destination
5287: lest in forgetfulness complete
5288: I drop my hero... I'll be truthful:
5289: ``It is a friend I sing, a youthful
5290: amateur of caprice and quirk.
5291: Muse of the epic, bless my work!
5292: in my long task, be my upholder,
5293: put a strong staff into my hand,
5294: don't let me stray in paths unplanned.''
5295: Enough. The load is off my shoulder!
5296: I've paid my due to classic art:
5297: it may be late, but it's a start.
5298: {204}
5299: Notes to Chapter Seven
5300: 1 Vasily Levshin (1746-1826), writer on gardening and agriculture.
5301: 2 Stanzas VIII and IX and XXXIX were discarded by Pushkin.
5302: 3 A statuette of Napoleon.
5303: 4 See note 1 to Chapter Five.
5304: --------
5305: Chapter Eight
5306: Fare thee well, and if for ever,
5307: Still for ever, fare thee well.
5308: Byron
5309: Days when I came to flower serenely
5310: in Lycée gardens long ago,
5311: and read my Apuleius keenly,
5312: but spared no glance for Cicero;
5313: yes, in that spring-time, in low-lying
5314: secluded vales, where swans were crying,
5315: by waters that were still and clear,
5316: for the first time the Muse came near.
5317: And suddenly her radiance lighted
5318: my student cell: she opened up
5319: the joys of youth, that festal cup,
5320: she sang of childhood's fun, indited
5321: Russia's old glories and their gleams,
5322: the heart and all its fragile dreams.
5323: {205}
5324: II
5325: And with a smile the world caressed us:
5326: what wings our first successes gave!
5327: aged Derzhávin1 saw and blessed us
5328: as he descended to the grave.
5329: ... ...
5330: III
5331: The arbitrary rules of passion
5332: were all the law that I would use;
5333: sharing her in promiscuous fashion,
5334: I introduced my saucy Muse
5335: to roar of banquets, din of brawling,
5336: when night patrol's a perilous calling;
5337: to each and every raving feast
5338: she brought her talents, never ceased,
5339: Bacchante-like, her flighty prancing;
5340: sang for the guests above the wine;
5341: the youth of those past days in line
5342: behind her followed wildly dancing;
5343: among my friends, in all that crowd
5344: my giddy mistress made me proud.
5345: {206}
5346: IV
5347: When I defected from their union
5348: and ran far off... the Muse came too.
5349: How often, with her sweet communion,
5350: she'd cheer my wordless way, and do
5351: her secret work of magic suasion!
5352: How often on the steep Caucasian
5353: ranges, Lenora2-like, she'd ride
5354: breakneck by moonlight at my side!
5355: How oft she'd lead me, by the Tauric
5356: seacoast, to hear in dark of night
5357: the murmuring Nereids recite,
5358: and the deep-throated billows' choric
5359: hymnal as, endlessly unfurled,
5360: they praise the Father of the world.
5361: V
5362: But then, oblivious of the city,
5363: its glaring feasts, and shrill events,
5364: in far Moldavia, fit for pity,
5365: she visited the humble tents
5366: of wandering tribesmen; while the ravage
5367: of their society turned her savage,
5368: she lost the language of the gods
5369: for the bleak tongue of boorish clods --
5370: she loved the steppe-land and its singing,
5371: then quickly something changed all this:
5372: look here, as a provincial miss
5373: she's turned up in my garden, bringing
5374: sad meditations in her look,
5375: and, in her hand, a small French book.
5376: {207}
5377: VI
5378: Now for the first time she's escorted
5379: into the social whirlabout;
5380: jealously, shyly, I've imported
5381: her steppeland charms into a rout.3
5382: Through the tight ranks -- aristocratic,
5383: military-foppish, diplomatic --
5384: past the grand ladies, see her glide;
5385: she sits down calmly on one side,
5386: admires the tumult and the pressing,
5387: the flickering tones of dress and speech,
5388: the young hostess, towards whom each
5389: new guest is gradually progressing,
5390: while men, all sombre, all the same,
5391: set off the ladies like a frame.
5392: VII
5393: She enjoys the stately orchestration
5394: of oligarchical converse,
5395: pride's icy calm, the combination
5396: of ranks and ages so diverse.
5397: But who stands there, in this selected
5398: assembly, silent and dejected?
5399: All who behold him find him strange.
5400: Faces before him flash and change
5401: like irksome phantoms, null as zero.
5402: Is spleen his trouble, or the dumb
5403: torment of pride? And why's he come?
5404: Who on earth is he? not... our hero?
5405: No doubt about it, it's Eugene.
5406: ``How long has he been on the scene?
5407: {208}
5408: VIII
5409: Still as he was? has he stopped prancing?
5410: does he still pose, and play the freak?
5411: Now he's returned, what role's he dancing?
5412: what play will he present this week?
5413: For what charade is he apparelled?
5414: Is he a Melmoth, a Childe Harold,
5415: a patriot, a cosmopolite,
5416: bigot or prude? or has he quite
5417: a different mask? is he becoming
5418: someone like you and me, just nice?
5419: At least I'll give him some advice:
5420: to drop all that old-fashioned mumming;
5421: too long he's hoaxed us high and low...''
5422: ``You know him, do you?'' ``Yes and no.''
5423: IX
5424: However has he earned so vicious,
5425: so unforgiving a report?
5426: Is it that we've become officious
5427: and prone to censure in our thought;
5428: that fiery souls' headstrong enthusing
5429: appears offensive or amusing
5430: to the complacent and the null;
5431: that wit embarrasses the dull;
5432: that we enjoy equating chatter
5433: with deeds; that dunces now and then
5434: take wing on spite; that serious men
5435: find, in the trivial, serious matter;
5436: that mediocre dress alone
5437: fits us as if it were our own?
5438: {209}
5439: X
5440: Blest he who in his youth was truly
5441: youthful, who ripened in his time,
5442: and, as the years went by, who duly
5443: grew hardened to life's frosty clime;
5444: who never learnt how dreamers babble;
5445: who never scorned the social rabble;
5446: at twenty, was a fop inbred,
5447: at thirty, lucratively wed;
5448: at fifty, would prolong the story
5449: by clearing every sort of debt;
5450: who, in good time, would calmly get
5451: fortune, and dignity, and glory,
5452: who all his life would garner praise
5453: as the perfection of our days!
5454: XI
5455: Alas, our youth was what we made it,
5456: something to fritter and to burn,
5457: when hourly we ourselves betrayed it,
5458: and it deceived us in return;
5459: when our sublimest aspiration,
5460: and all our fresh imagination,
5461: swiftly decayed beyond recall
5462: like foliage in the rotting fall.
5463: It's agony to watch the hollow
5464: sequence of dinners stretch away,
5465: to see life as a ritual play,
5466: and with the decorous throng to follow
5467: although one in no manner shares
5468: its views, its passions, or its cares!
5469: {210}
5470: XII
5471: To be a butt for the malicious
5472: is agony, if I may speak,
5473: and in the eyes of the judicious
5474: to pass for an affected freak,
5475: or for a lamentable manic,
5476: a monster of the gens Satanic,
5477: or for that Demon4 of my dream.
5478: Onegin -- now once more my theme --
5479: had killed his best friend in a duel;
5480: without a goal on which to fix,
5481: lived to the age of twenty-six;
5482: was finding leisure's vacuum cruel;
5483: and with no post, no work, no wife,
5484: had nothing to employ his life.
5485: XIII
5486: He was the slave of a tenacious,
5487: a restless urge for change of place
5488: (an attribute that's quite vexatious,
5489: though some support it with good grace).
5490: He's gone away and left his village,
5491: the solitude of woods and tillage,
5492: where every day a bloodstained shade
5493: had come to him in field and glade;
5494: started a life of pointless roaming,
5495: dogged by one feeling, only one --
5496: and soon his travels had begun,
5497: as all things did, to bore him; homing,
5498: like Chatsky,5 he arrived to fall
5499: direct from shipboard into ball.
5500: {211}
5501: XIV
5502: There came a murmur, for a fleeting
5503: moment the assembly seemed to shake...
5504: that lady the hostess was greeting,
5505: with the grand general in her wake --
5506: she was unhurried, unobtrusive,
5507: not cold, but also not effusive,
5508: no haughty stare around the press,
5509: no proud pretentions to success,
5510: no mannerism, no affectation,
5511: no artifices of the vain...
5512: No, all in her was calm and plain.
5513: She struck one as the incarnation --
5514: Shishkov,6 forgive me: I don't know
5515: the Russian for le comme il faut.
5516: XV
5517: Ladies came over, crossed to meet her,
5518: dowagers smiled as she went by;
5519: and bending deeply down to greet her
5520: men made their bows, and sought her eye;
5521: girls as they passed her spoke less loudly,
5522: and no one in the room so proudly
5523: raised nose and shoulders high and wide
5524: as did the general at her side.
5525: You'd never class her as a beauty;
5526: and yet in her you'd not detect --
5527: rigorously though you'd inspect --
5528: what London calls, with humble duty
5529: to fashion's absolute dictate,
5530: a vulgar touch. I can't translate.
5531: {212}
5532: XVI
5533: And yet, although it's past conveying,
5534: I really dote upon the word:
5535: it's new to us, beyond gainsaying;
5536: from the first moment it was heard
5537: it had its epigram-potential7...
5538: But let's return to our essential,
5539: that lady whose engaging charm
5540: so effortlessly can disarm.
5541: She sits with Nina8 at a table --
5542: bright Northern Cleopatra she:
5543: but you'll undoubtedly agree
5544: that marble Nina's proved unable
5545: to steal away her neighbour's light
5546: or dim her, dazzle as she might.
5547: XVII
5548: ``Can it be she?'' Eugene in wonder
5549: demanded. ``Yes, she looks... And yet...
5550: from deepest backwood, furthest under...''
5551: And every minute his lorgnette
5552: stays fixed and focused on a vision
5553: which has recalled, without precision,
5554: forgotten features. ``Can you say,
5555: prince, who in that dark-red béret,
5556: just there, is talking to the Spanish
5557: ambassador?'' In some surprise
5558: the prince looks at him, and replies:
5559: ``Wait, I'll present you -- but you banish
5560: yourself too long from social life.''
5561: ``But tell me who she is.'' ``My wife.''
5562: {213}
5563: XVIII
5564: ``You're married? No idea whatever...
5565: Since when is this?'' ``Two years or more.''
5566: ``To...?'' ``Larina.'' ``Tatyana? never!''
5567: ``She knows you?'' ``Why, we lived next door.''
5568: So to his wife for presentation
5569: the prince bring up his own relation
5570: and friend Evgeny. The princess
5571: gazes at him... and nonetheless,
5572: however much her soul has faltered,
5573: however strongly she has been
5574: moved and surprised, she stays serene,
5575: and nothing in her look is altered:
5576: her manner is no less contained;
5577: her bow, as calm and as restrained.
5578: XIX
5579: I don't mean that she never shivered,
5580: paled, flushed, or lost composure's grip --
5581: no, even her eyebrow never quivered,
5582: she never even bit her lip.
5583: However closely he inspected,
5584: there was no trace to be detected
5585: of the old Tatyana. Eugene tried
5586: to talk to her, but language died.
5587: How long he'd been here, was her query,
5588: and where had he arrived from, not
5589: from their own country? Then she shot
5590: across to her consort a weary
5591: regard, and slipped away for good, ...
5592: with Eugene frozen where he stood.
5593: {214}
5594: XX
5595: Was she the Tanya he'd exhorted
5596: in solitude, as at the start
5597: of this our novel we reported,
5598: in the far backwoods' deepest heart,
5599: to whom, in a fine flow of preaching,
5600: he had conveyed some moral teaching,
5601: from whom he'd kept a letter, where
5602: her heart had spoken, free as air,
5603: untouched by trace of inhibition,
5604: could it be she... or had he dreamed?
5605: the girl he'd scorned in what he deemed
5606: the modesty of her condition,
5607: could it be she, who just had turned
5608: away, so cool, so unconcerned?
5609: XXI
5610: Eugene forsakes the packed reception,
5611: and home he drives, deep-sunk in thought.
5612: By dreams now sad in their conception,
5613: now sweet, his slumbers are distraught.
5614: He wakes -- and who is this who writes him?
5615: Prince N. respectfully invites him
5616: to a soirée. ``My God! to her!...
5617: I'll go, I'll go!'' -- and in a stir
5618: a swift, polite reply is written.
5619: What ails him? he's in some strange daze!
5620: what moves along the hidden ways
5621: in one so slothful, so hard-bitten?
5622: vexation? vainness? heavens above,
5623: it can't be youth's distemper -- love?
5624: {215}
5625: XXII
5626: Once more he counts the hour-bells tolling,
5627: once more he can't await the night;
5628: now ten has struck, his wheels are rolling,
5629: he drives there like a bird in flight,
5630: he's up the steps, with heart a-quiver
5631: led to the princess, all a-shiver,
5632: finds her alone, and there they sit
5633: some minutes long. The words won't fit
5634: on Eugene's lips. In his dejection,
5635: his awkwardness, he's hardly said
5636: a single thing to her. His head
5637: is lost in obstinate reflection;
5638: and obstinate his look. But she
5639: sits imperturbable, and free.
5640: XXIII
5641: Her husband enters, thus concluding
5642: their unattractive tête-à-tête;
5643: he and Onegin start alluding
5644: to pranks and jokes of earlier date.
5645: They laugh. The guests begin arriving.
5646: Already now the talk was thriving
5647: on modish malice, coarse of grain
5648: but salt; near the princess a vein
5649: of unaffectedly fantastic
5650: invention sparkled, then gave way
5651: to reasoned talk, no dull hearsay,
5652: no deathless truths, nothing scholastic;
5653: and no one's ear could take offence
5654: at such vivacious, free good sense.
5655: {216}
5656: XXIV
5657: High rank, of course, and fashion's glasses,
5658: Saint Petersburg's fine flower was there --
5659: the inevitable silly asses,
5660: the faces met with everywhere;
5661: ladies of riper years, delicious
5662: in rose-trimmed bonnets, but malicious;
5663: a girl or two, without a smile
5664: to crack between them; for a while
5665: one listened to a chief of mission
5666: on state affairs; there was a wit,
5667: a grey-haired, perfumed exquisite,
5668: a joker in the old tradition,
5669: acute and subtle -- in a word
5670: all that today we find absurd.
5671: XXV
5672: There, with epigrammatic neatness,
5673: was one who raged and raged again,
5674: against the tea's excessive sweetness,
5675: the boring wives, the ill-bred men,
5676: a novel, vague and superficial,
5677: two sisters who'd received the initial,9
5678: the lies that in the press run rife,
5679: the war, the snowfall, and his wife.
5680: ... ...
5681: {217}
5682: XXVI
5683: There was -- --,10 so notorious
5684: through baseness of the soul that he,
5685: in albums, blunted the censorious
5686: cartoonist-pencils of Saint-Priest;11
5687: another of the ball-dictators,
5688: a fashion-plate for illustrators,
5689: stood in the door, cherubic, mute,
5690: frozen in his tight-fitting suit;
5691: a far-flung traveller who was creaking
5692: with foppery and too much starch,
5693: set the guests smiling at his arch,
5694: affected pose -- and an unspeaking
5695: unanimous exchange of looks
5696: entered his sentence in the books.
5697: XXVII
5698: But my Eugene that night directed
5699: his gaze at Tatyana alone --
5700: not the plain, timorous, dejected
5701: and lovelorn maiden whom he'd known,
5702: but the unbending goddess-daughter
5703: of Neva's proud imperial water,
5704: the imperturbable princess.
5705: We all resemble more or less
5706: our Mother Eve: we're never falling
5707: for what's been given us to take;
5708: to his mysterious tree the snake
5709: is calling us, for ever calling --
5710: and once forbidden fruit is seen,
5711: no paradise can stay serene.
5712: {218}
5713: XXVIII
5714: In Tanya, what a transformation!
5715: how well she'd studied her new role!
5716: how soon the bounds of rank and station
5717: had won her loyalty! What soul
5718: would have divined the tender, shrinking
5719: maiden in this superb, unthinking
5720: lawgiver to the modish world?
5721: Yet once for him her thoughts had whirled,
5722: for him, at night, before the indulgence
5723: of Morpheus had induced relief
5724: she once had pined in girlish grief,
5725: raised a dull eye to moon's refulgence,
5726: and dreamt that she with him one day
5727: jointly would tread life's humble way!
5728: XXIX
5729: Love tyrannises all the ages;
5730: but youthful, virgin hearts derive
5731: a blessing from its blasts and rages,
5732: like fields in spring when storms arrive.
5733: In passion's sluicing rain they freshen,
5734: ripen, and find a new expression --
5735: the vital force gives them the shoot
5736: of sumptuous flowers and luscious fruit.
5737: But when a later age has found us,
5738: the climacteric of our life,
5739: how sad the scar of passion's knife:
5740: as when chill autumn rains surround us,
5741: throw meadows into muddy rout,
5742: and strip the forest round about.
5743: {219}
5744: XXX
5745: Alas, Eugene beyond all query
5746: is deep in love, just like a boy;
5747: spends light and darkness in the dreary
5748: brooding that is the lover's ploy.
5749: Each day, despite the appeals of reason,
5750: he drives up in and out of season
5751: to her glass porch; pursues her round
5752: close as a shadow on the ground;
5753: and bliss for him is when he hotly
5754: touches her hand, or throws a fur
5755: around her neck, or when for her
5756: he goes ahead and parts the motley
5757: brigade of liveries in the hall,
5758: or else lifts up a fallen shawl.
5759: XXXI
5760: But she refuses to perceive him,
5761: even if he drops or pines away.
5762: At home she'll equably receive him,
5763: in others' houses she may say
5764: a word or two, or stare unseeing,
5765: or simply bow: within her being
5766: coquettishness has got no trace --
5767: the grand monde finds it out of place.
5768: Meanwhile Onegin starts to languish:
5769: she doesn't see, or doesn't mind;
5770: Onegin wastes, you'd almost find
5771: he's got consumption. In his anguish
5772: some vote a doctor for the case,
5773: others prescribe a watering-place.
5774: {220}
5775: XXXII
5776: But go he won't: for him, a letter
5777: fixing an early rendezvous
5778: with his forefathers would seem better;
5779: but she (for women, that's not new)
5780: remains unmoved: still he's persistent,
5781: active, and hopeful, and insistent:
5782: his illness lends him courage and
5783: to the princess, in his weak hand,
5784: he sends a letter, penned with passion.
5785: He deemed, in general, letters vain,
5786: and rightly so, but now his pain
5787: had gone in no uncertain fashion
5788: past all endurance. You're referred
5789: to Eugene's letter, word for word.
5790: {221}
5791: Onegin's Letter to Tatyana
5792: ``I know it all: my secret ache
5793: will anger you in its confession.
5794: What scorn I see in the expression
5795: that your proud glance is sure to take!
5796: What do I want? what am I after,
5797: stripping my soul before your eyes!
5798: I know to what malicious laughter
5799: my declaration may give rise!
5800: ``I noticed once, at our chance meeting,
5801: in you a tender pulse was beating,
5802: yet dared not trust what I could see.
5803: I gave no rein to sweet affection:
5804: what held me was my predilection,
5805: my tedious taste for feeling free.
5806: And then, to part us in full measure,
5807: Lensky, that tragic victim, died...
5808: From all sweet things that gave me pleasure,
5809: since then my heart was wrenched aside;
5810: freedom and peace, in substitution
5811: for happiness, I sought, and ranged
5812: unloved, and friendless, and estranged.
5813: What folly! and what retribution!
5814: ``No, every minute of my days,
5815: to see you, faithfully to follow,
5816: watch for your smile, and catch your gaze
5817: with eyes of love, with greed to swallow
5818: your words, and in my soul to explore
5819: your matchlessness, to seek to capture
5820: its image, then to swoon before
5821: your feet, to pale and waste... what rapture!
5822: {222}
5823: ``But I'm denied this: all for you
5824: I drag my footsteps hither, yonder;
5825: I count each hour the whole day through;
5826: and yet in vain ennui I squander
5827: the days that doom has measured out.
5828: And how they weigh! I know about
5829: my span, that fortune's jurisdiction
5830: has fixed; but for my heart to beat
5831: I must wake up with the conviction
5832: that somehow that same day we'll meet...
5833: ``I dread your stern regard surmising
5834: in my petition an approach,
5835: a calculation past despising --
5836: I hear the wrath of your reproach.
5837: How fearful, in and out of season
5838: to pine away from passion's thirst,
5839: to burn -- and then by force of reason
5840: to stem the bloodstream's wild outburst;
5841: how fearful, too, is my obsession
5842: to clasp your knees, and at your feet
5843: to sob out prayer, complaint, confession,
5844: and every plea that lips can treat;
5845: meanwhile with a dissembler's duty
5846: to cool my glances and my tongue,
5847: to talk as if with heart unwrung,
5848: and look serenely on your beauty!...
5849: ``But so it is: I'm in no state
5850: to battle further with my passion;
5851: I'm yours, in a predestined fashion,
5852: and I surrender to my fate.''
5853: {223}
5854: XXXIII
5855: No answer comes. Another letter
5856: he sends, a second, then a third.
5857: No answer comes. He goes, for better
5858: or worse, to a soirée. Unheard
5859: she appears before him, grim and frozen.
5860: No look, no word for him: she's chosen
5861: to encase herself inside a layer
5862: of Twelfth Night's chillest, iciest air.
5863: To batten down their indignation
5864: is all those stubborn lips desire!
5865: Onegin looks with eyes of fire:
5866: where are distress, commiseration?
5867: No tearstains, nothing. Wrath alone
5868: is graven on that face of stone.
5869: XXXIV
5870: Perhaps some secret apprehension
5871: lest signs of casual weakness drew
5872: her husband's or the world's attention...
5873: Ah, all that my Onegin knew...
5874: No hope! no hope! He leaves the revel,
5875: wishes his madness to the devil,
5876: drives home -- and plunging deeper in,
5877: once more renounces world and din.
5878: And he remembers, in the quiet
5879: of his own room, how cruel spleen
5880: had once before, across the scene
5881: of social buzz and modish riot,
5882: tracked him, and put him in duress,
5883: and locked him in a dark recess.
5884: {224}
5885: XXXV
5886: Once more he turned to books, unchoosing,
5887: devouring Gibbon and Rousseau,
5888: Manzoni and Chamfort,12 perusing
5889: Madame de Staël, Bichat,13 Tissot,14
5890: Herder, and even at times a Russian --
5891: nothing was barred beyond discussion --
5892: he read of course the sceptic Bayle15
5893: and all the works of Fontanelle16 --
5894: almanacs, journals of reflection,
5895: where admonitions are pronounced,
5896: where nowadays I'm soundly trounced,
5897: but where such hymns in my direction
5898: were chanted, I remember when --
5899: e sempre bene, gentlemen.
5900: XXXVI
5901: What happened? Though his eyes were reading,
5902: his thoughts were on a distant goal:
5903: desires and dreams and griefs were breeding
5904: and swarming in his inmost soul.
5905: Between the lines of text as printed,
5906: his mind's eye focused on the hinted
5907: purport of other lines; intense
5908: was his absorption in their sense.
5909: Legends, and mystical traditions,
5910: drawn from a dim, warm-hearted past,
5911: dreams of inconsequential cast,
5912: rumours and threats and premonitions,
5913: long, lively tales from wonderland,
5914: or letters in a young girl's hand.
5915: {225}
5916: XXXVII
5917: Then gradually upon sensation,
5918: and thought, a sleepy numbness steals;
5919: before his eyes, imagination
5920: brings out its faro pack, and deals.
5921: He sees: in slush, stretched out and keeping
5922: motionless as one soundly sleeping
5923: in bed, a young man, stiff and chilled;
5924: he hears a voice; ``well, what? he's killed!''
5925: And foes he sees, long-since forgotten,
5926: a rogue, a slanderer, a poltroon,
5927: young traitresses by the platoon,
5928: comrades despised, and comrades rotten;
5929: a country house -- and one who still
5930: sits there beside the window-sill!
5931: XXXVIII
5932: He got so used to this immersion,
5933: he almost lost his mind, expired,
5934: or joined us poets. His conversion
5935: would have been all that we required!
5936: It's true, the magnet-like attraction
5937: of Russian verse, its force in action, --
5938: my inept pupil, at that hour,
5939: so nearly had them in his power.
5940: Who could have looked the poet better,
5941: as in the nook he'd sit alone
5942: by blazing fireplace, and intone
5943: Idol mio or Benedetta,
5944: and on the flames let fall unseen
5945: a slipper, or a magazine?
5946: {226}
5947: XXXIX
5948: The days flew past; by now the season
5949: in warmer airs was half dispersed.
5950: He's neither died, nor lost his reason,
5951: nor turned a poet. In the burst
5952: of spring he lives, he's energetic;
5953: he leaves one morning the hermetic
5954: apartment where a double glaze
5955: has kept him warm in chimney's blaze
5956: while, marmot-like, he hibernated --
5957: along the Neva in a sleigh,
5958: past ice-blocks, blue and squared away,
5959: he drives in brilliant sun; striated
5960: along the street lies dirty snow;
5961: and like an arrow from a bow
5962: XL
5963: over the slush, where is he chasing?
5964: You've guessed before it all began:
5965: to his Tatyana, yes, he's racing,
5966: my strange, incorrigible man.
5967: He goes inside, corpse-like of feature...
5968: the hall's without a living creature,
5969: the big room, further, not a cat.
5970: He opens up a door. What's that
5971: that strikes him with such force and meaning?
5972: The princess, sitting peaked and wan,
5973: alone, with no adornment on;
5974: she holds a letter up, and leaning
5975: cheek upon hand she softly cries
5976: in a still stream that never dries.
5977: {227}
5978: XLI
5979: Who in that flash could not have reckoned
5980: her full account of voiceless pain?
5981: Who in the princess for that second
5982: would not have recognized again
5983: our hapless Tanya! An emotion
5984: of wild repentance and devotion
5985: threw Eugene at her feet -- she stirred,
5986: and looked at him without a word,
5987: without surprise or rage... his laden,
5988: his humbly suppliant approach,
5989: his dull, sick look, his dumb reproach --
5990: she sees it all. The simple maiden,
5991: whose heart on dreams was wont to thrive,
5992: in her once more has come alive.
5993: XLII
5994: Tatyana leaves Onegin kneeling,
5995: looks at him with a steady gaze,
5996: allows her hand, that's lost all feeling,
5997: to meet his thirsty lips... What daze,
5998: what dream accounts for her distraction?
5999: A pause of silence and inaction,
6000: then quietly at last says she:
6001: ``Enough, stand up. It's now for me
6002: to give you honest explanation.
6003: Onegin, d'you recall the day
6004: when in the park, in the allée
6005: where fate had fixed our confrontation,
6006: humbly I heard your lesson out?
6007: Today it's turn and turn about.
6008: {228}
6009: XLIII
6010: ``For then, Onegin, I was younger,
6011: and also prettier, I'll be bound,
6012: what's more, I loved you; but my hunger,
6013: what was it in your heart it found
6014: that could sustain it? Only grimness;
6015: for you, I think, the humble dimness
6016: of lovelorn girls was nothing new?
6017: But now -- oh God! -- the thought of you,
6018: your icy look, your stern dissuasion,
6019: freezes my blood... Yet all the same,
6020: nothing you did gave cause for blame:
6021: you acted well, that dread occasion,
6022: you took an honourable part --
6023: I'm grateful now with all my heart.
6024: XLIV
6025: ``Then, in the backwoods, far from rumour
6026: and empty gossip, you'll allow,
6027: I'd nothing to attract your humour...
6028: Why then do you pursue me now?
6029: What cause has won me your attention?
6030: Could it not be that by convention
6031: I move in the grand monde? that rank,
6032: and riches, and the wish to thank
6033: my husband for his wounds in battle
6034: earn us the favour of the Court?
6035: that, for all this, my shame's report
6036: would cause widespread remark and tattle,
6037: and so in the salons could make
6038: a tempting plume for you to take?
6039: {229}
6040: XLV
6041: ``I weep... In case there still should linger
6042: your Tanya's image in your mind,
6043: then know that your reproving finger,
6044: your cold discourse, were less unkind --
6045: if I had power to choose your fashion --
6046: than this humiliating passion
6047: and than these letters, and these tears.
6048: At least you then showed for my years
6049: respect, and mercy for my dreaming.
6050: But now! what brings you to my feet?
6051: What trifling could be more complete?
6052: What power enslaves you, with your seeming
6053: advantages of heart and brain,
6054: to all that's trivial and inane?
6055: XLVI
6056: ``To me, Onegin, all this glory
6057: is tinsel on a life I hate;
6058: this modish whirl, this social story,
6059: my house, my evenings, all that state --
6060: what's in them? All this loud parading,
6061: and all this flashy masquerading,
6062: the glare, the fumes in which I live,
6063: this very day I'd gladly give,
6064: give for a bookshelf, a neglected
6065: garden, a modest home, the place
6066: of our first meeting face to face,
6067: and the churchyard where, new-erected,
6068: a humble cross, in woodland gloom,
6069: stands over my poor nurse's tomb.
6070: {230}
6071: XLVII
6072: ``Bliss was so near, so altogether
6073: attainable!... But now my lot
6074: is firmly cast. I don't know whether
6075: I acted thoughtlessly or not:
6076: you see, with tears and incantation
6077: mother implored me; my sad station
6078: made all fates look the same... and so
6079: I married. I beseech you, go;
6080: I know your heart: it has a feeling
6081: for honour, a straightforward pride.
6082: I love you (what's the use to hide
6083: behind deceit or double-dealing?)
6084: but I've become another's wife --
6085: and I'll be true to him, for life.''
6086: XLVIII
6087: She went -- and Eugene, all emotion,
6088: stood thunder-struck. In what wild round
6089: of tempests, in what raging ocean
6090: his heart was plunged! A sudden sound,
6091: the clink of rowels, met his hearing;
6092: Tatyana's husband, now appearing...
6093: But from the hero of my tale,
6094: just at this crisis of his gale,
6095: reader, we must be separating,
6096: for long... for evermore. We've chased
6097: him far enough through wild and waste.
6098: Hurrah! let's start congratulating
6099: ourselves on our landfall. It's true,
6100: our vessel's long been overdue.
6101: {231}
6102: XLIX
6103: Reader, I wish that, as we parted --
6104: whoever you may be, a friend,
6105: a foe -- our mood should be warm-hearted.
6106: Goodbye, for now we make an end.
6107: Whatever in this rough confection
6108: you sought -- tumultuous recollection,
6109: a rest from toil and all its aches,
6110: or just grammatical mistakes,
6111: a vivid brush, a witty rattle --
6112: God grant that from this little book
6113: for heart's delight, or fun, you took,
6114: for dreams, or journalistic battle,
6115: God grant you took at least a grain.
6116: On this we'll part; goodbye again!
6117: L
6118: And my companion, so mysterious,
6119: goodbye to you, my true ideal,
6120: my task, so vivid and so serious
6121: and yet so light. All that is real
6122: and enviable for a poet,
6123: in your pursuit I've come to know it:
6124: oblivion of life's stormy ways,
6125: sweet talk with friends. How many days
6126: since, through the mist that dreams arise on,
6127: young Tanya first appeared to me,
6128: Onegin too -- and there to see,
6129: a free romance's far horizon,
6130: still dim, through crystal's magic glass,
6131: before my gaze began to pass.
6132: {232}
6133: LI
6134: Of those who heard my opening pages
6135: in friendly gatherings where I read,
6136: as Sadi17 sang in earlier ages,
6137: ``some are far distant, some are dead''.
6138: They've missed Eugene's completed etching.
6139: But she who modelled for the sketching
6140: of Tanya's image... Ah, how great
6141: the toll of those borne off by fate!
6142: Blest he who's left the hurly-burly
6143: of life's repast betimes, nor sought
6144: to drain its beaker down, nor thought
6145: of finishing its book, but early
6146: has wished it an abrupt goodbye --
6147: and, with my Eugene, so have I.
6148: {233}
6149: Notes to Chapter Eight
6150: 1 Gavrila  Derzhávin  (1745-1816), ``Russia's first outstanding  poet''
6151: (Nabokov). While still at the Lyceum in Tsarskoe Selo, in 1815, Pushkin read
6152: some of his verses to him. The stanza was unfinished.
6153: 2 Lenore, romantic ballad by Gottfried August Bürger, 1773.
6154: 3 ``Rout (Eng.),  an evening  assembly without dancing;  means properly
6155: crowd.'' Pushkin's note.
6156: 4 Refers to Pushkin's poem The Demon, of 1823.
6157: 5 Hero of Griboedov's Woe from Wit, 1824.
6158: 6 Admiral Alexander Shishkov (1754-1841)  championed the purity ot  the
6159: Russian language against the encroachment of foreign words.
6160: 7 Probably an allusion to Bulgárin,  an unfriendly  critic of Pushkin's
6161: work.
6162: 8 Nina Voronskoy, imaginary belle of Petersburg society.
6163: 9 Court  decoration given  to  the Empress's ladies-in-waiting.  Stanza
6164: unfinished.
6165: 10 Name left blank by Pushkin.
6166: 11 Count Emmanuel Sen-Pri (1806-1828) had a reputation as a cartoonist.
6167: He was the son of the Comte de Saint-Priest, a French émigré.
6168: 12 Author of Maximes et Pensées, Paris, 1796.
6169: 13  Author  of Recherches physiologiques sur la vie et  la mort, Paris,
6170: 1799.
6171: 14 Author of De la santé des gens de lettres, Lausanne and Lyon, 1768.
6172: 15 Pierre Bayle, French philosopher.
6173: 16 Author of Dialogues des Morts, 1683.
6174: 17 Persian poet of the thirteenth century.
